>  “有一天晚上我曾跟我老婆谈起我们的生活有多么完美，那是25年前，我们4个孩子，刚存够钱买新房子，我们感觉是如此幸运。记得她说：‘如果上帝从我们这儿拿走什么呢？’第二天，我下班回到家，发现我老婆在叫。她抱着我们的大儿子，他把手卡在洗衣机里触电了。我们唤不醒他，火速赶去医院，但医生说他们也无能为力，我求他们试一试。我教会的朋友们来了，我们都开始祈祷。后来医生们把他救活了，他成了一个被研究的范例。如今他29岁了，他有学习障碍，不能读或写，但他有一份工作，在当保安，他挺知足的。时至今日，我依然相信奇迹。”（瓦尔帕莱索，智利）@人在深圳 “One night I was talking with my wife about how perfect our life was. It was twenty-five years ago. We had four children. We’d just saved enough money to buy a new house. We felt so lucky. I remember she said: ‘What if God takes something from us?’ The next day I came home from work and found my wife screaming. She was holding our oldest son. He’d stuck his hand in the washing machine and electrocuted himself. We couldn’t revive him. We rushed to the hospital but the doctors said there was nothing they could do. I begged them to try. My friends from the church came and we all started to pray. And the doctors were able to bring him back to life. He became a case study. Today he’s 29. He has learning problems. He can’t read or write. But he has a job as a security guard. He enjoys his life. And to this day, I believe in miracles.”(Valparaíso, Chile)

>  “我迫不得已离开的委内瑞拉，我在那儿生活了一辈子，我父母都葬在那儿。但五个月前我不得不离开，那儿变得太危险了。有一天我从超市走回家时被袭击了，醒来时我在地上。我被枪指过好几次了，我再也受不了了。我想开始新的生活，但找不到工作。我已经申请过大概60家店了，但没人给我机会，他们觉得我太老了。我跟他们说试用我几天，但他们不。我找到一个兼职，打扫厕所和捡垃圾。这些是我从没做过的事，但现在我挑不得了。”（圣地亚哥，智利）@人在深圳 “I had to leave Venezuela. >  “那时我不想再吃避孕药了，我以为我自己能控制好，但那是个错误。发现怀孕时我哭了，想到宝宝100%依靠我，我吓坏了。要是我想去旅行呢？或者想去读研究生呢？或者只是想逃避、不跟任何人说话呢？起初我想堕胎，我都打了热线电话，但从没说完。现在我儿子就是我的命，我的生活里已经完全没有了我自己。一年后我跟孩子的父亲分手了。他现在有了新的女朋友，他要有他的生活，也要来看儿子，想来就来。他要出去，他要经历一个情绪化的阶段，然后决定不工作了。这样不公平，他能跟儿子玩，然后回到他的生活，想来就来，想走就走，却把困难留给了我。现在我的生活就是我儿子，我爱他，所以这是一件很好的事，但也是一件很糟的事。”（圣地亚哥，智利）@人在深圳 “I didn’t want to take the pill anymore and I thought I could control things on my own. Or just get the fuck away and not talk to anyone? At first I wanted to get an abortion. I even called the hotline but I never went through with it. Now my son is my life. He gets to go through an emo phase and decide not to work. It’s unfair. He can play with our son then go back to his life whenever he wants. I get left with the hard part. My life is my son now. >  “如果我做错了什么，那是出于无知。或许我对他太严厉了，我在军队待了27年，所以那是我所知道的一切。最近他真的有点出格，不去教堂，也不关心学业。他觉得自己什么都知道，而我们对他的生活一点也不了解。所以他总是把自己锁在他的房间里。最近他跟我说他恨我，我就发脾气，说他不再是我儿子。我们俩都道歉了，但是仍然不好过。我想他过得很不自在吧，可能他觉得他是家里的败家子。我妻子和我都是教授，他的两个姐姐也都不错。我只是不知道该做些什么，现在我在试着退让，更温和宽容一些，少惩罚他一些，他不做作业我也不收走他的手机了。我不想让他变得更叛逆，但我一撒手，就难再严厉起来和按规矩办了。所以我真不知道该如何是好。我正在看些书，看看该如何靠近他。我想让他明白我不在乎他在专业上是否成功，我只是想让他多少有些志向。”（圣地亚哥，智利）@人在深圳 “If I did something wrong, it was out of ignorance. Maybe I was too strict with him. I was in the army for twenty-seven years so that’s all I knew. He’s really pulled away lately. He doesn’t go to church. He doesn’t care about school. He thinks he knows everything and that we don’t understand anything about his life. So he always locks himself in his room. Recently he told me that he hated me. And I lost my temper and told him that he was no longer my son. Both of us apologized but things are still difficult. I think he’s just very uncomfortable with life. Maybe he feels like the black sheep of the family. My wife and I are professors and both his sisters are doing well. I just don’t know what to do. I’m trying to pull back now and be more lenient. I punish him less. I stopped taking away his phone when he doesn’t do his schoolwork. I don’t want him to rebel any more, but when I back off, it’s hard to be strict again and provide structure. So I just don’t know. I’m reading books to figure out how to reach him. I want him to understand that it doesn’t matter to me if he’s successful in a professional way. I just want him to have some sort of purpose.”(Santiago, Chile)

>  “我结婚15年，离婚一年多了。我很沮丧，有段时间我孤独得睡不着觉。我工作上的一个朋友跟我说下载一个约会软件。我试了好久，没人理我。我感觉更糟糕了，想把它删掉，但我朋友劝我继续试。然后，1月28号那天，我看到她的照片，给她发了一颗心，她给我发了条消息，我说：‘哇噻，真有哎。’她就像个从天而降的天使，给我的生活带来了光明。我爱我的巧克力糖。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “It's been over a year since my divorce. I wanted to delete it but my friend convinced me to keep trying. Then on January 28th, I saw her picture and gave her a ‘heart.’ And she sent me a message. I said: ‘Wow, this is really happening.’ It's like she's an angel who came from heaven to bring light to my life. I love my chocolate bonbon.”(São Paulo, Brazil)

>  “如果曾有人在乎过我，那么上帝已经把他们灭了。我11岁时我母亲死了，因为那些毒品，她心脏有毛病。我脸上纹的这两滴泪是为了她。我甚至都记不得她长什么样了。我记得去了她的葬礼，但记不得她的脸。我梦见她时听到的是她的声音，没有对话或任何东西，只有她的声音，在说：‘来，Jeff。来，Jeff。’她死后，至关重要的就是生存了。没人爱我。如果我父母还在，可能就不一样，可能我有地方住，可能我已经有了什么成就。所以我没感到什么内疚，我为什么要内疚呢？上帝夺走了我妈妈，他都没感到内疚呢。”（2/2）（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “If there was anyone who cared about me, God already killed them. My mother died when I was eleven. She had heart problems because of all the drugs. These two tears are for her. I can’t even remember her face. I remember going to her funeral but I don’t remember her face. When I dream about her, all I hear is her voice. There’s no dialogue or anything. It’s just her voice, saying: ‘Come here, Jeff. Come here, Jeff.’ After she died, all that mattered was surviving. Nobody showed me love. Maybe things would have been different if I had parents. Maybe I’d have a place to live. Maybe I’d have accomplished something. So I don’t feel guilty for anything. Why should I? God doesn’t feel guilty for killing my mom.” (2/2)(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EBtb6doXj&u=005trlAagy1fdzf1yh2cmj31kw11xq7l )

>  “贩毒好爽，我有一把枪，有妞儿，有放克。每个人都看重我。我帮忙保卫贫民区和维持规矩。你不能强奸，不能杀人，没经过允许不能打女人。每个人都知道这些规矩，没人能坏规矩，否则你会被干掉，去喂鳄鱼。我无情，冷血，我的肾上腺素上升——但也就这样，之后就又回到空虚。人们都怕我，尊重我，但后来我被人算计了。一个老大想要我的女朋友，他就告我偷窃，净是胡扯，他甚至说我吸可卡因。他们用棍子打我，打断了我的手指，打掉了我的牙。他们带走了我的妞儿，我的衣服，甚至我的狗。现在我流落街头，什么都没有。过去我拿什么都不要钱，现在我讨个饭都会被撵走。”（1/2）(里约热内卢，巴西)@人在深圳 “Drug dealing was delicious. I had a pistol, I had girls, I had funk. Everyone saw me as important. I helped defend the favela and maintain the rules. You couldn’t rape, you couldn’t kill, you couldn’t hit a woman without permission. Everyone knew the rules and nobody could break them. Or else you might get erased and fed to the crocodiles. I don’t have a heart. I’m cold blooded. My adrenaline goes up-- but that’s it. Afterwards it’s back to nothing. People feared me. People respected me. But then I got set up. One of the 'higher-ups' wanted my girlfriend. So he accused me of stealing. It was all lies. He even tried to say I smoked crack. They beat me with sticks. They broke my fingers. They knocked out my teeth. They took my girl, my clothes, even my dog. And now I live on the streets. I’ve got nothing left. I used to get everything for free. Now if I ask for food, I’ll get chased away.” (1/2)(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “60年代我父亲和他堂兄在这片棚户区创建了第一个毒品交易区。那时这儿是个充满暴力的地方，我父亲来之前，谁有武器谁牛逼。没法律，也没警察可以求助，凶杀、盗窃和强奸忒多。我父亲扮演着一个重要的角色，残忍，但重要。他得清理这里，犯事儿的不是走了而已，得被干掉。我父亲就负责干这个。他是个小个儿，穿着讲究，受过教育，有教养且谦逊。对很多人来说，他不是个好人，但他是个正直的人。我没有追随我父亲的足迹，我成为了一个摄影师和活动家。我不认为我父亲是个坏人，他给这一片带来了规则，今天的毒贩们执行着相同的规则。这片棚户区是本城最安全的地方之一，这里不允许盗窃，你不能强奸，不能打女人。是，这里是有暴力，因为警察一直在跟毒贩做斗争。但如果毒贩明天都走了，这里将会危险得多得多。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “My father and his cousin created the first drug dealing territory in this favela back in the 60’s. It was a very violent place back then. Before my father came along—anyone with a weapon had absolute power. There was no law. There was no police to turn to. There were many homicides, burglaries, and rapes. My father played an important role. It was a cruel role, but it was important. He had to clean up the favela. The criminals weren’t just going to leave. They had to be erased. And my father did that job. He was a tiny man. He dressed well. He was educated, and polite, and humble. To many people he wasn’t a good person. But he was a righteous person. I didn’t follow in my father’s footsteps. I became a photographer and an activist. But I don’t see my father as a bad man. He brought rules to this place. And today’s drug traffickers enforce those same rules. This favela is one of the safest places in the city. Stealing is not allowed here. You can’t rape. You can’t hit a woman. Yes, there is violence. Because the police are always fighting the drug traffickers. But if the drug traffickers were gone tomorrow, the favela would be a far more dangerous place.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EBprVkZIc&u=005trlAagy1fdyyh5z7k6j31kw11xdnx )

>  “里约是世界历史上最大的奴隶港，两百万奴隶曾涌到这个城市来，比整个南美多5倍。棚屋之所以建起来，是因为政府不想给奴隶们的后代提供基本的服务，所以这些后代们被迫修建了他们自己的居住区。贫民窟无序发展，服务很糟糕，但不要叫它们‘贫民窟’。那是个懒惰的翻译，对住在这里的人也不公平。‘贫民窟’这个词暗示着所有的棚户区都是一样的，也忽略了这些居民对他们的社区120年来所做出的改善。而且，‘贫民窟’这个词也使这些社区更容易被忽视，而这正是政府想要的。因为如果棚户区不被当成真正的居住区，那它们的居民也就不应得到真正的服务。所以请不要用‘贫民窟’这个词，因为它只会鼓励那种说辞。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “Rio was the biggest slave port in world history. Two million slaves arrived in this city—five times more than the entire American South. Favelas were built because the government didn’t want to provide basic services to the descendants of slaves. So these descendants were forced to build their own communities. Favelas are unregulated. They’re poorly serviced. But don’t call them ‘slums.’ That’s a lazy translation and it’s unfair to the people who live here. The word ‘slum’ implies that all favelas are the same. The word ‘slum’ ignores 120 years of improvement that these residents have made to their communities. And the word ‘slum’ makes it easier to ignore these communities. That's exactly what the government wants. Because if favelas aren’t viewed as real neighborhoods, then their residents don't deserve real services. So please don’t use the word ‘slum.’ Because it only helps to encourage that narrative.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EAEMxm562&u=005trlAagy1fdt8kyvfoxj31kw11xwkc )

>  “目前我们俩都没在工作，但我们能凑合着过。我们跟邻居借吃的和尿布。既然没钱外出，我们就跟孩子玩，前几天我们还用水桶做了个游泳池呢。我们去散步。很多时候我们就只是一起躺在床上。我们尽量不吵架，但很难做到。焦虑的时候就会有压力，不吵架好难哦。当我们没了吃的，他会自责。有时候他很焦虑，觉得我们的日子没盼头了。他彻底蔫掉，把自己关起来，不肯说话。吃的不够我都能忍，伤我最深的是他谈都不愿意谈的时候。”（萨尔瓦多，巴西）@人在深圳 “Neither of us are working right now, but we make do. We borrow food and diapers from the neighbors. Since we don’t have money to go out, we’ll just play with the baby. The other day we made a swimming pool out of a bucket. We go on walks. A lot of times we just lay in bed together. We try not to argue but it’s hard. When we get nervous, we get stressed, and it’s so hard not to argue. He blames himself when we run out of food, and sometimes he gets so nervous that he thinks we’ll never find a way out. He shuts down, and he locks himself away, and he won’t talk. I can handle us not having enough food. What hurts me the most is when he doesn’t want to talk about it.”(Salvador, Brazil)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EAECK89gy&u=005trlAagy1fdt7vhn4rxj31kw11x7d0 )

>  “我出生后不久我母亲就去世了，所以是我姑把我养大的。我是家里的败家子。我过去吸毒，在街上飚摩托。我毁了我的脸，丢了我的牙。我在监狱待了18个月，因为我骑车意外弄死了人。我姑是唯一一个始终对我不离不弃的人。现在我正要去她家旁边修一辆车，我要带些香蕉给她。我一进门，她就非让我吃早餐。她会把甜食收走，因为我有糖尿病。她会把鸡皮剥下来，因为她知道那是我的最爱。她还会问我吃药了没。最近她病得很厉害，我很害怕，因为我不能想象没有她的生活。如果我姑出了什么事，就不会再有人牵挂我了。”（萨尔瓦多，巴西）@人在深圳 “My mother died shortly after I was born. So my aunt is the one who raised me. I’m the black sheep of the family. I used to do drugs. I raced motorcycles through the streets. I destroyed my face. I lost my teeth. I spent eighteen months in prison because I accidentally killed someone with my bike. My aunt is the only one who never turned away from me. Right now I’m going to fix a bike by her house, and I’m going to bring her some bananas. When I walk in the door, she’s going to insist I eat breakfast. She’s going to hide the sweets because I have diabetes. She’s going to take the skin off the chicken because she knows it’s my favorite part. And she’s going to ask me if I’ve been taking my medication. Recently she got very sick. And I’m scared. Because I can’t imagine life without her. If something ever happened to my aunt, there will be nobody left to worry about me.”(Salvador, Brazil)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EAzzP1f1l&u=005trlAagy1fdslkvxq4aj31kw11xwk0 )

>  “我没怎么享受过生活，因为我总是在为未来做牺牲。我整个人生都是学习和工作：我做过很多份工；我读了大学，拿到了MBA；我没怎么旅行过；我没结婚，没孩子。所有我想要的就是有安全感。但我身体一直都很糟糕，所以我没能存住钱。两周前我丢了工作。当你到了我这个年纪，就业市场很残酷，人家不认为你还能学新东西。我连个文书的工作都找不到，因为他们觉得我那是大材小用。现在我没钱了，几乎负担不起食物和交通。我不知道该如何是好。为了有一天能有安全感，我穷尽一生在做牺牲，但似乎一切都只是一场虚空。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “I didn’t enjoy life very much because I was always sacrificing for the future. My whole life was about studying and working. I worked so many jobs. I went to college. I got my MBA. I didn’t travel very much. I didn’t get married. I didn’t have kids. All I wanted to do was feel secure. But I’ve had bad health problems my entire life. So I haven’t been able to save. And two weeks ago I lost my job. The job market is brutal when you’re my age. People don’t think you can learn new things. I can’t even get work as a clerk because they think I’m overqualified. I have no money now. I can barely afford food and transportation. I’ve spent my whole life sacrificing—just to one day feel secure. But it seems like it was all for nothing. And I have no idea what to do.”(São Paulo, Brazil)

>  “经过20年的婚姻，我抓到我丈夫出轨，只得离开他。但说实话，我希望我离婚离得更早一些。长久以来，我在否决我的权利，作为一个独立个体的权利。相比我的梦想，家庭变得重要得多得多。那时我也有一些小欢乐：买辆新车，纪念我们结婚20周年，等我儿子上了大学。但现在欢乐的强度甚之又甚：我做着所有我喜欢的事。我学了营养学，在医院找了份工作。我想买什么就买什么。我看动画片，从不错过任何一部《怪物史莱克》。我一个月至少去听一次管弦乐。而现在，我刚上完一堂金融课回来。我打算投资股市，然后在海边弄套房子。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “After twenty years of marriage, I caught my husband cheating and had to leave him. But honestly, I wish I’d gotten my divorce much sooner. For so long I’d been denying my right to be an individual. The family had become so much more important than my dreams. I had small joys back then: getting a brand new car, having our 20th anniversary, when my son got into college. But now the intensity is so much greater. I’m doing all the things I love to do. I studied nutrition and got a job at the hospital. I buy whatever I want. I watch cartoons. I never miss a Shrek movie. I go to the orchestra at least once a month. And right now I’m coming back from a class on finance. I’m going to invest in the stock market and get a house by the beach.”(São Paulo, Brazil)

>  “我在农村长大，14岁到城里来的，我想开阔眼界。当时我的全部家当就是一只行李箱，还有我的勇气。我父母想阻止我，我妈妈找到我买好的汽车票，把它撕得粉碎。但我告诉她我不会放弃的，最后我爸载我去了车站。一开始我在人家家里做女佣人。我服务的一户人家是一家大报的所有者，他夫人帮我上了高中，然后我去读了大学，在那儿我遇到了我身旁这位帅锅。现在我在做点小生意，卖木薯粉。我甚至可以帮助到我在老家的父母了。但我得承认我又变得忙碌起来了。我想去别的国家生活。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “I grew up in a rural area. I came to the city when I was fourteen. I wanted to expand my horizons. All I had was a suitcase and my courage. My parents tried to stop me. My mom found my first bus ticket and ripped it into pieces. But I told her that I wasn’t going to give up, and eventually my father drove me to the station. At first I worked as a maid in people’s houses. One of the people I worked for was the owner of a major newspaper, and his wife helped me go to high school. Then I went to college, where I met this handsome guy beside me. Now I run a small business selling tapioca. I’m even able to help support my parents back home. But I will admit that I’m getting restless again. I think I want to live in another country.”(São Paulo, Brazil)

>  “我17岁时有了第一个孩子。孩子的妈妈有毒瘾，而我当时处境很艰难，自己在抚养孩子。有人去抢劫一辆卡车，请我去帮忙，我心想：‘只做今天这一次，然后就收手不干了。’我负责放哨，我们逃跑时警察抓住了我们。监狱是个什么地方，简直没法说。审判之前我在那里关了两年半。我见过有人被刀捅了，见过有人拿剃须刀割自己的喉咙。夜里我会坐在窗户边，看着星星，想着：‘连只动物也不喜欢待在笼子里啊。’我所有朋友都把我忘了，只有我妈妈来看我。我永远都不会回那儿去了。现在我的处境又十分艰难，我没工作，但教堂的人帮我弄吃的。我坐在这儿，代客泊车。只是挣一点小钱，但我宁愿做这个，也不想偷别人的，人家也需要钱呢。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “When I was seventeen I had my first kid. The mother was addicted to drugs. I was in a tough situation. I was raising the child on my own. And I received an invitation to help rob a truck. I thought: ‘I’ll just do this today, and then it will be over.’ I was the lookout. The police caught us while we were running away. Prison is a place that’s impossible to explain. I was there for 2.5 years before I even had a trial. I saw a guy being stabbed. I saw a guy slit his own throat with a razor. During the night I used to sit by the window, and look at the stars, and think: ‘Not even an animal likes to stay in a cage.’ All my friends forgot about me. Only my mother visited. I’ll never go back there. Right now I’m in a tough situation again. I have no job. But people at the church help me with food. And I sit here and help people park their cars. It’s only a few pennies, but I’d rather do this than steal from someone else who needs the money.”(São Paulo, Brazil)

>  “我们在同一所学校读书。三个月前我约她出来，带她去看了场电影，那感觉还比较随意，那时我也不认为她会期待什么。离开电影院时，我递给她一首诗，那首诗讲的是我们过往的友谊，包括我们那次看电影的经历。那首诗最后一行写的是：‘看着我’。当她抬起头，我又朗诵了四行诗：‘除此之外，我们是如此要好的朋友。你会多往前一步，做我女朋友么？’”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “We go to the same school. I asked her out three months ago. I took her to a movie because it seemed casual, and I didn’t think she’d be expecting anything. When we left the theater, I handed her a poem that told the story of our friendship, including our trip to the movie. But the last line of the poem just said: ‘Look at me.’ When she looked up, I recited four more lines:‘In addition to this,we are such good friends.Will you take one more step,and be my girlfriend?’”(São Paulo, Brazil)

>  “我在一个很严苛的家庭长大，我妈妈就像个军士。我太早就结婚了，那时候我都没什么生活经验。结婚25年，我老公从不让我独自去任何地方。他去世时，我都不知道我该如何靠自己过活。我守寡14年，几乎都不出门。最近我在网上认识了这个男人，我们交换照片，煲电话粥，但我不敢见面。他就告诉我：‘抬起头来，你是你人生的主宰！’所以今天我终于同意见面了。早上我试了5套衣服，出门后我又回去换了双鞋。在公交车上我一路都在发抖，感觉胃不舒服。最后见到他时，我心里像是有一所桑巴舞学校，直冒汗。他做的第一件事是给了我些水。现在我们在一块儿待了一整天，我感觉好放松，好自在，我们仿佛已经认识了一辈子。”（萨尔瓦多，巴西）@人在深圳 “I was raised in a very strict family. My mom was like a sergeant. I married way too young. I had no life experience. I was married for twenty-five years and my late husband never let me go anywhere by myself. When he died, I had no idea how to live on my own. For fourteen years I’ve been a widow. And I’ve barely left the house. Recently I met this man on the Internet. We kept exchanging pictures. We kept talking on the phone. But I was too scared to meet. He told me: ‘Put your head up high! You are the boss of your life!’ So today I finally agreed to meet. I tried on five different outfits this morning. After I left the house, I went back once more to change my shoes. I was trembling the whole way on the bus. My stomach felt sick. When I finally saw him, it felt like there was a samba school in my heart. I was sweating. The first thing he did was get me some water. Now we’ve spent the whole day together. I feel so relaxed. I feel free. I feel like we’ve known each other for our entire lives.”(Salvador, Brazil)

>  “我年纪轻轻就开始做航空公司机修工，我很擅长干这个，总是加班。那还好，因为它让我变得老练，获得成长。但因为我老工作，人家就会认为我挺顺的，也容易让我不去想一些事情。如今我22岁了，我感觉茫然无措，感觉我就从没花时间想过我自己。我不擅长跟别人建立关系或者交谈，我从没想要去示弱，因为没人喜欢人老闷闷不乐。所以我变成了一个自我封闭的人。昨天我们分组做一个课题，没人想跟我一组，因为我工作太多。我不去看电影，甚至从没去过公园，这还是我第一次到这儿来。我也不知道，此时此刻我只是觉得如此茫然，我在寻找什么，但又不知道它是什么。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 ：图2是主人公和Brandon的合影。“I’ve been working as an airline mechanic since a young age. >  “你算是找对人了，我曾举着奥运火炬穿过这个镇。在那之前我甚至从没听说过‘火炬’这玩意儿。我是说，我并不蠢，我搞懂了。但当我看到它的时候，我还蛮紧张的。我得举着它上山。我都88了，我还以为我会摔跤呢。当时还有当兵的，排着队，拿着枪，长枪，我还心想：别有人枪走火打到我。我跑的时候所有人都在欢呼，那阵势，就没人见过。当时我真吓坏了，但我做到了，然后每个人就开始拥抱我。”（伦索伊斯，巴西）@人在深圳 “You found the right guy. I’m eighty-eight. I thought I might fall down. And there were all these soldiers lined up with guns. Big guns. I thought one of them might shoot me by accident. Everyone was screaming while I ran. Nobody had ever seen anything like it. I was really scared, but I made it. And everybody started hugging me.”(Lençóis, Brazil)

>  “我在城北的一个贫民区长大，那儿暴力事件很多。但那时候我并没过多感觉到我的肤色。我们那儿即便是白人也都挺穷的，我们的生活方式都一样，每个人似乎都是平等的。我妈总是鼓励我要努力学习，这样我就能离开那儿。她给一户富人家做女佣，她想让我过上像他们那样的生活。最终我大学毕业，找到了一份好工作，搬到了城南一个较富有的社区。我确实感觉更安全了，就像想象得那样。但我从未料到会感觉如此不受欢迎：交朋友会很难，我还被骂过。搞得我感觉到我的肤色比我成长过程中还要多。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “I grew up in a poor neighborhood on the north side of the city. There was a lot of violence. But I didn’t feel the color of my skin very much back then. Even the whites in my neighborhood were poor. We all lived in the same way and everyone seemed equal. My mother always encouraged me to study hard so I could leave the neighborhood. She worked as a maid for a rich family, and she wanted me to live a life like theirs. Eventually I graduated college, got a good job, and moved to a wealthier neighborhood in the south part of the city. I do feel safer— just like I imagined. But I never expected to feel so unwelcome. It can be hard to make friends. I've been called names. I'm made to feel the color of my skin more than I ever did growing up.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我想拥抱她，她说抱着太热了，所以我学会了不再尝试。我们从没有过真正的谈话，我觉得那很正常，我所知道的就是这样的，我一直以为母亲和孩子之间就是她说什么你做什么。但我10岁时去一个朋友家做一个学校布置的任务，记得一开始我还为他难过呢：他家穷得叮当响，可以说是家徒四壁。但我们一进门，他妈妈就给了他一个好大的拥抱，她看到他好开心哦。那是我这辈子最难过的时刻，因为我从不知道那是我本来可以拥有的。我妈妈还是不拥抱我，但我认为我们正朝着那个方向去：最近我哮喘发作，浑身没劲儿，她跟我说我可以把头放在她腿上。说不出来那让我感觉有多特别。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “When I tried to hug her, she’d tell me it was too hot for hugs. So I learned to stop trying. We never had conversations. I thought it was normal. It was all I knew. I always thought the relationship between a mother and a child was about giving and receiving orders. But when I was ten years old, I went to a friend’s house to do a school project. At first I remember feeling sorry for him. His family was so poor. There was almost nothing in the house. But when we walked inside, his mom gave him such a big hug. And she was so happy to see him. And that was the saddest moment of my life. Because I never knew that was something you could have. My mom still doesn’t hug me. But I think we’re on the way to that. I had an asthma attack recently, and I felt so weak, and she told me I could lay my head in her lap. I can’t explain how special that made me feel.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  回答网友提问：《人在纽约》至今出版了两本书，重庆出版社都已经引进推出了中文版：第一本《人在纽约》，以图片为主，那时的采访内容还不多；第二本《人在纽约：故事版》，图文并茂，采访内容深入而丰富，所以才叫故事版。最近刚上架的是这一本（见图2）。这两本书都是Facebook已发布内容的精选精编，中文版以中文为主，篇幅所限，只有少量的附带了英文原文。喜欢英文原版的请上亚马逊购买（价格会比中文版贵一些）。目前这两本书（中文版）京东、当当、亚马逊都有货，搜书名就能搜到。我拍@人在深圳 只是利用业余时间，我有自己的工作和工资收入。但Brandon是在专职全职拍@人在纽约 ，他的主要收入来自图书版税，​请大家支持他。​​​
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/pic/EApXIC1sH?rl=0 )

>  “我父亲从没学过该如何跟人说话，一切都得按他那一套来。他没少打我，有时真的打得很狠。老兄，我被搞惨了。我一直以为那是我的错。也许那谁的错都不是，也许他就知道这些，也许他老爹也那样打他。我不知道，但他给我弄了一身馊。我从不谈这事，我一直装得比自己更强大。但我必须得想法原谅他，因为我该得一些安宁。”（伦索伊斯，巴西）@人在深圳 “My father never learned how to talk to people. Everything had to be his way. He hit me a lot. It got really ugly sometimes. It really fucked me up, man. The whole time I thought it was my fault. Maybe it’s nobody fault. Maybe that’s all he knew. Maybe his dad did that. I don’t know. But he put me into some crazy shit. I never talked about it. I've spent my whole life pretending like I'm stronger than I am. But I’ve got to forgive him somehow. Because I deserve some peace.”(Lençóis, Brazil)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EzvAYnZpd&u=005trlAagy1fdki99jqv3j31kw11xaeo )

>  “两年前他心脏病发作过一次，他知道他不应该喝酒，吃上要注意。他刚添了个孙女，他还想看着她长大。但每次我抓住他吃不好的东西，我吼他，他就装俏皮装嫩，他叫我他的‘美丽的黑发女郎’，说我是他此生的最爱，还说他在寻找一个开怀大笑，就藏在我心里。我搓火啊，因为他搞得你非领情不可。我使劲儿想对他发飙，但我老憋不住，最后还是笑场了。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “He had a heart attack two years ago. He knows he shouldn’t be drinking. He knows he should be eating better. He has a new granddaughter that he wants to see grow up. But every time I catch him eating something bad, and I try to yell at him, he gets so playful and tender. He calls me his ‘beautiful brunette,’ and he tells me that I’m the love of his life. He says that he’s searching for a giant smile that’s hidden inside me. And it pisses me off because it’s patronizing. And I try so hard to be mad at him. But in the end I always crack, and I end up laughing.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我13岁时第一次到这儿来。一开始就我一个女孩，怪吓人的，那些家伙们会惹我生气，叫我‘玻璃’，我玩滑板时他们还会把他们的板滑到我面前。所以我每天一放学就到这儿来，那时太阳高照，场地空空。我滑得比他们好了，开始在淘汰赛中打败他们，所以现在他们尊重我了。过去好多女孩就在边上看着，因为太害怕，她们不敢参与进来。但现在我每天在这儿，她们中一些人也够胆来试了。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “I first started coming out here when I was thirteen years old. I was the only girl in the beginning. It was intimidating. The guys would try to make me angry. They’d call me ‘dyke.’ They’d roll their skateboards in front of me when I was skating. So I started coming out here every day right after school, when the sun was high, and the place was empty. I got better than a lot of them. I started beating them in elimination games. So they respect me now. A lot of girls used to watch from the edges because they were too intimidated to participate. But now that I’m out here every day, some of them have the courage to try.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我最疼的是我的小儿子，我的其他孩子甚至嫉妒我们的感情之深。他很小时，我离家去办公室，他会探出窗外呼唤我。我到了办公室，会在公文包里发现他的玩具。随着他长大，我们依然亲密，他总给我打电话，总向我问安，总带我去吃午饭。但有一天我去银行，我的很多钱都不见了。原来他一直在偷我，他伪造了我的签名。我跟他当面对质，他跪下来求我原谅。然后我就开始接到电话，他欠人家钱，人家威胁要杀了他。我去到那些贫民窟，找到那些放高利贷的，还清了他的债务。所有钱我都还了，包括利息。过去我穿的是靓衫，有一间靓屋，现在我一无所有，只剩下退休金。我的信用也被毁了。我卖掉所有，躲着他。晚上睡觉时我会想他怎么样，他是否安好。但我不能见他，因为如果我见到他，我会再次帮他的。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “The one I loved most was my last son. My other children were even jealous of our attachment. When he was very young, he would hang out the window and call to me as I left for the office. And when I arrived, I would find his toys in my briefcase. We remained close as he grew older. He was the one who always called me. He was always checking on me. He was always taking me to lunch. But then one day I went to the bank, and a lot of my money was missing. He had been stealing from me. He was falsifying my signature. When I confronted him, he begged on his knees for forgiveness. Then I started getting phone calls. He owed money to people who were threatening to kill him. I went into the slums to find the loan sharks and pay off his debts. I paid them all, with interest. I used to wear nice clothes. I used to have a nice apartment. Now I’m left with nothing but my pension. And my credit is ruined. I sold all my belongings and I’m hiding from him. When I go to sleep at night, I wonder how he is doing. I wonder if he is safe. But I can’t see him. Because if I see him, I will help him again.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我对我的健康状况会有那么一点不安。起初我担心我不能给Olga她所需的一切，因为我不能举她，不能追着她跑，做事情我也要花更长的时间。所以我想她可能会对我挺泄气的。但这些担心一个都没成真，她对我们的现实状况完全没问题。她很有耐心，我们下车时，她知道轮椅先出来，然后是爸爸，然后是妈妈，然后是Olga。她很喜欢坐我腿上，她还喜欢和我们一起躺在床上。她还想帮我呢。在家里我不用轮椅，因为我抱着老公的肩膀可以走。最近她看到我们这样做，就走到我身后，想要帮忙推我的腿呢。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “I can get a bit insecure about my health condition. In the beginning I was worried that I wouldn’t be able to give her everything she needs. Because I can’t lift her. I can’t run after her. It takes me longer to do things, so I thought she might get frustrated with me. But none of those worries came true. She’s perfectly fine with our reality. She’s very patient. When we get out of the car, she knows that the wheelchair goes first, then Daddy, then Mommy, then Olga. She’s very happy sitting on my lap. And she loves to lie in bed with us. She even tries to help me. In the house I don’t use my wheelchair because I can walk while holding onto my husband’s shoulders. Olga saw us doing this recently, and she came up behind me and tried to help by pushing my legs.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我17岁认识我老婆，我不想告诉她我有精神分裂症，当时她喜欢另一个家伙，那人好好的，我不想破坏我的机会。结婚后我仍隐瞒了好长时间，我总为我的怪异行为开脱，我会编故事来解释我工作时的暴力发作。但事态越来越严重，等我承认我的病时已经太晚了。一年前她得到了法院的禁制令。有一次我发作时打了她。为了我们的孩子，她原谅了我，但他们不再跟我住在一起了。我现在服用着5种强力药，要控制我思想的步伐仍有些困难。有些想法会在其他的想法还没结束前就冒出来。感觉就像我的大脑被掰开了，要让双脚都立足于现实很难。但我不想再惹麻烦了。我已经脱离了所有人，干活时不说话，独自过活，这是我过正常生活的唯一方式了。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “I met my wife when I was seventeen. I didn’t want to tell her about my schizophrenia. At the time, she liked another guy who had no issues and I didn’t want to ruin my chances. I hid the disease for a long time after we married. I would always find explanations for my strange behavior. I’d make up stories to explain my violent outbursts at work. But it got to be too much. By the time I admitted my disease, it was too late. She got a restraining order a year ago. I had an outburst and I hit her. She has forgiven me for the sake of our children, but they don’t live with me anymore. I’m on five strong medications now. I still have some difficulty controlling the pace of my thoughts. Some thoughts will begin before others end. It’s like my mind is divided. It can be tough to keep both feet in reality. But I don’t want any more problems. I’ve detached myself from everyone. I don’t speak at work. I spend my time alone. It’s my only way to live a normal life.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我不会教他去卖糖果的。他就在这儿玩儿，直到去上学。我小时候我妈妈带我到这儿来。我有9个兄弟姊妹，我们都得在街上卖糖果。我5岁就开始卖糖果，从没受过教育。我识字不多，我知道的真的就是这些了。有些人看低我。最近有个女的冲我发火，说她再也不会从我这里买东西了，还说她家附近的一个超市正在招人。我真的很灰心丧气，经历那件事后我很难再抬起头来。但这儿也有人支持我，我的一些朋友每天都路过这儿和我聊天。我的银行的朋友们还说：‘你别担心那女的，她不了解你，你是个很棒的人。’”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “I’m not going to teach him to sell candies. But there are also people out here who support me. I have some friends who walk by and talk to me every day. My friends from the bank told me, ‘Don’t worry about that lady. She doesn’t know you. You’re a great person.’”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我们俩认识得比较晚，我们正努力想要一个孩子。但我已经不再那么年轻了，我们已经努力了好几年，我们的家人开始真的给我们施加压力了。我肯定是我有问题，不是他有问题。我开始接受这个想法了，最近我一直在考虑收养的问题。如果能有一个小家伙儿在我的呵护下成长，我于愿足矣。我真的相信所谓母亲，就是那个养育孩子长大的人。所以我不介意说‘我不能生育’，至少这样人们不再问来问去了。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “We met later in life. We’re trying to have a kid but I’m not that young anymore. We’ve been trying for years now. Our families are beginning to really pressure us. I’m sure it’s my problem, not his. I’m starting to accept the idea. I’ve been thinking a lot about adoption lately. If I can have a small human being under my protection—that’s enough. I truly believe that a mother is the person who raises a child. So I don’t mind saying, ‘I can’t have children.’ At least then people stop asking about it.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我恨我父亲恨了很久。他是个酒鬼，还好动粗。我10岁时，他抛弃了我们一家。我母亲给人当管家，靠一己之力养活7个孩子。我父亲再婚，变得很有钱，但他从没给过我们一分钱。有时我们连吃的都没有，但我们活下来了，我们弟兄几个都长大成人，健健康康。最近我父亲去世了。临终前几周里，他请他的7个儿子来看他。只有我们两个去了，其余几个气都气不过来呢。我们主要就是谈谈足球和其他一些小事，他从没为自己所做的事道歉，他仍然不是那种能融入自己感情的人，但他却从头哭到尾。长久以来我把他当做一块冰，但那一刻他似乎又成了一个人。他躺在医院的病床上，看上去弱不禁风，那一刻我原谅了他，即使他并没要求我那么做。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “I hated my father for a long time. He was an alcoholic. He was abusive. And he abandoned our family when I was ten years old. My mother had to support seven children on her own. She worked as a housekeeper. My father remarried and became wealthy, but he never gave us a penny. Sometimes we went without food. But we survived. All of my brothers are grown and healthy. My father died recently, and in his final weeks he asked all seven of his sons to come visit him. Only two of us went. The rest were too angry. We mainly just talked about soccer and other small things. He never apologized for what he did. He still wasn’t the kind of person who could put his feelings into the world. But he cried the entire time. I had viewed him as a block of ice for so long. But he seemed human in that moment. He looked so vulnerable lying in his hospital bed. And at that moment I forgave him. Even if he didn’t ask me to.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我22岁时怀孕了，计划外的，孩子的父亲和我甚至都没在相处。但我认为我能靠自己处理好，当时我感觉自己像个现代的女人——我在上法学院，我想成为一名外交官。但是，噢天哪！那叫一个难。在情感上我并没准备好去面对它，而社会并不祝福一个未婚妈妈的孩子。当你结了婚怀了孕，人们会来问各种问题：‘男孩？还是女孩？’‘感觉咋样？’但当你是单身，就不会是这样。人们看到我越来越胖，但每个人都避而不谈，而是互相打听：‘咋回事？你知道么？’反倒我感觉被视而不见。我从法学院退学了，因为我觉得难为情。幸好还有几个好朋友陪我度过了那段时间。我女儿现在18岁，一切都好转了。但我真希望当初我能好好享受我的怀孕期。”（里约热内卢，巴西）@人在深圳 “I got pregnant when I was twenty-two. It wasn’t planned. The father and I weren’t even in a relationship. But I thought I could handle it on my own. I felt like a modern woman. I was in law school. I wanted to be a diplomat. But oh man, it was hard. I wasn’t emotionally prepared to deal with it. Society doesn’t treat the child of an unwed mother like a blessing. When you’re married and pregnant, people come up and ask all kinds of questions: ‘Is it a boy? Is it a girl? How are you feeling?’ But that doesn’t happen when you’re single. People saw me getting fatter, but everyone avoided the subject. Instead they asked each other: ‘What happened? Do you know anything?’ I felt invisible. I dropped out of law school because I felt so ashamed. Thankfully a few close friends carried me through. My daughter is eighteen now. Everything turned out fine. But I wish I could have enjoyed my pregnancy more.”(Rio de Janeiro, Brazil)

>  “我们在公园散散步，谈谈事情。几天前我们闹分手，我觉得她有时候占有欲太强了。当时我们在参加一个聚会，她吃醋了，我们就吵起来，我决定我需要些时间透透气。但只持续了几天，我就开始想很多事情。我权衡了所有的好与坏：我们是有我们的问题，但她照顾着我们的家，照顾着我的健康。我生病住院时，她整夜坐在我床边的地板上。她让我戒掉了我过去的那些习惯。反正我和她在一起，一家人不说两家话。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “We’re taking a walk in the park to talk things through. >  “外人看来我们最大的挣扎是孩子的残障，其实不是。我们最大的挣扎是我们曾彼此不相爱了。Tatiana出生时我失去了很多独立性，我陷入了抑郁。那时他工作很多，我们变得疏远，我曾想我不会再爱他了。两年前，一天晚上祷告，我说：‘上帝啊，你都做了这么多，请再给我一次奇迹，让我再爱他吧。’我先迈出了第一步，他一直是个随和的人，所以我必须先做出改变。我变得更信任了，我努力变得更宽容和理解，我给他做饭，整理家里的东西。他开始花更多的时间在家里，我们开始享受彼此的陪伴。我们谈论疾病之外的事情。我们开始一起外出,就像这样。我就像突然认识了一个朋友，他成了我最好的朋友，成了我的爱人。我们的生活又重新开始了。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “People who see us from the outside think that our greatest struggle is the disability. It’s not. Our greatest struggle is that we’d fallen out of love with each other. I lost a lot of my independence when Tatiana was born. I fell into a depression. He was working a lot. We grew distant. I didn’t think I could ever love him again. Two years ago I prayed one night, and said: ‘God, you’ve done so much. Please grant me one more miracle and make me love him again.’ The first change came from me. He’s always been the easygoing one, so I had to change first. I started trusting more. I tried to be more forgiving and understanding. I started to cook for him and organize things around the house. And he started spending more time at home. We started enjoying each other’s company. We talked about things other than diseases. And we started going out together-- just like this. It was like I suddenly met a friend, who became my best friend, who became my love. And our life started over again.”(São Paulo, Brazil)

>  “她有自主力，意志力也很强，但她动不了。所以，从很多方面来说，她的生命就是我的生命。那比我还大，它控制着我，让我以一种从未有过的方式去战斗。我们在一起这么久，以至于她成了我的一部分。她知道她对我有多么重要。她得了儿童癌，心脏衰竭过三次，我一直在她身边。我从未意识到我可以像这样爱一个人。她永远不会伤害我，她永远不会伤害任何人。我们老问她：‘你生气吗？你愤怒吗？’她总说‘不’。我笑她就笑，而现在我在忍着不哭，因为如果我哭，她也会哭。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “She has autonomy. She has a strong will. But she can’t move. So in many ways her life is my life. It’s bigger than me, it controls me, and it makes me fight like never before. We spend so much time together that she’s a part of me. She knows how important she is to me. She had childhood cancer. Her heart failed three times. And I was by her side the entire time. I never realized that I could love someone as much as this. She could never hurt me. She could never hurt anyone. We always ask her: ‘Are you angry?’, ‘Are you mad?’ And she always says ‘no.’ She laughs when I laugh. And right now I’m trying not to cry. Because she'll cry if I cry.”(São Paulo, Brazil)

>  “对Heloisa来说，每个上了年纪的人她都觉得像爷爷奶奶。她爱她爷爷奶奶，所以我问她想不想在一个老人之家举办她的6岁生日会。她喜欢这个主意，我就联系了当地的一家，和协调人计划好了一切，我们向所有老人的家属发了邀请。我是个摄影师，我早去了几天，给所有老人拍了不错的肖像照。聚会那天，我把照片打印出来，带去作为礼物送给他们的家属。我们玩游戏、做活动，可欢乐了，每个人都开怀大笑。老人们哭了，他们的家人哭了，我也哭了。我想Heloisa会永远记住这段经历的。聚会过后，她学校里的朋友和我们来到家，我们开了个老式的睡衣趴。”（圣保罗，巴西）@人在深圳 “For Heloisa, every elderly person feels like a grandparent. And she loves her grandparents. So I asked her if she wanted to have her sixth birthday party at a home for the elderly. She loved the idea. So I contacted a local home and planned everything with the coordinator. We sent invitations to the family members of all the residents. I'm a photographer, so I went a few days early and took nice portraits of all the residents. On the day of the party, I printed out the photographs and brought them as gifts for their family members. We did games and activities. There was so much joy. Everyone had such big smiles. The residents were crying. Their families were crying. I was crying. I think Heloisa will remember the experience forever. Afterward, her school friends came home with us and we had an old-fashioned pajama party.”(São Paulo, Brazil)

>  “每天早上我给我的草坪浇水，然后鸟儿们来找从潮湿的地面爬出来的虫子。如果我错过一天，地面会太硬，鸟儿们就会在院子里叫，因为它们的孩子们饿了。我就是这样感受我这辈子的，就像一只鸟儿呼唤着食物。30年前，就在这个广场，我参加过罢工。当时我们拿不到薪水，没钱付账单或买食物。那时我儿子一个1岁，一个8岁，还有一个9岁。我们决定去野营，每天晚上我都去湖里钓鱼，抓两条鳟鱼，那就够我们四个人吃的了。我们那样做是迫于生计，但挺美好的。我的儿子们现在都三十多了，他们都飞走了，但他们记得那些快乐的时光。”（圣卡洛斯-德巴里洛切，阿根廷）@人在深圳 ：情人节快乐！“I water my lawn every morning and birds come to get worms out of the wet ground. Like a bird calling out for food. Thirty years ago I went on strike in this same square. We weren’t getting paychecks. There was no money for bills or food. At the time my sons were one, eight, and nine. So we decided to go camping. I’d go fishing on the lake every night and catch two trout. That was enough to feed the four of us. We did it out of necessity but it was beautiful. My sons are in their thirties now. All of them have flown away. But they remember those times with happiness.”(San Carlos de Bariloche, Argentina)

>  “我父亲是个简单劳动者，我母亲的大脑像个12岁的孩子，她有发育问题。我成长过程中从不能问她问题，像：‘这东西怎么用？这是什么意思？’倒是所有问题都是她问我。打招呼之外，她从不跟我多说。很长时间我都以为那是正常的。但当我去了我朋友家，我注意到他们的母亲在拥抱他们，给他们做饭，和他们交谈，可是却没人照顾我。我12岁就开始去夜总会了，没人管我。我从没上过大学。我一周工作70个小时。我没成家，现在仍住在家里。如果我离开家，那将是一场灾难。我父母既不会读也不会写，我为他们做一切。我感觉没有门是为我敞开的。但我经常听人说：‘有梦就追，舍我其谁’，所以我真感到内疚，因为我没啥成就。”（科尔多瓦，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “My father is a simple laborer and my mother has the brain of a twelve year old child. She has a development problem. I was never able to ask her questions when I was growing up, like: ‘How does this work?’ or ‘What does this mean?’ She was the one asking me all the questions. She never said much to me beyond ‘Hello.’ For the longest time I thought it was normal. But when I started to visit the houses of my friends, I noticed that their mothers were hugging them, and cooking them food, and talking to them. But I had no one to take care of me. I started going to nightclubs at the age of twelve. I had no supervision. I never went to college. I still live at home now. I work seventy hours a week and I don’t have a family of my own. If I left the house, it would be a disaster. Neither of my parents can read or write. I do everything for them. I feel like there are no doors open for me, but often I hear people say: ‘No matter what, you can accomplish your dreams.’ So I do feel guilty for not achieving more.”(Cordoba, Argentina)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EvfrseyXM&u=005trlAagy1fco44l7qthj31kw11xjwt )

>  “她不像其他同龄的孩子那样叫什么，也不指什么。当我们试着纠正她，她从不回应。通常小事情都会让她心烦意乱，我们尽力安慰她，但都不管用。那时我只想告诉她我爱她，一切都会好起来的。但如果我想拥抱她或亲吻她，她会把我推开。她是我的小姑娘，但我甚至都吼不住她，就只是担心她。现在我们每周去看两次心理医生，情况正在好转。几个月前一切都开始改变，一天早上她拉着我的手，给我看她发现了什么。有时她看着我，听我说话。早上她是第一个醒来的，她会到床边来，请求躺在我们身边。她甚至喜欢被拥抱和亲吻了。”（布宜诺斯艾利斯，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “She wasn’t naming things like other children her age. She wasn’t pointing at things. She would never respond when we tried to correct her. Often small things would upset her, and we’d try to comfort her, but nothing worked. All I wanted to do was tell her that I loved her and everything would be ‘ok.’ But she would push away if I tried to hug or kiss her. She was my little girl but I couldn’t even hold her. All I ever did was worry about her. We go to a therapist twice a week now, and things are getting better. Everything began to change a few months ago. She pulled me by the hand one morning to show me what she found. And sometimes she looks at me and listens. She’s the first one to wake up in the morning, and she’ll come to the side of the bed, and ask to lie next to us. And she even loves to get hugs and kisses.”(Buenos Aires, Argentina)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Evf4JifTA&u=005trlAagy1fco2hzc5p4j31kw11xjzw )

>  “你能在街上感受到每个人都在担心。我们来自一个很小的小镇。我们整个经济的引擎是一个糖果厂，可大家正在被解雇。我不喜欢我的工作，我包糖果，还得整天呆在室内。年轻时我会考虑辞工，那时我的包总是打包好的。但当你感受到一只小手抓住你的手指，一切就变了。现在我很害怕失业。每天早上我们都一成不变，每当我不想去工作，他说‘来’，然后他给我一个拥抱，那改变了我。他是我的充电器。”（科尔多瓦，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “You can feel in the streets that everyone is worried. We come from a very small town. The engine of our entire economy is a candy factory, and people are getting laid off. I don’t like my job. I package the candies and I have to stay indoors all day. When I was younger, I would think about quitting. My bags were always packed. But everything changes when you feel a small hand gripping your finger. Now I’m terrified of losing my job. Every morning we have a routine. Whenever I don’t feel like going to work, he says ‘come here,’ and he gives me a hug, and that changes me. He’s my battery charger.”(Cordoba, Argentina)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EveyrF9L7&u=005trlAagy1fco07rd17vj31kw11xn53 )

>  “是有早期迹象的，我曾经有种感觉，我可以操控未来。在赌场走了好运，我就以为是因为我有控制结果的能力。那时我是个生物老师，结了婚，四个孩子，每周读三本书，每天晚上只睡几个小时。然后一天早上，在巴士上，有那么一会儿我脱离了现实：我在和一个朋友说话，我开始用一种完全不同的方式理解她，而我所理解的那些是邪恶的。就像我的整个心理结构改变了，我开始让人害怕，我失去了所有的过滤，我会说出所有那些我在想的奇奇怪怪的东西。人们认为我嗑药了。我失业了，我老婆带着孩子们回了娘家，最后我露宿街头。我花了好几年才意识到我得了精神分裂症。我被关在精神病院里两个月。现在我在吃三种药。我又在看书了。我已经赢回来一些自尊。我正在和我的孩子们建立关系。但我仍在抗争它。它一直在那儿，并不是来了就走了。它以一种持续的方式看着那个世界，而那正是我必须不断对抗的。”（科尔多瓦，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “There were early signs. I used to have this feeling that I could manipulate the future. I got lucky at casinos, and I thought it was because I had the power to control events. I was a biology teacher back then. I was married with four kids. I read three books per week. I was only getting a few hours of sleep every night. Then one morning on the bus I had a break from reality. I was speaking to a friend, and I started to understand her in a completely different way. And the things I understood were evil. It was like my entire mental structure had changed. I began to frighten people. I lost all filters. I would say all of the strange things that I was thinking. People thought I was on drugs. I lost my job. My wife went to her mother’s place with the kids. I ended up sleeping on the streets. It took me years to realize I had schizophrenia. I was put in a psychiatric ward for two months. Now I’m taking three different medications. I’m reading books again. I’ve got some self-esteem back. I’m building a relationship with my kids. But I’m still fighting it. It’s always there. It doesn’t come and go. It’s a continuous way of looking at the world that I must keep pushing back against.”(Cordoba, Argentina)
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EveiR7kt8&u=005trlAagy1fcnywhqd6dj31kw11xn22 )

>  “我父亲长大时压迫多多了，所以我们的世界观不一样。我不认为他觉得我幼稚，我认为他挺欣赏我有机会去抱有希望。对我来说世界似乎更柔和了点，也更宽容了点。我相信我们能解决我们的问题。我想他也曾有过同样的信念，也想过去改变世界，但或许他失望了。我正在尝试许多他年轻时尝试过的事情，但现在这是一个不同的世界，所以或许会有不同的结果。”（科尔多瓦，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “There was a lot more oppression when my father grew up, so we have different views of the world. I don’t think he views me as naïve. I think he appreciates that I have the opportunity to be hopeful. The world for me seems a little bit softer. A little bit kinder. I believe that we can solve our problems. I think he used to share those same beliefs. I think he wanted to change the world, and maybe he was disappointed. And now I’m trying many of the same things that he tried when he was young. But it’s a different world now. So maybe there will be different results.”(Cordoba, Argentina)

>  “我是他和世界之间的纽带，这可是个累人的活儿。顺利时我感觉责任感增强了。他小学毕业时，感觉就像大家都在为我们俩鼓掌。但不顺时我也感觉责任感增强了。他在人群中有困难。几年前他在超市里变得很紧张，他推了一个小女孩儿，女孩儿的爸爸很生气，朝着我吼。当时我一方面感到内疚，一方面又希望更多的人明白我所经历的。那次以后我们就没再去过超市。对我来说最好的时刻就是没有我他也能够与世界连接起来。上周四我们去拜访另一个有唐氏综合症的女孩，她那天挺糟糕的，交流很少。所以他想给她一盒多米诺骨牌作为礼物，但她拒绝了。他就再给，她又拒绝。他们就那样来回推就了一会儿，直到那个女孩把它当作一个游戏，并且笑了。然后他给了她一个拥抱，一个真正的拥抱，带着感情的。他做了一次接触，那是他的主意奥，不是我的。”（罗萨里奥，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “I’m the link between him and the rest of the world. It can be an exhausting role. When things go well, I feel an increased sense of responsibility. It felt like the audience was clapping for both of us when he graduated from primary school. But I also feel an increased sense of responsibility when things go wrong. He has difficulties in crowds of people. A few years ago he got very nervous at the supermarket, and he pushed a young girl. Her father got very angry and started screaming at me. Part of me felt guilty for what happened. But part of me wished that more people understood what I go through. We haven’t been to a supermarket since that incident. The best moments for me are when he’s able to link to the world without me. Last Thursday we were visiting another girl with Downs Syndrome. And she was having a bad day. There was very little communication. So he tried to give her a box of dominos as a gift. But she refused. So he tried again. But she refused again. They went back and forth like this for a while, until the girl started to view it as a game, and she started to smile. Then he gave her a hug. A real hug with feeling. He made a connection. And it was his idea. Not mine.”(Rosario, Argentina)

>  “巴拉圭的工作机会不多，那时我在街上卖些用具，没钱，什么都没有。我19岁来到阿根廷，生活好过多了。我每天都在工作，我快要像这样再开一家商店了。他们叫我很多称呼，像‘烂巴拉圭佬’，但现在我已经习惯了。刚开始我会试着反击，但现在不会了。刚来那会儿，一个男的隔着笼子想捅我，我跟他打了一架。但他带了二十个人回来，把我的店毁坏了，所以我不再反击了。现在这一片每个人都认识我，所以他们对我更尊重了。我儿子出生在这个国家，所以他是个阿根廷人了。他将来会去上学的。”（布宜诺斯艾利斯，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “There weren’t many opportunities to work in Paraguay. >  “我遇到他是在五年前，我贴了个提供保洁服务的广告，他回应了。他那儿真是一团糟，他活得像个隐士。他是个疑病症患者。他妻子2007年去世了，所以他就只是闲坐在电脑前，等着死亡。现在我们就像一家人，我每天都去看他。我们一起拍了不下于5000张照片了。我们去买东西、去散步，他现在甚至做饭了。他让我有了目标，他的成就让我骄傲。有时候我感觉我做了好大件事，他变成了一个完全不同的人。”（布宜诺斯艾利斯，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “I met him five years ago. >  “我父母在最后的独裁统治期间失踪了。他们是政治积极分子。我父亲先在1977被带走，一年以后，我母亲在世界杯期间被带走了。当时我们站在一个广场上，两辆车停下来，他们抓住我和我母亲，他们让我走了，但从那以后就再没听到过我母亲的信儿。这一切我都是后来才听说的，因为当时我才3岁。我祖父母抚养了我。当我还是个孩子时，他们告诉我我父母在工作。我曾经想象我父母在建一座摩天大楼，戴着安全帽，离封顶越来越近。直到10岁，我知道到底发生了什么，才不那样想了。但即便那样，对我来说我父母也还只是个概念，他们是二维的。但当我长到17岁，我去了他们初次相识的小镇。我找到他们的老朋友，他们给我讲了些故事。我了解到我父亲喜欢披头士，他也喜欢跳舞。一个男的给了我一件我父亲跳舞时穿的衣服。突然之间，我父母不再是概念了，他们是人，是Daniel和Viviana。第一次，我为他们而哭了。”（布宜诺斯艾利斯，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “My parents disappeared during the last dictatorship. They were political activists. My father was taken first in 1977. My mother was taken a year later during the World Cup. We were standing in a public square, and two cars stopped, and they grabbed me and my mother. They let me go. But my mother was never heard from again. I learned all of this later because I was only three at the time. My grandparents raised me. When I was a child they would tell me that my parents were working. I used to imagine them building a skyscraper, wearing helmets, and getting closer and closer to the top. It wasn’t until the age of ten that I learned what really happened. But even then, my parents were only ideas to me. They were two-dimensional. But when I turned seventeen, I visited the town where they first met. I found their old friends and they told me stories. I learned that my father loved the Beatles. He also loved to dance. A man gave me a costume that my father would wear when he danced. And suddenly my parents weren’t ideas anymore. They were people. They were Daniel and Viviana. And for the first time, I cried for them.”(Buenos Aires, Argentina)

>  “这段时间真是苦乐参半。我努力想保持开心，因为据说宝宝能消解悲伤的时刻。但我爸爸五个月前去世了。时至今日，我们还不知道当时到底发生了什么：当时他独自一人，我们认为有人企图抢劫他，因为他被发现时是被枪杀在他的车里。我想对我来说这是最难的，因为我们是如此亲近。过去我工作的时候，他每天都去医院看望我。他死后不久，我得知我怀孕了。我想我的怀孕让我们家还有点生气，尤其是我妈，现在她一直和我在一起，给我弄我需要的一切。宝宝让我们俩都向前看。她将是个女孩。”（布宜诺斯艾利斯，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “It’s a bittersweet time. >  “我年轻时总是穿得像个男的那样出门，然后再把衣服换掉。我妈说我中了邪，我爸说我没用。他们甚至带我去看医生，看看我怎么了。但我爷爷总是支持我，他比我父母更开明。我想是因为他在一家24小时餐馆工作吧，他见过所有那些夜里出来活动的人。甚至当我还是个孩子的时候，他看到我穿的衣服，会对我说：‘如果你是个女娃，会很漂亮的。’当我终于告诉他我所感受到的一切时，他说：‘你是个很棒的人，不管你怎么了我都不怕。’”（布宜诺斯艾利斯，阿根廷）@人在深圳 “When I was younger, I’d always leave the house dressed like a man, but then I’d change my clothes. He was more open-minded than my parents. I think it's because he worked at a 24 hour restaurant and met all the people who came out at night. Even when I was a child, he'd see the clothes I wore, and he'd tell me: ‘If you were a girl, you’d be very beautiful.’ When I finally told him everything I was feeling, he said: ‘You’re a great person, and I’ll never be afraid of what’s going on with you.’”(Buenos Aires, Argentina)

>  “过去八年我一直是联合国难民署的通讯部主管，我的工作就是让人们关心世界上六千万流离失所的人。我真希望我能把他们的故事讲给每个人听，因为如果人们了解了他们的故事，我想就不会有这么多阻隔了，也不会有那么多人淹死在海里了。但我没想到要让人们关心这个有多么困难。并不是说人们自私，我只是觉得当人们自身缺乏安全感时，他们是很难去关心别人的。当世界不稳定，人们感到脆弱，那么脆弱的人就会专注于保护他们所拥有的，他们会专注于自己的家庭、自己的群体。当你感觉受到威胁时，你是很难去欢迎陌生人的，即使那些陌生人比你更弱势。”小编@人在深圳 “For the last eight years I’ve been the head of communications for the UN Refugee Agency. My job is to make people care about the sixty million displaced people in the world. I wish I could tell every single one of their stories. Because if people knew their stories, I don’t think there would be so many walls. And there wouldn’t be so many people drowning in the seas. But I don’t think I anticipated how difficult it would be to make people care. It’s not that people are selfish. I just think that people have a hard time caring when they feel insecure. When the world is unstable, people feel vulnerable. And vulnerable people focus on protecting what they have. They focus on their own families. They focus on their own communities. It can be very hard to welcome strangers when you’re made to feel threatened. Even if those strangers are more vulnerable than you.”

>  “我第一个纹身纹的是‘我恨’，很久以前我又纹身把它盖住了。纹它时我21岁，那是我此生一个非常自暴自弃的时期：我从大学退学了；女友刚把我甩了，找了个比我年长的家伙；我梳着扫把头，没少跳碰碰舞；感觉家里每个人都对我失望。我爸是个非常成功的律师，我哥是名外交官。所以我反叛一切，决定要过一种完全‘诗意的生活’。我在沙漠里住了几年。然后我来到纽约，试图当个诗人。最后我在康尼岛游乐场的杂耍里扮怪物。但15年后，连那都变得像其他任何工作了：每天重复同样的东西，只是观众变了。我还是没搞清楚我在逃离什么。没有什么真正的局外人，我们都得呼吸，我们都得吃饭，我们都得工作。我想逃离一切，但逃避不了我自己：我仍是个中产阶级，来自郊区，一个智力上的孩砸。”@人在深圳 ：《人在纽约：故事版》已经由重庆出版社引进，春节后上市。我拿到了样书，好棒！“My first tattoo said: ‘I Hate’. I tattooed over it a long time ago. I was twenty-one when I got it. It was a very self-destructive period of my life. I’d dropped out of college. My girlfriend had just left me for an older guy. I’d gotten a Mohawk and was doing a lot of slam dancing. I felt like everyone in the family was disappointed with me. My dad was a very successful attorney. My brother was a diplomat. So I rebelled against everything and decided that I was going to live the whole ‘poetry lifestyle.’ I lived in the desert for a couple years. Then I came to New York and tried to survive as a poet. I ended up working as a freak in the Coney Island Side Show. But after fifteen years, even that became like any other job. It was the exact same thing every day. Only the audience changed. I still haven’t figured out what I was trying to escape. There’s no such thing as a true outsider. We all have to breathe. We all have to eat. We all have to work. I wanted to run away from everything but I ran into myself. I’m still a middle class, intellectual kid from the suburbs.”

>  “上帝没有像他曾经那样回应我的祈祷，但他仍然跟我说话，他通过我的大脑和我的嘴巴跟我交谈。他对我失望，因为他想让我向街上的人挥手，而我没有，所以他把我的钱拿走了，告诉我离开我的工作。我的家人把我送去医院，他们说我有躁郁症。但我没精神病，我吃药是因为那是说好的一部分，这样我才能有自己的住处，但我真没精神病。当我把债还清，上帝就会让我焕发新声，他会让我成为一个伟大的歌唱家。有天晚上我做了一个梦，梦见我在唱歌，金色的东西从天而降，我抓住它，然后每个人都聚集到我周围。希望你为我祈祷，然后你会看到真相的。向上帝祷告吧，问他：‘这个人诚实么，还是真有精神病？’”@人在深圳 “God doesn’t answer my prayers like he once did. >  “我妈妈和我一直都很亲密。但我爸爸去世后，我们不得不重新学习该如何沟通。我们彼此不再坦诚，为此还去看了心理医生。当时我爸爸生病让我们压力很大，我们不想再制造任何烦恼，所以我们就尽量互相保护着。如果我们某天过得糟糕，或者心情不好，我们都不会承认，一切的回答都是‘我还好’。但其实我们并不好，显而易见，所以我们总是互相担心。它带来了很多精神压力和争执，我们不得不重新学习如何承认这一点，当我们某天过得不好。因为你永远无法真正知道别人是不是‘好’，除非你相信他们会告诉你，如果有什么不对劲儿。”@人在深圳 “My mom and I have always been close. But we had to learn how to communicate again after my dad died. It took therapy. We’d stopped being honest with each other. My dad’s illness had been so stressful that we didn’t want to create any additional worries. So we tried to protect each other. Neither of us would admit if we were having a bad day. Or if we were feeling depressed. The answer to everything was always: ‘I’m fine.’ But we weren’t fine. And it was obvious. So we worried about each other all the time. It caused a lot of stress and arguments. We had to relearn how to admit when we were having a bad day. Because you can never truly know if someone's 'fine' unless you trust them to tell you when something's wrong."

>  “我称之为打击人的经文，有六处，它们是用来敲打同性恋的。搞笑的是我从未感受到上帝给我压力，只有他的信徒。但我十分渴望上帝能改变我，我不想成为一个群体的一员，却带给它这么多耻辱。所以二十几岁时，我开始祈祷上帝能让我成为直男。如果吃片药就成，我会的。我奉了神职。我结婚了。我告诉我妻子，我曾跟男的交往过，但我说服了我们两个，我可以选择有所不同，我想变正常，我想要孩子。我认为这只是个承诺的问题。我甚至试过采取修复性的心理治疗，为了向她表明我是认真的。他们试图教导我同性恋不是真的，他们说我只是有一个专横的母亲。但我就是变不过来，我老出问题，我给不了我妻子她所需要的。我的婚姻还是结束了。我付出这么多努力，但都没用。我为上帝出尔反尔而生气，但过了段时间，我终于明白为什么他不改变我了，他从未觉得他需要这么做。”@人在深圳 “I call them clobber verses. If I could have taken a pill, I would have. I joined the ministry. I got married. I told my wife that I’d had experiences with men, but I convinced both of us that I could choose to be different. I wanted to be normal. I wanted kids. I thought it was just a matter of commitment. I even tried to take reparative therapy classes—just to show her I was serious. My marriage ended. I had tried so hard but nothing worked. I got so angry with God for not keeping up his end of the bargain. But after some time, I finally realized why he wouldn’t change me. He never felt like he needed to.”

>  “我曾想：到了纽约，随着环境的巨大变换，我能成为任何我想成为的人。我想总会有一个计划，或者发生一个事件，然后我就永远不会感到孤独了，我会成为很棒的那种人——找不到个更好的词，就说像Carrie Bradshaw那样棒吧。可事实上呢，很多时候我仍然是独自一人，我想是因为我害怕给周围的人添麻烦吧——如果我不够有趣呢？如果我悲伤和抱怨的那一面多过我好的那一面呢？我是在浪费别人的时间吗？当我和别人在一起时，我害怕去要求一定程度上的友好和尊重，因为也许那样会让我更觉得自己是个负担。所以我跟别人接触不多，很多时候都在独处。但在Snapchat上看到人家去逛而没我，我还是会搓火。但我也正在尽量改变这种想法。如果我没努力过，就不该觉得自己被冷落。我不是现实生活的主角，我不能指望仅仅因为我的存在，良好的人际关系就会落到我的头上来。”@人在深圳 ：Carrie Bradshaw，《欲望都市》第一女主角，活得洒脱。“I thought when I came to New York it was going to be this huge change of scenery and that I could be whoever I want to be. I thought there’d always be a plan, or an event, and that I’d never feel alone, and that I’d be very ‘fabulous’ — for lack of a better word. ‘Carrie Bradshaw-esque,’ so to speak. But in reality, I still spend a lot of time alone. I think it’s because I’m afraid of being a burden on those around me. What if I’m not fun enough? What if the parts of me that are sad and complaining outweigh the parts of me that are good? Will I be wasting other people’s time? And when I do spend time with other people, I’m afraid to demand a certain level of kindness and respect. Because maybe that will make me even more of a burden. So I don’t reach out to other people very much. I spend a lot of time alone. But then I still get mad when I look on Snapchat and see people hanging out without me. But I’m trying to change my thinking. I’m not allowed to feel left out if I’m not making an effort. I’m not the protagonist of reality. I can’t expect good relationships to happen just because I exist.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EpK4jFphF&u=005trlAajw1fbi8w76rrrj31kw11xwok )

>  “去年我开始给美术课做人体模特。我是加大码，所以我有点担心脱光光。一想到大家看到我的肚腩、大腿和所有赘肉，我就紧张。但显然我身上的曲线画起来还蛮有趣的，在课堂上，所有我觉得不好的那些都被当成了挺有价值的东西，有个学生跟我说画那些直愣愣的线条才没劲呢。那对我来说是个解脱，过去我一直对我的肚子不自信，但现在我的肚子已经成为这么多美丽的艺术作品的一部分。”@人在深圳 “Last year I started figure modeling for art classes. I’m plus-sized, so I was a little worried about being nude. I was nervous about everyone seeing my stomach, and my thighs, and all my fat. But apparently my curves are fun to draw. In the classroom, all the features I saw as negative were viewed as assets. One student told me that it’s no fun to draw straight lines. It’s been liberating for me. I’ve always been insecure about my belly. But now my belly has been part of so many beautiful pieces of art.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/pic/EpIX1wAeS?rl=0 )

>  “我想成为一个讲笑演员。最难的是找素材，不只是搞笑的那种，而且要真实。单纯搞笑会流于哗众取宠，而好的段子会以一定的方式表现真理。我不认为我的经历足以让我知道对别人来说什么才是真理。我的日子过得还挺爽的，没有什么太惨的事情发生在我身上。我创作的劲头很旺，但我不确信我的储备足以实现它。最近我去了上州的一个开放麦，有个老家伙演一个曾经的海洛因瘾君子，我只是有种感觉，就是你要留意他说的每一个字眼儿，而不仅仅是他抖的那些包袱。我还差得远呢。”@人在深圳 “I want to be a stand up comic. The hardest thing is to find material that’s not just funny—but also true. Funny can just be a surprise. But good comedy articulates truth in a certain way. And I don't think I've experienced enough to know what’s true for other people. I’ve had a bit of a charmed life. Nothing too traumatic has happened to me. I have a lot of creative energy but I’m not sure that I have the arsenal to back it up. Recently I was at an open mic upstate, and there was an older guy performing who used to be a heroin addict. There was just this sense that you should be paying attention to every word he says, and not just the punch line. I’m not there yet.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EpIbwl49L&u=005trlAagw1fbi0n2kdwlj31kw11x0wd )

>  “感觉有时候她并不想让我出生，每件事情她都怪我，我就像个灰姑娘，尽管我是个男的。我猜可能是因为我丑吧，女孩们都躲着我。我的兄弟们倒比我好看。当我再长大些，一切就都是关于钱了。她从没跟我讨论过任何自己的事情，看起来她总是想要从我这儿得到些什么。有一次我哭着给她打电话，当时因为我正在戒大麻，人很颓。她只是跟我说：‘那些钱都被你糟蹋了，还不如给我呢。’她曾经把我学生贷款的支票兑现，有一次她甚至用我的社安号去办了张信用卡，我收到账单才知道。所以我离开了她，不再接她的电话。两年前，她给我打电话说她得了癌症，要动手术，但我连那个电话都没接，我以为她又在骗我。她留言说：‘Michael，我一直在努力联系你。我爱你，我知道你也爱我。’但我还是忽略了它。她死了。她的死让我备受折磨。最近我在尝试写写我的人生，但我无法跳过我母亲这一章。我多希望我能开始我的人生故事，从那个电话，从她说她爱我开始。我唯一另一次感受到她的爱是当我尝试强效可卡因的时候，当时我十几岁，已经嗑了几周了。我到她房间去要苏打粉，她哭了，看上去吓坏了，她说：‘Michael，你为什么要苏打粉？’那一刻我感受到了爱，它是那么强烈，以至于那之后我就放弃吸毒了，我也再没吸过，我也没去参加戒毒计划什么的，那感觉就是那么强烈。”@人在深圳 “I felt like sometimes she didn’t want me born. I was like Cinderella—even though I was a dude. She blamed me for everything. Maybe it’s because I was ugly, I guess. Girls were all running from me. My brothers were better looking. When I grew older, it was all about money. Mom and I never discussed anything personal. It seemed like she always wanted something from me. One time I called her crying, because I was trying to quit marijuana, and I felt really depressed. She just told me: ‘You’re wasting all that money on weed. You could be giving it to me instead.” She used to cash my student loan checks. One time she even used my social security number to get a credit card, and I didn’t even know until I got the bill. So I detached myself from her. I stopped answering the phone. Then two years ago she called to tell me she had cancer, and she needed an operation, but I didn’t even answer the phone. I thought she was tricking me again. She left a message, it said: ‘Michael, I’ve been trying to get a hold of you. I love you. And I know you love me.’ And I just ignored it. And she died. And I’m haunted by that. I’ve been trying to write about my life lately, but I can’t get past my mother. I wish I could just start my story with that phone call. With her saying that she loved me. The only other time I ever felt love from her was when I tried crack cocaine. I was a teenager, and I had been using for a couple weeks, and I went in her room to ask for baking soda. She started crying, and she looked scared, and she said: ‘Michael, why do you need baking soda?’ And I felt love at that moment. And it was so strong that I quit doing crack right then. I never used again. I didn’t go to a program or anything. That’s how strong that feeling was.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EpiJW7yfe&u=005trlAajw1fbewa4mv4ij31kw11xn1w )

>  “我属于他们所说的‘种族含糊’的那类人，所以我得到了很多群演的工作。今天我演的是个公园里的行人，这是我十月以来的第25份工作了。光在《国务卿女士》里，我就演过以色列军官、哥伦比亚大学生，还有伊朗总统顾问，这还是在同一季里。只要你没台词，他们就会一直用你。也许有一天我能演一个能反复出现的角色吧，但现在能这样我真的很感激了。我父母都是萨尔瓦多移民，他们是我所知道的工作最辛苦的人。他们真的很怀疑我想成为一名演员，所以我乐于让他们看到我在工作。我的第一次演出是一部Hallmark圣诞电影，跟Melissa Joan Hart和Dean Cain演的，当时我父母都不相信我竟然跟小女巫Sabrina和超人同台演出呢。”@人在深圳 “I’m what they call ‘ethnically ambiguous,’ so I get a lot of work as a background actor. I’m playing a ‘parkgoer’ today. It’s my 25th job since October. In Madam Secretary alone, I’ve played an Israeli military officer, a Colombian college student, and an advisor to the Iranian president. And that was all in the same season. They’ll keep using you as long as you don’t have any speaking lines. Maybe one day I'll have a recurring role, but right now I’m really grateful to be doing this. My parents are immigrants from El Salvador. They are the hardest working people I know. They were really skeptical about me wanting to be an actor, so I love that they get to see me working. My first gig was a Hallmark Christmas movie with Melissa Joan Hart and Dean Cain. My parents couldn’t believe that I was on the same show as Sabrina The Teenage Witch and Superman.”

>  “当最后一个孩子上大学走了，事情到了一个地步——过去那只是个借口，而我不能再隐瞒了。我厌倦了那种担心，担心别人是否怀疑，或者他们是否发现了，又或者如果他们知道了，是否还关心我。第一个我公开自己同志身份的人是我老婆，那让人痛苦，它也成了我们婚姻的结束。我就那样不停地跟她说对不起，我想她感觉被人离弃了，我很抱歉。我也在想她会觉得我们的生活是一个谎言，但我不那么看。我们是一家人，我们有四个很棒的孩子，我们把他们抚养成人，这些都是事实。我并不想造成那些伤害，但我现在感觉很真实，我为我所做的事感到遗憾，但我又为我所做的事感到如此高兴。”@人在深圳 “When the last kid left for college, it came to a point where it was just pretense. And I couldn’t hide it anymore. I was tired of worrying if people suspected, or if they’d find out, or if they’d still care about me if they knew. The first person I came out to was my wife. It was wrenching. It was the end of our marriage. I just kept telling her I was sorry. I think she felt abandoned. And I’m sorry for that. I also think she felt that our life together was a lie. But I don’t see it that way. We were a family. We had four wonderful children that we raised to adulthood. And those are facts. I’m not happy about the hurt I caused. But I feel authentic now. I regret the things I did, but I’m so happy about what I’ve done.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EnaTEA5IH&u=005trlAagw1faypf125lej31kw11xjuy )

>  “我四十八了。我和一个女人好了两年多了，我要到那个点了，可能我得摆脱她，或者表个态。我从没结过婚，我曾跟两三个女人走得挺近，实际上有一次都快要到市政厅办结婚了，但我总是退缩。我想我认为最终我会遇到一个女人，让我脑洞大开，一条明路浮现出来，然后我就知道她就是那个对的人。但它并没发生，我从没到一个点上说结婚的念头不再让我心神不定。这回我又走到这一步了，我刚和这个女人在公园里度过了美好的一天，挺愉快的。但现在我的思绪跳向未来，我担心有些事情我还没看到，我怕一旦我们相互许下诺言，就有事情显露出来，然后突然之间，我的生活变得比我独自一人时更糟。”@人在深圳 “I’m forty-eight now. I’ve been dating a woman for over two years. And I’m getting to the point where I probably need to cut her loose or commit. I’ve never been married. I’ve gotten close with two or three women. I actually got as close as City Hall one time. But I’ve always backed down. I guess I thought that I’d eventually meet a woman, and some sort of pathway would open up in my mind, and I’d know that she was the right one. But it hasn’t happened. I’ve never gotten to the point where the thought of marriage doesn’t freak me out. And here I am again. I just spent a wonderful day in the park with this woman. It was lovely. But now my mind jumps to the future. And I worry that there’s something I’m not seeing. I'm afraid that something will reveal itself once we’ve exchanged our vows, and suddenly my life will be worse than when I was alone.”- 4/27 on Facebook

>  “我们做朋友很长时间了。我们俩结婚都四十年，各自的配偶都去世了。我丈夫去世几年后，有天晚上他给我打电话，请我到纽约跳个舞。那天晚上他戴了一顶高顶窄边的大礼帽，打了白色的领带，但他有点喝高了，走路送我回家时掉进了一个雪堆里。我都等不及要再见到他了——第二天早上，我坐在客厅，看着报纸，心想：'哦卖糕的，四十年的婚姻，此刻我却满心期待着一个男人会打电话过来。’”@人在深圳 “We’ve been friends for a long time. Both of us were married for forty years and both of our spouses passed away. A couple years after my husband died, he called me one night and invited me to a dance in New York. He wore a top hat and white tie, but he had a little too much to drink that night, and he fell into a snowdrift while he was walking me home. I couldn’t wait to see him again. The next morning I was sitting in my living room, reading the paper, and thinking: ‘Oh my God. Forty years of marriage. And here I am hoping that a man will call.’”- 4/27 on Facebook

>  “我生命的百分之五六十我妈妈都病得很严重。我父亲离开时，她精神崩溃了，最后进了精神病房。我年少时她还得过两次乳腺癌。我是她唯一的孩子，所以压力山大。当朋友们在操场上时，我却得回家，去把妈妈从浴室的地板上扶起来。现在我新婚不久，孩子快要出生了。但我仍然要时时刻刻担心她，她没再婚，所以她只有我。她现在还在吸氧。我度蜜月时她病得很严重，我不得不每三小时给医院打个电话。每天晚上我下班回家，她都有一长串事情要我去做。如果我有几天不去看她，她会说我多自私，她会说：‘算了，没人来看我我也挺好，别回来了。’我不知道我想要什么，但我正在开始一个新的家庭，我正处在一个节骨眼儿上——我想有些许自由，好过我的生活。”@人在深圳 “My mom has been really sick for 50 to 60 percent of my life. She had a nervous breakdown when my father left, and she ended up in a psychiatric ward. Then she had breast cancer twice while I was young. I was her only child so it was a lot of pressure. While my friends were at the playground, I’d be coming home to pick my mother up off the bathroom floor. I’m newly married now and have a child on the way. But I still have to worry about her all the time. She never remarried, so I’m all she has. She’s on oxygen now. She was so sick during my honeymoon that I had to call the hospital every three hours. Every evening when I get home from work, she has a list of things for me to do. If I don’t visit for a few days, she tells me how selfish I am. She’ll say: ‘Forget it. I’m fine without visitors. Don’t come back.’ I don’t know what I want to happen. But I’m starting a new family. And I’m at the point where I’d like some freedom to live my life.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EmYs1xiM8&u=005trlAagw1fax663mzwpj31kw11xjtp )

>  “我在皇后区一所社区大学教英语。我喜欢这份工作，但我讨厌评卷，我宁愿讨论莎士比亚讨论个没完没了。我挺羡慕数学老师的，他们只需要把答题卡过机器一扫就完了，而给学生的作文评分可微妙和复杂得多。如果他们有好想法，但英语语言技能还不够呢？如果英语是他们的第二语言呢？如果他们生活中碰到过难题呢？我要对这些视而不见吗？或者我打分时要考虑背景因素吗？我想设定高标准，让我的学生们为下一步做好准备。但他们很多人已经有一种挫败感，我不想再给他们泼凉水哦。”@人在深圳 “I teach English at a community college in Queens. I love the job, but I hate grading papers. I’d prefer to just have one continuous discussion about Shakespeare. I envy the math teachers who can just put their tests through a Scantron machine. Placing value on a student’s writing is much more nuanced and complicated. What if they have great ideas but their English language skills aren’t as developed? What if English is their second language? What if they’ve faced major challenges in life? Do I ignore those things? Or do I consider context while grading? I want to set high standards and prepare my students for what comes next. But so many of them already have a self-defeating attitude. And I don’t want to discourage them any further.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EmY8tqRPW&u=005trlAagw1fax5950vu2j31kw11x0xg )

>  “本来以为今天我们就只是去他姐姐家，但当我到了那儿，Jim不在。他姐姐给了我一个信封，说Jim在我们看《胡桃夹子》的地方等我。但当我到了那个剧院，只有Jim的父母在那儿，他们又给了我一个信封，说Jim在我们最喜欢的咖啡馆等我。但当我到了那个咖啡馆，只有我父母在那儿，他们又给了我一个信封，说Jim在我们第一次划船的地方等我.。当我到了这儿，Jim在这儿呢，他给了我最后一个信封。我打开了四个信封，上面写着：‘你’ ‘会’ ‘嫁给’ ‘我么？’”@人在深圳 “I thought we were just going to hang out at his sister’s place today, but when I got there, Jim wasn’t there. But they gave me another envelope and told me that Jim was waiting for me at the place where we first went row boating. And when I got here, Jim was here. And he gave me one last envelope. >  “六个月大时，我被丢在中国北方的一家孤儿院，有个小纸条别在我的小衣服上，上边只有我那个村的名字。孤儿院给我起名叫高安娜，翻译过来就是‘高山上来的女孩’。我妈妈通过邮件收到我的照片后，就决定收养我。当时她45岁，刚离婚不久。她从未生孩子，所以我从小到大就只是我们两个人。记得高中时，我们有过一次争吵，我妈妈情绪很激动，哭着说：‘我们不能吵，就只有我们两个，我们得相依为命。’那一刻我才意识到我在多大程度上改变了我妈妈的生活。当然，这一点她从一开始就知道，但却是我需要去了解的东西。”@人在深圳 ：图3是Facebook原博中的一条热门评论，点赞35046个，回复567次。一位叫Sharon Gilligan的妈妈分享了2003年她在南宁收养她现在14岁的女儿时，女儿被放到她臂弯中的一刻。“When I was six months old, I was dropped off at an orphanage in Northern China with a little note pinned on my shirt. It only had the name of my village. The orphanage named me Gaoanna, which translates to ‘Girl From High Mountains.’ My mother decided to adopt me after she received my picture in the mail. She was 45 at the time. She had recently gotten divorced. She’d never had children. So it’s just been the two of us my whole life. I remember one time in high school, we got in an argument and my mom got very emotional. She started crying and said: ‘We can’t fight. It’s just the two of us. We have to stick together.’ At that moment I realized how much I had changed my mom’s life. She’d known from the start, of course. But it was something I needed to learn.”- 6/2 on Facebook
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/pic/EmIm3k38x?rl=0 )

>  “我写了25年了。我刚完成我的第二部小说。就在最后期限前，我有一种严重的焦虑，几乎无法呼吸，也难以平静下来，我还以为是我心脏病发作呢。一部分是最后期限的压力，但另一部分是那种要做一些很棒的事情的压力：我感觉自己一直都是‘就快到了’，我想我还在努力证明我挺专业的。我一直都在场上，但每一次我起身击球，下雨，比赛取消了。我希望最终能有所突破，我不知道会以一种什么样的形式，也许是一本畅销书，或者是好评如潮，或者是一个评审邀请。我看那些成功作家的采访，他们大多数人都会指出具体的一件事，然后说：‘从那之后，我就一发而不可收拾。’那就是我想要的，一炮而红，一帆风顺。”@人在深圳 “I’ve been writing for twenty-five years. I just finished my second novel. I had a really severe anxiety attack right before my deadline. I thought I was having a heart attack. I could barely breathe. I couldn’t calm down. Part of it was just the pressure of the deadline. But another part of it was the pressure to do something great. I feel like I’ve always been ‘almost there.’ I think I’m still trying to prove I’m a professional. I’ve always been on the playing field, but every time I get up to bat, the game gets cancelled for rain. I'm hoping to finally break through. I don’t know what form that will take. Maybe a bestseller, or a great review, or an invitation to sit on a panel. When I read interviews with successful authors, most of them point at a specific event, and say: ‘After that happened, I never looked back.’ And that’s what I want. To never look back.”- 6/6 on Facebook
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EmAQV4gW6&u=005trlAagw1faua5auvqxj31kw11x43c )

>  “我出生三天我妈就不要我了，我是祖父母养大的。他们是移民，他们只能教我那些他们所知道的东西。他们认为看孩子就行了，孩子说什么一概不听。在他们的世界里，你不应该有感情或意见，直到你十八岁成年。所以当我告诉他们我爸虐待人，他们不想听，我该保持沉默，道歉就免了吧。一到十六岁我就离开了家，然后立刻就进入了一段虐待性的男女关系：我在寻找爱，而他看起来像有爱，他给了我那些我从未有过的，他让我觉得被需要——我给他做饭时他有爱，他发脾气我安抚他时他有爱，但过不了一会儿，就再也没什么能安抚他了。”@人在深圳 “My mom gave me up when I was three days old, and I was raised by my paternal grandparents. They were immigrants. They could only teach me what they knew. And they thought that children should be seen and not heard. In their world, you're not supposed to have feelings or opinions until you turn eighteen. So when I told them that my father was abusive, they didn’t want to hear it. I was expected to keep quiet. And apologies were expected to be forgiven. I left the house as soon as I turned sixteen. And I immediately entered an abusive relationship. I was looking for love and he seemed like love. He gave me what I never had. He made me feel needed. He loved when I cooked for him. He loved that I soothed him when he lost his temper. But after awhile, nothing could soothe him anymore.”- 6/7 on Facebook
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EmAwO8Ww0&u=005trlAagw1fau9386a5fj31kw11xdjz )

>  “我一直相信有天堂，但爸爸去世后，我很难再依靠那样的理解了。我曾是一个爸爸的乖乖女，他的去世让我在情感上乱了套：过去我可以闭上眼，想象他在哪儿。但人生第一次，我在地图上不能确定他的位置。即使我在大学上了天文课，用望远镜我也找不到他。他不在了，那比我想象的还要真实得多。这真的动摇了我的信念，我必须有一个更深刻地理解——到底什么是‘天堂’。我还在努力，但我仍然每天都跟他说话，我仍然相信我会再见到他。”@人在深圳 “I’ve always believed in heaven. But it was so hard to lean on that understanding after my father passed away. I was a Daddy’s girl. His death was an emotional clusterfuck. I could close my eyes and imagine he was somewhere else. But for the first time in my life, I couldn’t pinpoint his location on a map. And even though I’d taken an astronomy class in college, I couldn’t find him with a telescope. His absence was so much more real than I thought it would be. And it really shook my beliefs. I had to form a deeper understanding of what exactly ‘heaven’ means. And I’m still working on that. But I do still talk to him everyday. And I still believe that I’ll see him again.”-6/4 on Facebook
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EmAlR2Hj4&u=005trlAagw1fau8awpscaj31kw11x7cx )

>  “最难的是她离家去上大学的时候，我们提前几天把她送去的，所以当时校园里空无一人，我清楚地记得：她就那样，独自一人走过那片校园里的四方院。而我，望着女儿的背影，目送她走进了她人生的下一个阶段。好多问题，在我脑子里翻滚：‘我们给她做足准备了么？她快乐么？如果她不快乐，她会乐意告诉我们么？’回顾过去，我真希望我没在那些小事上操那么心——她小时候，我们是如此操心：她是否进了足球队；舞蹈比赛她是否被选在前排；或者音乐会上是否有她吹长笛。我们很操心这些事，因为我们在寻找任何一种证明，证明我们做得还不错。我们拼命想成为好父母，我们仿佛成了我们的孩子。我希望过去我知道这些事情会有多快消退，而一旦她长大成人，它们又是多么地微不足道。”@人在深圳 “The hardest was when she left for college. We dropped her off a couple days early, so the campus was empty, and I have this very clear image of her walking alone across the quad. I stared at my daughter’s back while she literally walked into the next phase of her life. So many questions were running through my mind: ‘Did we prepare her enough? Is she happy? Will she feel comfortable enough to tell us if she’s not?’ Looking back, I wish I hadn’t fretted so much over the small stuff. When she was young, we were worried so much about whether she started on the soccer team, or if she got chosen for the front row at the dance competition, or if she was playing flute at the recital. We worried so much about that stuff because we were looking for any sort of validation that we were doing a good job. And in our desperation to be good parents we became our children. I wish I knew how fast all that stuff would fade away. And how little any of that would matter once she became an adult.”-6/8 on Facebook
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EmmLGq9QT&u=005trlAagw1fask0nkm5aj31kw11xwle )

>  “当你4岁时，你的绝活儿可棒了，你能翻跟头儿，还能打车轱辘儿。其实我不会打车轱辘儿，但姐姐会。她5岁，她可喜欢跟我玩儿了。她喜欢飞，每次坏人偷字的时候她都能转危为安。水妞儿、火妞儿、风妞儿，还有鲨妞儿都是她的朋友。鲨妞儿有鲨鱼的力量，每一次她都能拯救世界。她只需要伸出双手，用劲儿想着鲨鱼就行了。但我还没见过姐姐，我都不知道她叫啥名儿，因为，因为她是我想象出来哒。”@人在深圳 “When you’re four you can do awesome tricks. You can do a tumble and a cartwheel. Actually I can’t do a cartwheel, but my sister can do that. She’s five years old and likes to play with me but I haven’t met her and I don’t know her name because she’s imaginary. She likes to fly. Her job is so save the day every time the bad guys try to steal the word. She is friends with Water Girl, and Fire Girl, and Wind Girl, and Shark Girl. Shark Girl has the power of sharks. She can save the world every single time. All she has to do is put out her hands and think really hard about sharks.”- 6/9 on Facebook

>  “我爸要我回博茨瓦纳，他说他老了，他需要我回家。我也想念家人，但我想留在这儿。这儿的生活不一样，我遇到了这么多人，来自这么多不同的文化。我跑过半程马拉松，甚至完成一次铁人三项。而在博茨瓦纳是不一样的，我完全依赖于我爸，女生直到结婚才离开家。所以我想留下。但我姐是我在美国唯一的家人，上周她告诉我她要回博茨瓦纳了，所以现在我要靠自己了。我很担心，因为，虽然我不喜欢麻烦别人，我也从没麻烦过我姐，但以后我想指望她也指望不上了。几个月前我加入了我们教会的‘连接组’，现在我有这么多朋友了，她们就像我的姐妹，我们一起早午餐、晚餐、徒步，我能感受到她们很爱我，所以我希望她们能像我的家人一样。”@人在深圳 “My father wants me to come home to Botswana. I’ve done half marathons. I even did a triathlon. It’s different back in Botswana. I was completely dependent on my father. Women don’t leave home until they get married. So I’d like to stay here. But my sister is the only family that I have in America. And last week she told me that she’s moving back to Botswana. So now I’ll be on my own. And I’m worried. Because I don’t like to ask for help. But I never had a problem asking her for help. And now I won’t have that anymore. But a few months ago I joined something at my church called a ‘connect group.’ And now I have so many friends. They are like my sisters. We have brunches, and dinners, and go hiking. I feel very loved by them. So I’m hoping they will be like my family.”

>  “我第一次接触到芭蕾是在7岁，当时一个流动表演团来到我们教堂，在北卡罗莱纳州。到我11岁时，一周练六天，它成了我全身心的投入，修行般虔诚。最终我进了纽约城市芭蕾舞团。我一直把芭蕾当成我侍奉上帝的方式，我认为这是上帝的召唤。你可以说我的看法轻率或肤浅，但你也可以把它延伸到无限——为什么我们有画？为什么我们有建筑？我认为这都是一种敬奉上帝的形式。在一个世俗的年代，戏院就相当于教堂。这个世界可以如此缺乏同情和协作，但在戏院里，我们看到了塑造给我们的美、秩序、和谐，一次两个小时。那可是人们做了很多奉献，才使之成为可能。”@人在深圳 “I was first exposed to ballet at the age of seven when a traveling company came to my church in North Carolina. By the time I was eleven I was practicing six days a week. It became my all-consuming monastic devotion. I eventually made it to the New York City Ballet. I’ve always seen ballet as my way of serving God. I think it’s what God has called me to do. You can call it frivolous, or superficial. But you can stretch that argument to infinity. Why do we have painting? Why do we have architecture? I think it’s all a form of worship. In a secular age the theater becomes the cathedral. There can be such a lack of empathy and collaboration in this world. But in the theater we see beauty and order and harmony modeled for us-- two hours at a time. And it took a lot of sacrifice to make that possible."
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=ElUbafn77&u=005trlAagw1fap1g2bc9uj31kw11xtch )

>  “我们来自玻利维亚，我父母都是守旧派：女儿不应该离开家，直到结婚。但我19岁就离开家了，因为我受不了那种持续的斗争——关于我该如何生活的。并不是说我想滥交，我只是想探索纽约，交黑人朋友、白人朋友，还有同性恋朋友。从那儿以后我和父母的关系很糟。最终我嫁给了一个来自Corona的多米尼加男生，他全心全意对我好，但我父母从未接受他。我们在市政厅结的婚，现在我都33岁了，我们刚刚有了我们的第一个孩子。所以我以为和父母之间最终会好起来的，我以为我们可以平等了，现在我都有自己的孩子了，也许他们最终会接受我的选择，但他们仍是老样子。我工作时我母亲在帮我看孩子，一切都是按她自己的方式在做，我说什么她都批。当我坚持要以一定的方式抚养我的孩子时，她生气了，开始哭，还提醒我，说我19岁时离开了家。然后我父亲就会打电话过来，吼我，说我惹母亲生气。真让人心碎。但我意识到了：要想跟父母保持一个良好的关系，他们说什么，你就要做什么，永远都是这样。”@人在深圳 “My parents are old school. We’re from Bolivia. The daughter isn’t supposed to leave the house until she’s married. But I left when I was nineteen because I couldn’t take the constant fighting about how to live my life. It’s not that I wanted to be promiscuous. I just wanted to explore New York and have black friends and white friends and gay friends. I’ve had a bad relationship with my parents ever since. I ended up marrying a Dominican boy from Corona. He’s been nothing but good to me. But they’ve never accepted him. We got married at City Hall. I’m thirty-three now. We just had our first child. So I thought things would finally get better with my parents. I thought we could relate as equals now that I have my own child. Maybe they’d finally accept my choices. But they’re still the same. My mother helps babysit my child while I’m at work. She does everything her own way. She criticizes all my decisions. When I insist on raising my child a certain way, she gets upset. She starts crying and reminds me that I left the house when I was nineteen. Then my father calls and yells at me for upsetting my mother. It breaks my heart. But I’m realizing that a good relationship with my parents will always require doing exactly what they say.”

>  “我害怕回去工作，我刚还叫别人来着，在一大群人面前，可我就是放不下。我本该把它先搁一搁，但我必须正确。我本可以退一步，脑子里像过电影一样审视一下自己，看看周围的人是如何看我的，但不行，我就是放不下。我的医生会很生我的气的现在。我几乎都要回家了，但有个女的在站台上拉肚子，然后我就想：上帝——我都不信他那一套的——上帝在提醒我，我要回去办公室，把问题搞定。”@人在深圳 “I’m scared to go back to work. My therapist would be so upset with me right now. I almost went home, but there was a woman taking a diarrhea shit on the train platform. >  “上大学时我在一个兄弟会里，我们老是搞笑，互相吐槽。然后我就这样，从没真正停止过，老是挖苦人，总说俏皮话，只要我笑得开怀，根本不在乎别人的感情受到了伤害。我也不太注意去维持关系，好就好，不好就拉倒。但最近我得了肺癌，住院时竟没人来看我，这真是让我反思了。我不再把我的那些关系当成是理所当然，现在我说话小心多了，我不想惹任何人生气，我听得多了，我尽量去了解认识每一个肯花时间和我说话的人。”@人在深圳 “I was in a fraternity when I was in college. >  “我和我老公都在零售业做，我在34街的梅西百货做了18年了。每天早上我5:30起床，给孩子们做早餐，7:30前把他们送去学校，然后去工作6个钟，然后再带儿子去做治疗，去舞蹈练习课接闺女。我们乘19路公交到2号线，再坐到终点，通常到家是七点，这样我还有时间在九点睡觉前吃晚饭。我这么辛苦，还不是为了这些孩子。我父母来自多米尼加共和国，我父亲只读完三年级。他总是说我要完成学业，但也就是嘴上说说，作业他从未帮过我。他总是在工作，他只是不知道怎么做好。所以，我在确保一切我都有参与，开放日，家长会，还有学校所有那些重大聚会。我苦点累点，为了他们将来好点。”@人在深圳 “Both my husband and I work in retail. I’ve worked for eighteen years at the Macy’s on 34th street. I wake up at 5:30 every morning, make the kids breakfast, and get them to school by 7:30. Then I go to work for six hours, then take my son to therapy, and pick up my daughter from dance practice. We catch the nineteen bus to the two train, and ride it to the last stop. We’re normally home by seven so I have time to eat dinner before going to sleep at nine. I’m busting my hump for these kids. My parents were from the Dominican Republic. My dad only finished the third grade. He’d always tell me to finish school, but it never really went beyond words. He never helped me with my homework. He was always working and he just didn’t know any better. So I’m making sure that I’m involved with everything. I go to the open houses, the meetings, and all the school functions. I’m busting my hump so they won’t have to.”- 6/14 on Facebook

>  “任何地方养孩子都不容易，尤其是在城里。各种事情，纷至沓来，无时不刻。看这个，我们有一小片泥巴地可以玩球，但到了周末，我得化身成一个海豹特遣队员，只是为了带他去兰达尔岛参加棒球比赛。压力山大。他出生不久，我的工作开始走下坡路。第一次离婚让我刚失去一切。工作时我就没在打电话，也没人想听任何借口。那时我看谁都烦，有一天情况糟到我很用力地抓他的胳膊，那就好比一道压力的巨浪在我头顶溃掉。当时是夏天，他不听话，瞎胡闹，而那时我正在设计一段推销词，又是月底，账单就要到期，我就失去了控制。那算是个叫醒电话吧，我不得不学着划分清楚压力。现在我好些了，能面对现状好多。过去对他哥哥我要是能这样就好了。”@人在深圳 “It’s hard to raise a kid anywhere, but especially in the city. There’s just so much coming at you all the time. Look at this—we have one little dirt patch to play ball. And I have to be a navy seal just to get him to Randall’s Island on the weekend for his baseball games. It’s a lot of stress. He was born right before my job started going downhill. I’d just lost everything in my first divorce. I wasn’t hitting my numbers at work and nobody wanted to hear any excuses. I was getting pissed off at everybody. It got so bad one day that I grabbed his arm really hard. It was like a giant wave of stress just broke on top of me. It was summer and he wasn’t listening and he was acting crazy and I was trying to put together a sales pitch and it was the end of the month and bills were due and I just lost it. It was a wake up call. I had to learn to compartmentalize the stress. I’m better now. I’m a lot more present. I just wish I’d been this way with his older brother.”- 6/15 on Facebook

>  “医科有一种奇怪的文化，大家对彼此的友好比我想象的要少。我拿到了医学博士和神经学博士，马上就要完成住院实习。我原以为每个人都会有同情心，会互相帮助互相友好——别误会我，跟我一起工作的很多人都挺有同情心的，只是压力削弱了人的同情心。紧张和愤懑多了去了，我们被教导说：每周工作80小时是正常的，没什么好商量的。但同时呢，医学实习生所做的大量工作又是行政性的，它可以外包啊，又不影响教育或护理质量。真正害人的是这种文化。我有两个朋友都自杀了：一个在耶鲁学麻醉学，服药过量，死在一个停车场。另一个从纽约大学的宿舍楼纵身跳下。得有个更好的方法啊，可我也不知道，也许我这么说只是因为我压力大吧。我现在是去急诊室。我的住院实习快结束了，能看到隧道尽头了，但这隧道里头太有破坏性了。”@人在深圳 “There’s a strange culture in medicine. People are less friendly to each other than I imagined. I got an MD and a PhD in Neuroscience. I’m finishing my residency right now. I guess I thought that everyone would be compassionate, and would help each other, and would be nice to each other. And don’t get me wrong—I work with a lot of compassionate people. But the stress just erodes people. There’s a lot of tension and anger. We’re taught that 80 hours per week is normal and shouldn’t be questioned. But at the same time, a huge amount of work that medical interns do is administrative. It could be outsourced without affecting the quality of education or care. And the culture does real harm. I’ve had two friends commit suicide. One of them was studying anesthesiology at Yale and overdosed in a parking lot. The other jumped off the dorm building at NYU. There’s got to be a better way. I don’t know, maybe I’m just saying this because I’m stressed. I'm heading to the ER now. I’m almost at the end of my residency. I can see the end of the tunnel. But the tunnel is very damaging.”- 6/16 on Facebook
