>  “我来自加纳，我总是微笑，人家就问我：‘Isaac，为什么你老在笑？’ 我就告诉他们：‘不笑我还能干啥捏？’ 能到这个国家来我算是有福了。我在57街的CVS工作，做客服，我喜欢这份工作。CVS最好了，我超喜欢。我帮人们处理他们的需求，这让我很开心。我帮他们使用他们的优惠券，教他们如何用药，反正人们带着问题来，我就解决他们的问题，你可以说我是他们的好帮手。我还不是美国公民，但当我帮人们解决了他们的问题，它就使我成了大家的一员，所以我真感觉自己像个美国人了。”@人在深圳 “I come from Ghana. I’m always smiling. People ask me: ‘Isaac, why are you always smiling?' I tell them: ‘What else can I do?’ I am so blessed to be in this country. I work in customer service at the CVS on 57th Street and I love it. CVS is the best place that I love so much. I help people with their needs and it makes me so happy. I help them with their coupons. I help them with their medication. People bring me their challenges and I solve their problems. You can say that I am their champion. I am not a citizen. But when I help people with their problems, that makes me part of the community. So I do feel like an American.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EkQjFxAIp&u=005trlAagw1fah006svyuj31kw11xn3e )

>  “随着你年岁渐长，友谊是会萎缩的。除非你对友谊的定义比较宽泛——我曾经跟一个人工作过，他是费城最有钱的人之一，70岁，他可以和费城任何人共进晚餐。但那些不是我所说的朋友类型，我说的是真正懂你的人。因为我还单身，感觉这种情况在我这儿更明显。我的朋友们都结婚生子了，能腾出来的时间是越来越少，而进入他们生活的人是越来越多。但我生活中的人数量却是保持不变的。我会给他们发短信，看看他们想不想去看费城人队的比赛，总是能马上得到一个回复‘好’，但就在比赛到来之前，总会有事冒出来，他们不得不另作打算，因为‘Ethan的朋友要开生日趴’，或‘Sarah有足球比赛’。要说不感到冷落，好难哦。过去这些家伙我一周见几次，现在一年也就那么五六次。”@人在深圳 “Your friendships shrink as you get older—unless you have a loose definition of friendship. I used to work with one of the richest guys in Philadelphia. He was seventy years old. He could have dinner with anybody in the city. But those aren’t the types of friends I’m talking about. I mean the people who really know you. I think it’s amplified for me because I’m still single. My friends have gotten married and had kids. They have less and less time to give. More and more people have come into their lives. But the amount of people in my life has stayed the same. I’ll text them to see if they want to go to a Phillies game. And I always get an immediate ‘yes.’ But something always comes up right before the game. They have to reschedule because ‘Ethan’s friend is having a birthday party,’ or ‘Sarah has a soccer game.’ It’s hard to not feel left out. I used to see these guys several times a week. Now it’s five or six times per year.”- 6/19 on Facebook
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EkKWbmLS8&u=005trlAagw1fagbe9azhcj31kw11x11s )

>  “我会说12岁，通常这儿的孩子第一次单独出去，从那儿开始麻烦就来了。在外头，当你还是个生瓜蛋子的时候，没人告诉你该怎么做。我妈不让我出去，直到我14岁。我两个哥哥都进去过，所以她对我要求更加严格。出来第一年，我被逮捕四次，第二年可能也是四次。我从没去过那个岛上，但我妈妈不得不一次一次去分局领我。他们叫‘扰乱社会治安’，但几乎都是因为打架。一群从别的街区来的孩子走过去，盯着你，有人还叫嚣：‘看什么看？’ 你信不信，这就够了，就一小句话。每个人都想自豪地说他没认怂。我本可以选择不参加的，但真的很难避免。想象一下，如果你周围有一百个人抽烟，十次有九次，你也会抽的。”@人在深圳 “I’d say twelve is the normal age when a kid around here comes outside alone for the first time. That’s when the trouble starts. When you’re fresh outside and nobody’s telling you what to do. My mom kept me inside until I was fourteen. Both my brothers had been to juvenile, so she was more strict with me. I got arrested four times that first year. Probably four times the next year too. I never went to The Island, but my mom kept having to pick me up from the precinct. They called it ‘Disorderly Conduct,’ but it was almost always for fighting. A group of kids would walk by from another block, and they’re staring, and somebody yells out: ‘What are you looking at?’ And believe it or not-- that’s all it takes. One little sentence. Everybody wants the pride of saying they didn’t back down. I could have chosen not to participate. But it’s hard to avoid. Imagine if one hundred people around you are smoking cigarettes. Nine times out of ten, you’re going to start smoking.”- 6/21 on Facebook
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EkKHe9kEb&u=005trlAagw1fagb8n5xv2j31kw11xaed )

>  “每周我有一块钱零用钱，然后我就得选，看把我的钱放在哪一项里面，有四项呢：花掉，存起来，捐赠和投资。如果我在‘投资’里放一块钱，爸爸妈妈每个月底就会额外给我两分钱。‘花掉’我只使用过两次！‘投资’那一项里我有超过10美元，过去比这还多！但我拿出一些钱放在‘捐赠’里了，我们用它来买吃的，给那些在他们的‘花掉’那一项里没太多钱的人。”@人在深圳 “Every week I get one dollar for allowance. Then I get to choose the section where I put my dollar. There are four sections: spend, save, donate, and invest. If I put a dollar in the ‘invest section,' my parents give me two extra pennies at the end of every month. I’ve only used my 'spend section' twice! I have way over $10 in my 'invest section.' I used to have more but I took some money out and put it in my 'donate section.' We used it to buy food for people who don’t have much money in their 'spend section.'”- 6/20, Facebook

>  “姥姥去年母亲节前去世的。姥姥在佐治亚州长大，童年大都是在棉花地里干活儿，七年级后辍学，和家人搬到北方，开始在一家钮扣厂工作。我妈妈是她唯一的孩子，生我妈妈时她们母女差点都死掉。姥姥独自一人抚养妈妈，我们出生后，她也帮着抚养我们。我的朋友都叫她Diva Miss Eva，她会摇下她的Oldsmobile汽车车窗，提醒别人提裤子。她喜欢粉红色。这张照片是我妈妈社区大学毕业那天拍的，当时是六月中，天儿那叫一个热，但姥姥出来时，身穿粉红色晚礼服，披着貂儿，戴着晚礼服手套。我们说她，天儿太热，但她说：‘我的宝贝毕业哎！’ 她喜欢这张照片，把它放进相框，挂在床头——粉红色的床奥，在她粉红色的房间里。”@人在深圳 “Gram died right before Mother’s Day last year. She grew up in Georgia and spent most of her childhood working in the cotton fields. She dropped out of school after seventh grade. She moved North with her family and started working in a button factory. My mom was her only child. They both almost died during childbirth. Gram raised Mom all by herself, and after we were born, she helped raise us too. My friends called her Diva Miss Eva. She’d roll down the window of her Oldsmobile to tell people to pull up their pants. And she loved pink. We took this picture on the day my mom graduated from community college. It was in the middle of June. It was so hot. But Gram comes outside in a pink evening gown, mink fur, and evening gloves. We told her it was too hot but she said: ‘My baby’s graduating!’ She loved this photo. She put it in a frame and hung it above her pink bed. In her pink room.”- 6/22, Facebook
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EkGSOwlnv&u=005trlAagw1faftmleaiyj31kw11xtcr )

>  “三十周年纪念日前一周她自杀的，在那早几年我们大女儿死于白血病，而Holly很难接受它。我们的关系都因此而疏远了，说话都得注意措词，一切都变得不再自然：‘这样说话对吗？’ ‘此刻该笑吗？’ ‘我们还有权利笑吗？’ 但我仍然认为我们做得还OK，过去不再了，但我仍然认为都还OK。我们在酒店开个间房，为了我们的三十周年纪念日，下班后我本该在那儿跟她会合，但我还没到，她服了过量的药。我不知道她为什么要这样做，她在她的本子上说她不生气，但我不知道她为什么要这样做。我崩溃了，开始酗酒和吸可卡因。我丢了工作——有一天，在药效作用下过了一整夜后，我在做一个报告，我产生了幻觉，以为一个客户是Holly，就停下来叫她的名字。这家公司很好，他们给了我很好的遣散费，但我把那些钱都给了我的孩子们。从那儿开始我就一直流落街头，八年了已经。孩子们想把钱给回我，但我不会要的。我晚上乘地铁，如果够暖和，就在长椅上睡。我看点东西，也写点东西。我早上会去排队领点救济。我只是活着而已。我不是个好丈夫，不是个好父亲，现在我是在赎罪。”@人在深圳 “She committed suicide a week prior to our thirtieth anniversary. Our oldest daughter had died of leukemia a couple years earlier. Holly took it extra hard. We drifted apart. We’d parse our words. Nothing was natural anymore: ‘Do we talk this way?’ ‘Do we laugh at this moment?’ ‘ Do we even have a right to laugh?’ But I still thought we were doing OK. Things weren’t like they used to be. But I still thought things were OK. We rented a hotel room for our thirtieth anniversary. I was supposed to meet her there after work. She overdosed on pills before I got there. I don’t know why she did it that way. She said in her note that she wasn’t angry, but I don’t know why she did it that way. I fell apart. I started drinking a lot and doing cocaine. I lost my job. One day I was giving a presentation after being up all night on drugs, and I just started hallucinating. I thought one of the clients was Holly. I stopped the presentation and started calling her name. The company was nice about it. They gave me a nice severance package. But I gave all the money to my kids. I’ve been on the streets ever since. It’s been eight years. My kids have tried to give me the money back but I won’t take it. I ride the subways at night. If it’s warm enough, I sleep on a bench. I read a little. I write a little. I go to the soup line in the morning. I’m just existing. I wasn’t a good husband. I wasn’t a good father. And now I’m doing penance.”- 6/24, Facebook
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EkGCV4hyc&u=005trlAagw1fafs0gmstwj31kw11xn1u )

>  “六年了，我和我老公一直在努力想收养一个寄养中的孩子，过程之难，不可思议。人们选择从国外收养是有原因的。现在我在等我儿子，等他演完芭蕾舞。他来自危地马拉的一家孤儿院，你能想象如果我们没收养他，他的生活会有多不一样么？所以这一次我们想在美国收养。五年来我们询问了530个，好几次都到了最后一轮，但每一次我们都没有被选中。有一次还是收养兄弟姐妹五个，最后我们好像都沾边了，和他们花了那么多时间，已经建立了亲密关系，但在最后一刻，高层管理者把我们否决了。没有理由，他认为我们‘不好不合适’，真让人崩溃。我还留着他们的照片呢。我们是好父母哦，我们六个孩子都成年了，两个还和我们住在一起，他们每一个都不错，没道理我们不能收养啊。可就因为这些官僚机构，负担过重，又资金不足，一切进展得如此缓慢。这些孩子们没钱，所以他们的声音也发不出来。我在Facebook上的一个互助小组里，那里面都是像我这种情况的，每个人都备受折磨，被那些匹配不上的原因：太老了，太多孩子了，孩子少了，钱不够。各种猜测，无止无休。与此同时，这个国家有10万个孩子在等待着一个家庭来收养。”小编@人在深圳 “My husband and I have been trying to adopt a child from foster care for six years. The process is unbelievably difficult. There’s a reason people choose to adopt from foreign countries. Right now I’m waiting on my son to finish his ballet performance. He came from an orphanage in Guatemala. Can you imagine how different his life would be if we hadn’t adopted him? So this time we tried to adopt in America. We’ve inquired on 530 cases in five years. We’ve reached the final round several times, but each time we’re not chosen. Once it seemed like we were finally on the brink of adopting five siblings. We spent so much time with them. We were bonded with them. But at the last moment, the top administrator vetoed our case. No reason was given. He thought we ‘weren’t a good fit.’ We were devastated. I still have their pictures. We’re good parents. We have six grown children and two who still live with us. Everyone is doing well. There’s no reason we shouldn’t be able to adopt. Everything moves so slowly because the bureaucracy is overloaded and underfunded. These kids have no money so they have no voice. I’m in a support group on Facebook full of people like me. Everyone is agonizing over the reasons that they aren’t being matched: too old, too many children, not enough children, not enough money. The guesses are endless. In the meantime there are 100,000 kids in this country who are waiting for a family.”- posted on 6/23
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ekqa3fChi&u=005trlAagw1fadr1qxa1wj31kw11xafb )

>  “我是在那些廉租房里中长大的，早早就涉毒。17岁时我愚蠢地搞了次抢劫，后被作为成年人起诉。20岁出狱，我找了份最低工资的工作干了一段时间，然后我在做成衣的那个片区发现一家韩国人开的店，他们做假冒服装，任何我想要的标签，他们都能弄上去。牛仔裤，进价15刀，运到哈莱姆区，拿去台球室，卖给那些牙买加人和多米尼加人，25刀。准确说这不合法，我清楚，但我终于感觉自己在做正当营生了，尤其是和过去相比。我努力工作，一切都好。头一年我大概卖了有两千条牛仔裤，但圣诞前三天，我被抢劫了。三个孩子偷袭了我。我在外干了一整天活儿，精疲力尽，手指冰凉，我不想把钱交出去，他们就朝我肚子上开枪。我气疯了，倍感冒犯。我的血汗钱，他们就那样拿走了。我都能感觉到过去的我又回来了，我想杀了他们。出院后我去找他们，带着结肠镜袋走街串巷。我差点就要被拉回到我的过去了。但最终当愤怒平息，我又回去工作了。我甚至不再做假冒服装的生意，而是卖自己设计的东西。我不想回监狱。监狱虽没纠正我，但它确实抑制了我。过去的我一直还在那儿，只是一点点，当我感到绝望时，当我为自己仍没能力让我妈妈搬出那些廉租房而感到恼怒时。但我始终抑制住了过去的自己。我见过太多的人就那样在监狱里过活，我不能成为他们那样，我热爱生活太多。我还想将来有一天去蹦极，我还想去钓鱼。”小编@人在深圳 “I grew up in the projects and got involved in drugs early. I committed a stupid ass robbery when I was seventeen and ended up being charged as an adult. I got out of prison when I was twenty. I worked a minimum wage job for awhile, then I found a Korean shop in the garment district that was making counterfeit clothes. They would put any label I wanted on them. I could buy jeans for $15 and bring them up to Harlem, and I’d go to the pool hall and sell them to the Jamaicans and Dominicans for $25. I know it wasn’t exactly legal. But I finally felt like I was making an honest living. Especially compared to my past. I was working hard. Things were going well. I probably sold two thousand jeans that first year. But three days before Christmas I got robbed. Three kids ambushed me. I’d been out working all day. I was tired. My fingers were cold. And I didn’t want to hand over the money. So they shot me in the stomach. I was so angry. I felt so violated. I’d made that money by working hard and they’d taken it from me. I could feel the old Gerald coming back. I wanted to kill them. I went looking for them after I got out of the hospital. I walked the streets with my colonoscopy bag. I was so close to being pulled back to my past. But eventually the anger subsided and I went back to work. I even stopped with the counterfeit clothes and sold my own designs. I didn’t want to go back to prison. Prison didn’t correct me, but it did check me. The old Gerald is always there. Just a little bit. Like when I’m feeling desperate and I’m mad that I still can’t afford to get my mom out of the projects. But I always keep him in check. I saw too many guys in prison who were there for life. And I love life too much to be them. I want to go bungee jumping one day. I want to go fishing.”- posted on 6/28
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EkpzSv4HP&u=005trlAagw1fadps6vbssj31kw11xdjo )

>  “在这儿要想得到你应得的，你就不能客气。我学到这招也是不容易。刚来时我还是那种小岛思维，因为在波多黎各，你能得到的，你只管取。要是别人看你不容易，他们也会帮助你。不像在这儿，你好好做生意，人们会踩你，直到你做不下去。刚开始卖咖啡我们是在街市上，租个摊儿那管事的一天要收600刀，而一天你根本卖不了那么多咖啡。他们知道我们在赔钱，也知道我们不好过，但他们说他们也无能为力，嫌贵也没用。然后我们了解到我们旁边的摊才300刀，我们威胁说我们不租了，他们才把租金降到125刀。一开始他们说的可是再低也低不了了！真让人无语。管事的压根儿不在乎价格公不公平，他们只关心自己的利益最大化。反正在这儿你不能等着别人施舍，如果你想得到什么，你得明说。”小编@人在深圳 “You can’t be humble about what you deserve in this city. I had to learn that the hard way. I came here with a small island mentality. In Puerto Rico, you take what you can get, and if someone sees that you are struggling, they will help you. Not here. If you are running a business, people will step on you until you break. We first started selling coffee at street fairs. The organizers were charging us $600 per day to rent a spot. It was impossible to sell that much coffee. They knew we were losing money. They knew we were suffering. But they told us there was nothing they could do—that was the fee. Then we learned that the people next to us were paying $300. When we threatened to leave, they lowered our rent to $125. And at first they told us they couldn’t go any lower! That’s what I mean. The organizers didn’t care what was a fair price. They cared about getting the biggest share they could. You can’t wait to be given anything in this city. If you want something, you have to demand it by its name.”- posted on 6/29
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EkoAy4Yde&u=005trlAagw1fadknnezofj31kw11xk03 )

>  “我们在一起20年了，我再没约会过其他任何人。但我们之间并没亲密感，手上没戒指，他甚至都不想让他家人知道我们在一起。也许是因为我的体重，也许是身份的缘故，他就是让我避开他的家人。有次篮球比赛，我不小心坐在他妹旁边，他下巴都快掉地上了。我们只做过一次爱，那还是12年前。他不会吻我或摸我，我刚不再问了，但他坚持说我们是在相处。我想把我的情感状态变成‘单身’，他抓狂了，到我电脑上又把它改了回来。我都不知道他居然知道我的密码。我跟自己说OK就这样吧，他不碰我也没关系，但我并不认为我OK。最近我去看了个理疗师，平生第一次。我好害怕，害怕他发现我把车停在隔壁。但也许他发现了倒好，也许他会离开我，给我一个机会。”小编@人在深圳 “We’ve been together for twenty years. I’ve never dated anyone else. But there’s no intimacy. There’s no ring on the finger. He doesn’t even want his family to know we’re together. Maybe it’s my weight. Maybe it’s a status thing. But he keeps me away from his family. I accidentally sat by his sister at a basketball game, and his jaw nearly dropped to the floor. We’ve only made love once. That was twelve years ago. He won’t kiss me or touch me. I’ve just stopped asking. But he insists that we’re in a relationship. He got mad when I tried to change my relationship status to ‘single.’ He got on my computer and changed it back. I didn’t even know that he knew my password. I told myself that I was OK with it. I told myself that I’m OK with not being touched. But I don’t think I am. I recently went to a therapist for the first time. I was so scared he’d find out that I parked my car next door. But maybe it would be good if he found out. Maybe he’d leave me and give me a chance.”

>  “成千上万的人跟我一样，每次去赛马场都能看到他们。这些可悲的混蛋，他们所有人，总想着再捞一大把，却永远都捞不到，总是紧张和沮丧，真是个很坏的瘾。我从不喝酒，也不嗑药，我就是停不了赌博。我在几千匹马身上下过注，赢的越多，赌注就越大，直到你再次输得精光。每天，都是这样。每天早上我都在凑钱，好坐上地铁，去赛马场。我的工作也不怎么样，就是在街上卖点东西：衬衫、皮带、T恤、毛衣，一卖卖了五十年。很多时候我都没地儿住。但至少我从没犯过罪，我知道很多人都犯过，那特么才是祸害。”小编@人在深圳 “There are thousands of people like me. I saw them every time I went to the racetrack. Miserable motherfuckers, all of them. Always looking for the next big score that never comes. Always nervous and depressed. It’s a very bad addiction. I never drank. I never did any drugs. But I couldn’t stop gambling. I bet on thousands of horses in my life. The more you win, the more you bet, until you lose it all again. It was the same routine everyday. I spent every morning looking for enough money to get on the subway and get to the racetrack. I did menial jobs. I sold things on the streets: shirts, belts, t-shirts, sweaters. For fifty years I did this. A lot of times I didn’t have a place to live. At least I never committed any crimes. I know a lot of guys who did. It’s a real fucking curse.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ek8Lfs7DB&u=005trlAagw1fabmsnqprij31kw11xq7n )

>  “没想到我们还要抚养孙女，过去我们谈论的是退休后搬到乡下去住，而现在我们谈论的是搬到最好的学区。现在我是尽量多工作，我每天都在担心她长大之前我们会发生什么。我去健身房多了，要努力保持身体健康。为了她上大学，我还参保了一个专门的储蓄计划，从她出生那天起，我就一直在投钱进去。因为如果我发生了什么不测，那钱是要翻一番的。”小编@人在深圳 “We didn’t expect to be raising our granddaughter. We used to talk about moving to the country when we retired. Now we talk about moving to the best school districts. I’m working as much as I can. I worry every day that something will happen to us before she’s grown. I’m going to the gym more. I’m trying to stay healthy. I’m enrolled in a special savings program for her college education. I’ve been adding money to it since the day she was born. Because if something happens to me, the amount doubles.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ek5gkqN5h&u=005trlAagw1fab88sth5uj31kw11xgt1 )

>  “我在郊区长大的，我曾以为我能给一个穷人指条出路：‘找份工作，钱省着点花，自力更生。’ 但我不信那一套了，过去我对穷人的遭遇竟一无所知。我想请任何人到这儿来，来看看这儿的人吧。现在我们周围都是工作着的穷人，这些人是在西尔斯卖给你工具、给你修房顶、帮你照顾父母、帮你割草坪、伺候你吃饭的人。可他们的工资并不足以维持生活，也存不了钱。他们一生病，或者车坏了，就什么都没了。上帝不允许他们犯错，因为他们没有任何剩余可以让他们去付那些罚款或费用。你在这儿跌倒了，这套体制会继续往你脸上踢污垢。你也振作不起来，当你没有任何可以抓住的东西。我们付给我们的兄弟姐妹的不足以让他们维持生活，我们希望他们为我们服务，但我们却不为他们服务。”小编@人在深圳 “I grew up in the suburbs. I used to think that I could write a prescription for a poor man: ‘Get a job, save your money, pull yourself up by the bootstraps.’ I don’t believe that anymore. I was ignorant to the experiences of poor people. I’d invite anyone to come and meet the people who live in this neighborhood. Right now we are surrounded by working poor people. These are the people who sell your tools at Sears, and fix your roofs, and take care of your parents, and mow your lawns, and serve your meals. They’re not getting a living wage. There’s no money left to save. There’s nothing left if they get sick. Nothing left if their car breaks down. And God forbid they make a mistake, because there’s nothing left to pay fines or fees. When you’re down here, the system will continue to kick dirt in your face. You can’t pull yourself up when there’s nothing to grab onto. We aren’t paying our brothers and sisters enough to live. We want them to serve us, but we aren’t serving them.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ek4XVfwuG&u=005trlAagw1fab63baasyj31kw11xgtw )

>  “所有老板关心的都是完成工作，所以如果你够敬业，会有更多活儿落在你头上。老板们都门儿清：让一个好工人多干活儿，比找一个烂工人来做容易得多。这样阻力最小，尤其是当老板跟烂工人是哥们儿的时候。过去这搞得我很烦，我受不了它的不公，但我不得不学会由它去吧。过去我会把压力带回家，一点小事就会让我生气，我会‘砰’一声关抽屉。我甚至在梦里发飙，其实我并不喜欢暴力，但我做过那样的梦：老板挑剔我的工作，我一把掐住他脖子。所以我得学会由它去吧。过去我是真心在乎这份工作，但我得开始把它当成一份薪水就好了。”小编@人在深圳 “All the bosses care about is getting the job done. So if you have a good work ethic, the work falls on you more. The bosses know that it’s easier to push a good worker than it is to get a bad worker to do their job. It’s the path of least resistance. Especially when the boss happens to be friends with the bad workers. It used to really bother me. I couldn’t stand the injustice of it. But I’ve had to learn to let it go. I was bringing the stress home with me. I’d get mad at little things and slam drawers. I was even having rage dreams. I abhor violence, but I was having dreams where the boss would criticize my work and my hands would go around his neck. So I had to learn to let it go. I used to really care about the job. But I’ve had to just start viewing it as a paycheck.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EjVJAu93B&u=005trlAagw1faa1l85xsqj31kw11xn0t )

>  “我90岁的老母亲刚搬来和我们一起住，所以我成了一个全职的看护。她只有我了，我父亲过世了，我是她唯一的子女，所以只能靠我了。她现在人很消极，似乎老是盯着事情的负面。我说出去，她说天太冷。我说去买点东西，她说路太堵。她想要独立自主，但当她有了，她又觉得孤独。好难哦。我本是个积极的人，这么多负能量好难对付。我老公也在担心我，他也觉得负能量太多，疲于应付。我有家有口，有自己的生活，还有事情要做。但如果我把她交给别人照顾，我怕更糟，我得确保她得到了适当的照顾。因为她的消极悲观，过去她总是教我们要尊重，尊重你的玩具，尊重你的父母，尊重别人，尊重别人的东西。尊重是一切的基础，没有它，一切都完了。”小编@人在深圳 “My ninety-year-old mother just moved in with us. So I’ve become a full time caretaker. I’m all she’s got. My father passed away and I’m her only child. So I’m it. Right now she has a lot of negativity. She seems to fixate on the negative side of things. If I suggest going outside, she’ll say it’s too cold. If I suggest that we go shopping, she’ll say there’s too much traffic. She wants her independence, but when she has it, she gets lonely. It’s hard for me. Because I’m a positive person by nature. And it’s hard to deal with so much negative energy. My husband is worried about me. He thinks it’s too much to deal with. I have a family, a life, and a business. But I’d be even more of a wreck if I put her in assisted living. I need to know for sure that she’s getting the proper care. Because for all her negativity, my mother always taught us respect. Respect your toys. Respect your parents. Respect other people. Respect their property. Respect is the basis for everything. Without it, everything falls apart."
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EjVyUBepa&u=005trlAagw1faa0c4vi39j31kw11x0yw )

>  “我是一个遗嘱见证律师，代理那些对父母的遗愿有异议的人。我想写一本书，关于我所看到的一切。它还不完全到《黑道家族》那一步，但已经接近了。我同事喜欢说：有争议的遗嘱是一个非常家庭的最后战场。从童年开始的一切都会浮出水面，你会惊讶于人们能怀恨在心多久。而遗嘱检验法庭是他们报复的最后一次机会，因为‘妈妈爱你更多’。疯狂的是多少客户宁愿要正确，也不要快乐。它几乎总是能以最聪明的方式解决，但相比握手言和，通过斗争的方式解决，双方的付出都更多。然而，人们仍然会选择花费所有的时间和金钱，就只为了从法院得到一个判决，证明最后一次他们是正确的。”小编@人在深圳 “I’m a probate lawyer. I represent people who contest their parents' wills. I want to write a book about all the things I’ve seen. It’s not quite The Soprano’s, but it’s close. My colleague likes to say that contested wills are the final battleground of a dysfunctional family. Everything from childhood gets brought to the surface. You’d be amazed how long people can hold grudges. And probate court is their last chance to get revenge for ‘Mom loving you more.’ The crazy thing is how many clients would rather be right than be happy. It’s almost always smartest to settle. It costs both sides more to fight it out than to make a deal. Yet people still choose to spend all their time and money, just to get a judgment from the court that will prove they’re right one final time.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EjPO1wyZ0&u=005trlAagw1fa9b22hgegj31kw11xwmp )

>  “我们是世界上最可怕的恐怖分子，这是长期形成的结果。这整个国家都是建立在对无辜者的屠杀之上，我们得到了应得的报应。看看美国参与中东的历史吧，所有那些国家都是人为的。奥斯曼帝国垮台后，我们就像造塑料一样，造了那些国家。而要统治一个‘塑料’国家，唯一的方法就是联合一个独裁者，阿萨德，侯赛因，还有沙阿，是我们一手扶持的。几十年的折磨、谋杀和压迫，是我们资助的。只要一有机会我就会说。有人威胁要杀了我，有人威胁要强暴我的孩子，但我会继续说下去。你可以认为我是个怪物——我认为世贸双塔中的那些人是我们的代表，他们因我们反人类的罪行而死。我不仅认为9/11是活该，我还认为它是人类历史上最伟大的事件之一。”小编@人在深圳 “We’re the worst terrorists in the world and it was a long time coming. We created those countries like plastic after the fall of the Ottoman Empire. And the only way to rule a plastic country is with a dictator. Assad, Hussein, the Shah—we propped them all up. Decades of torture, murder, and oppression. We sponsored it. So I say it whenever I can. I’ve had people threaten to kill me. I’ve had people threaten to rape my children. But I’ll keep saying it. You can call me a monster. I think the people in those towers died as representatives for the rest of us for our crimes against humanity. Not only do I think that 9/11 was deserved. I think it was one of the greatest events in human history."

>  “我们都知道，这张照片会成为一张标志性的照片。将来有一天，人们会研究来研究去：‘这老兄太帅了，就那样站在拐角，拿着奥巴马同款手机，戴着150刀的手表。’ 我们也很清楚：要不是我这么挺，永远也不会有这张照片。托Bradley先生的福，你就要成名了。现在我也无所谓了，白人、黑人，哪怕是紫人，谁发财我都无所谓了。啥时候这张照片卖到1000万，你回来找我，我要分十分之一。”小编@人在深圳 “We both know this could become one of those iconic photos. This could be one of those photos that they study one day: ‘Pretty Handsome Brother On The Corner With Obama Phone and $150 Watch.’ And we both know that if I wasn’t so statuesque, this photo never would have happened. You are about to get famous off Mr. Bradley. Now I don’t mind. I don’t mind if white, black, or purple people prosper. But when this picture sells for $10 million, you come back and find me. Cause I’m gonna need one-tenth of that.”

>  “我来自一个小国家，加蓬，它曾经是非洲的瑞士——只有150万人，某些石油储量也是世界最大，铁矿供应世界前十大，还有铀、锰，要什么有什么，还有最美丽的热带雨林。这个国家是如此富有，但人民却是如此贫穷：没有干净的水；人们的生活取决于如何能找到吃的；也没有教育；多数青少年都有艾滋病。你要是在加蓬生了病，那你死定了。现在我就起了鸡皮疙瘩，因为我妈妈还生活在那儿呢。人们在死亡线上挣扎，但统治家族却坐着私人飞机上飞来飞去。他们在联合国发表演讲，然后人们鼓掌。总统夫人提的手袋就值25000刀。统治家族已经执政50年，每一分钟他们都变得越来越有钱。你知道他们为什么能掌权？你知道他们为什么这么有钱？因为他们把我们的自然资源拱手送给了法国人。”小编@人在深圳 “I come from the small country of Gabon. It used to be the Switzerland of Africa. There are only 1.5 million people there. It has some of the largest oil reserves in the world. It is top ten in iron supplies, uranium supplies, manganese supplies—you name it. And it has the most beautiful rainforest. The country is so wealthy but the people are so poor. There is no clean water. People’s lives are defined by the search for bread. There is no education. And most teenagers have HIV. And when you get sick in Gabon, you die. I have goose bumps right now because my mother still lives there. The people are dying, yet the ruling family flies around in private jets. They give speeches at the UN and people clap. The president’s wife wears handbags that cost $25,000. The ruling family has been in power for 50 years and they get richer and richer every minute. And do you know why they’re in power? Do you know why they’re so rich? Because they hand over our natural resources to the French.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EjOlfAWS0&u=005trlAagw1fa94ia90g5j31kw11x43p )

>  “车臣战争时我还在法学院，记得看一则新闻：一个男孩走上去求一个记者，寻求帮助，希望能唤醒他爷爷，他爷爷刚被炸弹炸死。正是那时，我决定成为一名人权律师。我去了联合国工作，想象着自己起草更强大的人权法，还想着我会会见国家元首，说服他们建立更好的法律和社会机构。那些会见确实有，我也做了研究，并且做了报告。你应该看到过我，我是那么充满激情和自信，对自己的论断确信无疑。那些领导人会点头，然后说：‘很感谢你。’ 但之后什么都不会改变，除非有经济利益，没有人会关心保护孩子、或授权给妇女、或停止种族屠杀。它消磨着我的斗志，我同事也是，十年后，我不得不放弃。上周我开了这个酒吧，这不是人权，但至少现在我有免费的酒喝了。”小编@人在深圳 “The War In Chechnya was going on during the time I was in law school. I remember watching a news report where a young boy walked up to a journalist and asked for help waking up his grandfather. The grandfather had just been killed by a bomb. I decided then that I’d be a human rights lawyer. I went to work at the United Nations. I pictured myself drafting stronger human rights laws. I thought I’d meet with heads of state and convince them to form better laws and better institutions. And those meetings did happen. I did my research and made my presentations. You should have seen me— I was so passionate and confident and sure of my reasoning. The leaders would nod their heads, and say ‘thank you very much,’ but then nothing would change. Unless there was an economic benefit, nobody cared about protecting children, or empowering women, or stopping genocide. And it wore me down. My colleagues were worn down too. After ten years I had to quit. Last week I opened this bar. It’s not human rights, but at least now I can drink for free.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EjO3UBDs3&u=005trlAagw1fa93l0ztuaj31kw11x0x7 )

>  “五年来我头回回家，本来只是来看望一下妈妈，我还想着妈妈会来机场接我呢，但落地后发现是我嫂子。她说我妈在医院里，内出血，腿上还有个血凝块。我们刚一到那儿，两名外科医生让我坐下来，告诉我他们需要马上有一个决定。他们已经给我妈输了十一单位的血，他们要锯掉她的腿，还要给她弄一个结肠镜袋。一开始我还问我们能做什么，但后来我告诉他们去做吧。我觉得我做了个错误的决定。现在我妈正在恢复中，益发明显的是，她的基本生活都将永远无法自理了。我了解我妈妈，她是个非常独立的女人，她自己耙落叶，自己吹车道上的雪。她不会想这样活着。她决不会这样跟我说，但我想她觉得我让她失望了。”小编@人在深圳 “This was supposed to be a regular “hi mom” visit. It was my first time coming home in five years. I was expecting my mother to pick me up from the airport, but my sister-in-law was there when I landed. She told me that my mother was in the hospital. She was bleeding internally and had a blood clot in her leg. Right after we arrived, two surgeons sat me down, and told me they needed a decision immediately. They’d given my mother eleven units of blood and they wanted to amputate her leg and give her a colonoscopy bag. At first I asked if we could do nothing. But then I told them to go ahead and do it. And I think I made the wrong decision. She’s recovering now, and it’s becoming apparent that she’ll never be able to do basic things by herself. And I know my mother. She’s a very independent woman. She rakes her own leaves and blows the snow off her own driveway. She wouldn’t want to live like this. She’d never say this to me, but I think she feels that I let her down.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EjMbHB0n0&u=005trlAagw1fa8v4snvm4j31kw11x7i2 )

>  “12岁起我就靠自己了，我妈妈觉得她的毒贩男友比我更重要。一天晚上我玩完回家，钥匙转不动了，敲门也没人应。接下来几年我就跟朋友们一起住，一家又一家，一个沙发又一个沙发。我朋友的妈妈是个酒保，她给我找了份工作洗碗碟。16岁，我攒够钱买了辆车，开去了亚利桑那。21岁，我怀孕了。我儿子改变了我的生活。我不是一夜之间就变成特蕾莎修女的，我得忘掉过去学的每一样东西，然后学着如何用正确的方式做事情，不卖毒品，也不抄近道儿。现在，作为一个单身妈妈，我正努力完成大学学业，我在照顾83岁的奶奶，我刚打败癌症，过去四年这是第二次。但现在仿佛一切归于平静了，不过我总是屏着呼吸——我的人生经历就像是暴风雨前的平静呢。”小编@人在深圳 “I’ve been on my own since the age of twelve. My mom decided that her drug-dealing boyfriend was more important than me. One night I came home from playing and the key wouldn’t turn. I started banging on the door but nobody answered. I lived with friends for the next few years. I went from house to house, couch to couch. My friend’s mom was a bartender so she got me a job washing dishes. I saved enough money to get a car when I turned sixteen, and I drove out to Arizona. I was pregnant by the time I was twenty-one. My son changed my life. I didn’t turn into Mother Theresa overnight. I had to unlearn everything I’d ever known. I had to learn how to do things the right way, not sell drugs, not cut corners. Right now I’m trying to finish college while being a single mother. I’m taking care of my eighty-three year old grandmother. I just beat cancer for the second time in four years. But things seem to be quiet now. I’m always holding my breath, though. The story of my life has been the calm before the storm.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EjE161ye1&u=005trlAagw1fa7uwgjzj6j31kw11xtdj )

>  “我13岁时奶奶送给我一把小提琴。那时候每当人们打架，我就想离开，回到我的房间拉小提琴。有时候我一拉拉四五个小时一晚上，它给了我很大的自信，我开始在教堂前拉，在学校前面拉，感觉自己棒棒的。但我妈事儿多，她没少犯错，她陷入一些糟糕的关系当中，我们在很多不同的地方住过，有时候几周连电都没有。有一次简直糟透了，我们不得不卖我们的东西。她没让我卖我的小提琴，但我们的电视已经卖了，然后她问我你有啥想法，最后，145刀，我把小提琴卖给了一个朋友。那段时间我真的好难过，我是个基督徒，上帝知道我有多爱那把小提琴，那他为什么还让我把它卖了呢？我都被搞糊涂了当时。有几个月我仍坚持在学校的音乐室里拉小提琴，但最终不得不放弃，为了专心付账单——我在一间杂货店找到一份正式工作。”小编@人在深圳 “My grandmother got me a violin when I was thirteen. Whenever people were fighting, and I wanted to get away, I’d just go in my room and play. Sometimes I’d play for four or five hours per night. It gave me a lot of confidence. I started playing in front of the church, in front of the school--- it made me feel good about myself. But my mom struggled a lot. She made a lot of mistakes. She got in some bad relationships and we lived in a lot of different places. Sometimes we’d go weeks without having power. One time it got really bad and we had to start selling our stuff. She didn’t ask me to sell my violin. But we’d already sold our TV. And she just asked if I had any ideas. I ended up selling it to a friend for $145. I was really upset for a while. I’m a Christian, and God knew how much I loved the violin. So I was confused why he’d make me sell it. For a few months, I tried to keep playing in the music room at school. But eventually I had to stop so I could focus on paying the bills. I got a real job at the grocery store.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EjCSyrJiN&u=005trlAagw1fa7q2rqzcjj31kw11xqen )

>  “我这辈子收养过13个小婴儿，就是这么个心性，热心肠。通常他们都是裹在毯子里送来的，我一次只能养一个，因为我自己还有五个孩子呢。但有一次一个母亲丢下三个孩子在我家门口，她刚喂过他们巧克力冰淇淋，我永远都忘不了那冰淇淋是如何从他们脸上往下滴的。大多数情况下孩子只会在我这儿几个月，一旦他们被人家收养了，我就再也不跟他们联系了。但我老想知道他们怎么样，也许我们会在天堂重逢呢。”小编@人在深圳 “I fostered thirteen little babies in my life. It’s just a passion I have in my heart. Often they’d just come wrapped in a blanket. I could only foster one at a time because I had five children of my own. But one time a mother dropped three children off on my doorstep. She had just given them chocolate ice cream. I’ll never forget how the ice cream was dripping off their faces. Most of the time I’d only have the children for a few months. And once they were adopted, I’d never contact them again. But I often wonder what happened to them. Maybe we’ll meet again in heaven.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ejm3ZxmgW&u=005trlAagw1fa5o963mubj31kw11xjw7 )

>  (3/3)“我想念那些时光，我们能出去、跳舞，或访问人。过去我们每周三都在老年活动中心做志愿者，她弹钢琴，我给她翻页。她能记得的就有那些圣歌，音乐是她的命呢。但有一天她弹不了了，我告诉工作人员他们要找别人了。所以，现在我们就待在这儿了。但我不认为这是个灾祸，这是福，不是祸，这是上帝交给我做的。她为了这个家操劳一生，现在也该我来为她操劳操劳了。我可能没她的那股心性，但我有她啊。我仍能逗她笑，我能发出欢快的声音，朝着她吹气，她就会笑。每天早上我们会坐在这张椅子上，依偎着到中午。我摇她可比摇孙子们还多呢。她喜欢把她的手滑到我的衬衫下摸我的皮肤，她还喜欢亲吻呢，过一会儿她就会伸起身给我一个吻。有时她开始唠叨，也没说什么实际的话，都是些没意义的话，但我从不说要她保持安静，因为那比什么都没有可好多了。”小编@人在深圳 (3/3) “I miss that we can’t go out and dance. Or visit other people. We used to volunteer at the senior center every Wednesday. She’d play the piano, and I’d turn the pages for her. The hymns were some of the last things she remembered. Music was her life. But one day she wouldn’t play anymore. And I told the staff that they’d need to find someone else. So we stay here now. But I don’t see this as a curse. It’s an honor. This is what the Lord has given me to do. She has served this family her entire life. And now it’s my turn to serve her. I might not have her mentally. But I have her. I can still make her smile. I can make bubbly noises, and blow on her, and she’ll smile. Every morning we’ll sit in this chair and we’ll cuddle until noon. I rock this lady more than I rock my grandchildren. She likes to slip her hand under my shirt to feel my skin. And she still likes to kiss. Every once in awhile she’ll reach up and give me a kiss. Sometimes she starts ‘yakking.’ She doesn’t say actual words. And it doesn't make any sense. But I never tell her to be quiet, because it’s better than nothing at all.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiII0227o&u=005trlAagw1fa0tovgno5j31kw11xdnb )

>  (2/3)“我们结婚50周年纪念日是在密苏里州的布兰森庆祝的。开车回家的路上，她不停地说我们走错路了，很坚持，但我也没反驳她，只是不停地让她转向，因为我知道我们最终会回到回密歇根的主路上。正是那时我知道了——她父亲有老年痴呆，她爷爷也是，所以我知道发生了什么。很快她开始忘记人名，当它开始变得很糟时，她就老想走，老想离开家，为了不让她走，我不得不躺在门前。有天早上醒来找不到她，我吓坏了：‘她去哪儿了？她去哪儿了？’ 我跑出去，那时天还没亮，四周一片漆黑，路上有个路灯，将将能看见她正过马路。我跑过去，找到了她，但她打我，就是不想回家。”小编@人在深圳 (2/3) “We celebrated our 50th wedding anniversary in Branson, Missouri. On the drive home, she kept telling me that we were going the wrong way. She was very insistent. I didn’t fight her. I kept letting her turn around because I knew that eventually we’d hit the main road back to Michigan. I knew then. Her father had dementia. And so did his father. So I knew what was happening. Soon she started forgetting names. When it started getting really bad, she wanted to walk away. She was always trying to leave the house. I’d have to lie in front of the door to keep her from going. One morning I woke up and I couldn’t find her. I freaked out: ‘Where did she go? Where did she go?’ I ran outside and it was totally dark. Down the road there was a streetlight. And I could barely see her—crossing the road. I ran and I got her. But she fought me. She didn’t want to come back home.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiInwitF0&u=005trlAagw1fa0szi69dvj31kw11xten )

>  (1/3) “我19，她16，我们一般都约会在星期天，也没做什么，我们都比较保守，我是个农民，我们不是那种摇摆的人，但每次约会都多一分亲热。然后她带我去了她的毕业舞会，在里士满，离这儿只有十英里。我是唯一一个没穿晚礼服的，那些城里人都不知道该如何对待我。我都说不清我们是啥时候坠入爱河的，包括我啥时候请求她嫁给我，它就那样自然发生了。我想我们就只是坐在车里，然后我把戒指给她。我没有很多重大的时刻来分享，我们是简单的人，但那些都是快乐的日子。”小编@人在深圳 (1/3) “I was nineteen. She was sixteen. Our dates were normally on Sunday. We didn’t do much of anything. We were conservative. I was a farmer. We weren’t those swinging type people. But every date was a little more cuddly. Then she took me to her senior prom. It was just ten miles from here—in Richmond. I was the only one there without a tuxedo. All those city folks didn’t know what to make of me. I can’t tell you when we fell in love. I can’t even tell you when I asked her to marry me. It was just natural. I think we were just sitting in the car and I gave her the ring. I don't have many big moments to share. We were simple people. They were all happy days.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiIc6iZIM&u=005trlAagw1fa0s6j17m4j31kw11xn2p )

>  “别误会，我希望每个人都能和睦相处，我不想让自己听上去像个种族主义者。但他们在进入我们的国家，如果你问我，我会说正是这点使那些人成为了种族主义者。伴随着那些到来的穆斯林，有些事情正在发生，它就在那儿，只是很多我们都不知道而已。他们蓄谋已久，他们想要所有这些，他们想要控制这一切，他们想让我们的子孙为他们工作。我希望床破能做点什么，我们需要有人说不。”小编@人在深圳 “Don’t get me wrong. I want everyone to get along. And I don’t want to sound racist. But they’re coming into our country. If you ask me, that makes them racist. There’s something going on with the Muslims. There’s something going on there. There’s a lot we don’t know about. They have a game plan. They want all the businesses. They want control. They want my grandchildren to work for them. I’m hoping he can do something about it. We need somebody to say no.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiCkItRun&u=005trlAagw1fa02k3bc1jj31kw11xtg7 )

>  “感觉无家可归，感觉这不是我曾以为的那个地方，感觉不知道自己身在何处、我们又身在何处。上周学生们开始高喊，要在当地一所中学的餐厅里建一堵墙，然后一些西班牙裔的孩子开始哭。要是你是校长，你会怎样阻止这种行为？要是总统一意孤行，你该怎样告诉孩子这是不可接受的？如何站得住脚呢？真是让人心碎。已经有朋友联系我，他们说：‘我知道你为啥不开心，但那些不是我投票给他的原因。’ 然后我才开始明白，我意识到：很多人想要改变，超过了他们希望孩子们不哭。”小编@人在深圳 “I feel homeless. Like this isn’t the place that I thought it was. I feel like I don’t understand where I am. Where we all are. Last week students started chanting ‘build the wall’ in the lunchroom of a local middle school. Some of the Hispanic children started crying. If you’re the principal-- how are you supposed to stop that behavior? If the president can behave in a certain way, how are you supposed to tell a child that it’s unacceptable? How does that hold up? It breaks my heart. I’ve had friends reach out to me. They’ve told me: ‘I understand the reasons that you’re upset. But those aren’t the reasons I voted for him.’ And I’m just starting to understand that. I’m realizing that a lot of people wanted change more than they wanted kids not to cry."
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiCcWgDHY&u=005trlAagw1fa0230bc1mj31kw11xtjq )

>  “这不是我第一次开花店，二十年前我就开过一间，但它倒闭了。当时我一蹶不振，而且那时我刚离婚，有一种彻底地挫败感。几个月我都不能开车经过那间店所在的那条街。但有一天一个朋友告诉我，说我的想法大错特错，他说：‘你把注意力太多地放在了关门上，想想你开店的那些年，想想你做的那些工作、你卖的那些花、你服务过的那些人吧。你都开了二十年，开都开了，不能因为它没能永远开下去，就说它没价值啊。’”小编@人在深圳 “This isn’t the first time I’ve owned a flower shop. I owned another store twenty years ago, but it went bankrupt. I was devastated. I’d just gotten divorced. I felt like a complete failure. For months I couldn’t even drive down the street where the shop had been. But one day a friend told me that I’d been looking at it all wrong. He told me: ‘You’re focused too much on the closing. Think of all the years that the shop was open. Think of all the jobs you provided, the flowers that you sold, and all the people that you served. You were open for twenty years. It was happening. And just because it didn’t happen forever, doesn’t mean it wasn’t valuable.’”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiBUXEjaG&u=005trlAagw1fa00yg0wfwj31kw11xq7u )

>  “我只是觉得人们都喜欢把自己的问题怪罪于别人，他们惦记错了，他们太专注于别人得到了什么。我没能上大学，我妈妈靠一己之力养活了五个孩子，我16岁就不得不工作，所以我没能去做所有那些我想去做的事，但我从没抱怨过。我的工作从来说不上太好，我工作过汉堡王、沃尔玛，现在在克莱斯勒。三家，我都获得过晋升。在被人注意到这方面我从未有问题，经理们留心着呢——如果你不抱怨，努力工作，该轮班轮班，你会得到晋升的。所以我不抱怨。我今年28，无债一身轻。克莱斯勒还有一个程序，他们会支付我上大学的费用。我也有了足够的条件来帮我妈妈，实际上现在我就在给她挑一台新的烘干机呢。”小编@人在深圳 “I just think that people are looking to blame someone else for their problems. They’re worried about the wrong stuff. They’re too fixated on what other people are getting. I wasn’t able to go to college. My mom raised five kids on her own. I’ve had to work since I was sixteen. So I haven’t gotten to do all the things I wanted to do. But I’ve never complained. I’ve never been ‘too good’ for a job. I worked at Burger King. I worked at Walmart. Now I work at Chrysler. And I got promoted at all three places. I've never had a problem getting noticed. Managers notice things. If you don’t complain, and work hard, and pick up shifts, you’ll move up. So I don't complain. I’m twenty-eight now. I have no debt. Chrysler even has a program where they’ll pay for my college. I've got enough to help out my mom. I’m actually picking her up a new dryer right now.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiAI7wnvb&u=005trlAagw1f9zusclp6pj30xc0m8n0k )

>  “我以为我们幸福：我们两个孩子，她是个好妈妈。但婚后三四年，她开始玩那种虚拟人生的在线游戏。游戏中你可以成为任何人，她可以是一个完美的妻子或任何人，然后她就老是待在电脑前。然后她开始玩另一个游戏，能跟人结婚、约会，还能上床。这一切都是假的是没错，但实际上人们会因此而发展感情。现实生活中这些人可能450磅，但在网上看起来就像超人。实际上就有这么个人，她叫他‘我的超人’，那人甚至开始邮寄超人的那些小玩意儿到家里。她就是不肯戒，我甚至用手打烂她的手机。我只是想让她跟我们好好过日子，但对她来说光有我们还不够。”小编@人在深圳 “I thought we were happy. We had two kids. She was a great mom. But three or four years into our marriage, she started playing that Sims game online. You can be anyone in that game. She could be the perfect wife or whatever. She was always on that computer. Then she started playing this other game where you can marry, date, and screw people. All of it is fake, but people actually develop feelings for each other. In real life these guys are probably 450 lbs. but online they look like Superman. There was actually one guy that she called ‘her Superman.’ He even started mailing Superman trinkets to the house. She wouldn’t quit. I even tried to break her cellphone with my hand. I just wanted her to live her life with us. But we weren’t enough for her.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Eiz8AB1MQ&u=005trlAajw1f9zo5olnqcj31kw11x44y )

>  “13岁时我就知道了，这没啥好纠结的，我也不问对错，我只知道这就是我。但我仍然深柜，因为我在一个笃信宗教的社区，连我想去上个大学都会被人质疑。它会被视为不信奉上帝。如果我家人知道我是个同志，我会很惨——听着，他们都还不错，他们不是坏人，这只是他们信仰的东西，我也没生他们的气。让我生气的是现状——如果我选择去坠入爱河，那么任何我认识的人都不会再理我。”小编@人在深圳 “I’ve known since I was thirteen. It wasn’t a struggle for me. I didn’t question whether it was ‘right’ or ‘wrong.’ I just knew it was me. But I’m still completely closeted. I’m part of a very religious community. Even my choice to go to college was questioned. It’s seen as not trusting in God. If my family knew I was gay, I’d be cut off completely. Listen, they’re not bad. They aren’t bad people. It’s just what they believe. I’m not angry at them. I’m angry at the situation. If I choose to fall in love, then nobody that I’ve ever known will speak to me again.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiyNU9BGn&u=005trlAagw1f9zmqaz08tj31kw11xtde )

>  “我认为很多人都生活在种族主义的临界线上。我工作在一个机械车间，那儿有三十来个年长的家伙。我不认为我们组里有一个坏蛋，如果你遇到他们，你会喜欢他们的，他们所有人都爱自己的家人。但我听到他们中80%的人都说过某种形式的种族主义言论，很多年长点的说得更劲爆。但如果一个黑人走过来，他们又会很友好，他们甚至会跟他一起出去吃午饭，并且分享着吃。老实说，我不认为他们会当自己是种族主义者，他们每个人都会矢口否认，他们会指着那个他们友好相处的黑人，而绝口不提当他不在时他们说的那些话。”小编@人在深圳 “I think a lot of people live on the borderline of racism. I work in a machine shop with about thirty older guys. I don’t think there is one bad guy in the group. You’d like them if you met them. All of them love their families. But I’d say that I’ve heard eighty percent of them make racist comments of some sort. A lot of the older guys drop ‘n bombs.’ But if a black guy walks up, they’ll be friendly. They’ll even go out to lunch with him and share a meal. I honestly don’t think they see themselves as racist. Every one of them will deny it. They’ll point to the black guy that they’re friendly with. They won't point to the things they say when he’s not around.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EisKQ8H9e&u=005trlAagw1f9yw01dhfsj30xc0m8diy )

>  “If I think back, I get depressed. If I think ahead, I get afraid.”小编@人在深圳 ：欢迎你来译，看谁点赞多 [good][围观] ​​​
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EisB3t9ZD&u=005trlAagw1f9yvuf2re9j30xc0m80uu )

>  “我在一家机床自动化公司工作，我们生产那种能制造汽车的机器。高中真不是我能上的，我都没好好上过课，脑子里塞满了各种东西。一开始我是在工厂里打扫地板，后来又被调到电锯车间，现在我在做电气安装。现在我一个小时17刀呢。我已经开始学PLC了，这样还能升得更高。实际上在我这块儿机会挺多的，并没有太多竞争。在我这个年龄没人愿意干这活儿，他们都想去上艺术学校，或者做视频游戏，或者其他东西。我想可能是因为太多的人被告知你要去做任何你想做的事情。反正不管你认为你能成为什么样的人，仍然会有像我这样的人。”小编@人在深圳 “I work at a machine tool automation company. We build the machines that build the cars. High school wasn’t for me. I didn’t respond well to being lectured and having things jammed into my brain. So I started out sweeping floors at the factory, then I got moved into the saw shop, and now I do electrical installation. I’m up to $17 an hour now. And I’ve started studying PLC so I can move up even further. There’s actually a lot of opportunity in my field. There's not much competition. Nobody my age wants to do this stuff. They all want to go to art school or make video games or something. I think maybe it’s because too many people are being told to do whatever they want. Because no matter what you think you can be, there’s still gotta be people like me.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EisyYCZfC&u=005trlAagw1f9yvh4yd3yj31kw11xafj )

>  “我妈妈死于肺癌，我16岁生日那天。实际上我的生日就快到了——就这个周六。我妈妈去世前我还是个好学生，一切都好，可能还会得一笔奖学金，唱歌方面的，但她去世后我不再关心这些了。我妈妈是我最大的粉丝，即使病得不轻，她也会坐着轮椅来看我表演，她的头发从头上滑落，就那样坐在前排。她去世后我停止了歌唱，没人再让我为她唱歌了。我爸爸养育了我们，他人很好——你想知道他有多么了不起么？他上法庭，想通过法律途径把我的生日改了，这样我就不用每年生日都经历一次那种痛苦。虽然最后不允许这样做，但他毕竟试过了。”小编@人在深圳 “My mom died of lung cancer on my sixteenth birthday. My birthday is actually coming up—this Saturday. Before she passed away, I was a good student and everything. I was probably going to get a scholarship for singing. But I stopped caring after that. My mom was my biggest fan. Even when she was really sick, she came to my singing recital in a wheelchair, with her hair falling out of her head, and she sat on the front row. I quit singing after she died. There was nobody to sing for anymore. My Dad raised us. And he was wonderful. You want to know how awesome my Dad is? He went to court and tried to legally change my birthday. Just so I wouldn’t have to go through it every year. It turns out you’re not allowed to do that. But he tried.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EirVNomvB&u=005trlAagw1f9ys4it6lkj30xc0m8mz0 )

>  “我妹搬来住了，她的五只猫也跟来了，连她前夫也一起来了，让人抓狂。我妹看电视喜欢看那些谋杀案，她前夫是个爱尔兰人，总在说马铃薯饥荒，跟他喜欢马铃薯饥荒似的，老扯马铃薯饥荒。还有那几只猫，小Louie还蛮可爱，但最大的那只看起来就像加菲猫，喵喵叫个不停，它叫Nitro。我在努力保持淡定，这不刚拿起一本教人正向思考的书么。”小编@人在深圳  “My sister moved in, her five cats moved in, and her ex-husband moved in. It’s driving me nuts. My sister watches those murder programs. And her ex-husband is Irish so he keeps talking about the potato famine. He loves that potato famine. Always the potato famine. And those cats. Little Louie is sweet, but the biggest cat looks like Garfield and won’t stop meowing. His name is Nitro. I’m trying to keep it together. I just picked up one of those positive thinking books.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Eirob1cvo&u=005trlAagw1f9ypy2e9l3j30xc0m8wgh )

>  “早上我和女友分手了。我们在一起三年，但我是天主教徒，而她不知道她是否相信上帝。本来我还想有一天向她求婚呢，我觉得她会是个好妈妈和好妻子。但我又觉得这可能是我们克服不了的东西——我想在天主教教堂里结婚，我想让我的孩子们也成为天主教徒，这对我来说很重要，而这是我们迟早都要去面对的，我觉得这样拖下去也不好。但失去她真的很痛苦，我们俩都哭红了眼睛。她在我生命中是如此重要的一部分，一有啥好事，我首先想告诉的人就是她。我真的尊重她，虽然她拒绝因为我那么做而去相信一些东西，但我又不知道该咋办，希望上帝能给我一个答案。”小编@人在深圳 “I broke up with my girlfriend this morning. We’d been together for three years. But I’m Catholic, and she doesn’t know if she believes in God or not. I wanted to propose to her one day. I think she’d be a great mom and a great wife. But I feel like this might be something we can’t overcome. I want to get married in a Catholic church. I want to raise my children to be Catholic. It’s important to me and it's something that we’d have to deal with eventually. So I didn’t think it would be a good idea to keep putting it off. But it really hurts to lose her. Both of us were bawling our eyes out. She was such a big part of my life. Every time something good happens, she is the first person I want to tell. And I do respect that she refuses to believe in something just because I do. But I don’t know what to do. I’m hoping God will give me an answer.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EirdvobwF&u=005trlAagw1f9yp2pl99ij31kw11xgt0 )

>  “我爸妈都是意大利移民，我们成长于‘万宝路计划’(Marlboro projects)期间。我爸是个卖肉的，很有‘故国风范’，印象里他一次都没跟我说过他为我感到骄傲。不过那也没什么，他教会我生活中每一样东西都要你自己去赚。我25岁生日那天，我爸碰到我的一个工友，那时我刚被升为副工头，工友告诉我爸我工作做得有多棒。然后我爸回家，一把揪住我的衣领，拉我过去吻我的额头，眼含热泪，跟我说他有多为我感到骄傲。对我来说，那比之前我做的任何事都意味着更多。要想听到我爸再说这句话，估计我还要再等25年吧。”小编@人在深圳 “Both my parents were Italian immigrants. We grew up in the Marlboro projects. My dad was a butcher. He was very ‘old country.’ I don’t think he once told me that he was proud of me. But it didn’t bother me. He taught me that you have to earn every single thing you get in life. On my twenty-fifth birthday, my Dad ran into one of my coworkers. I’d just been promoted to deputy foreman. They told him how great of a job I was doing. My dad came home, grabbed me by the neck, pulled me toward him, and kissed me on the forehead. There were tears in his eyes. He told me how proud he was of me. And that meant more to me than anything I’d done until then. It’ll probably be another twenty-five years before I hear it again.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiqOveisy&u=005trlAagw1f9yn66riulj31kw11x42o )

>  “1999年我第一次参加国会竞选，就被打败了，而那时我刚得到人们的欢呼声——我在州立法机关工作了很长时间，我在少数党，并未做很多事，又离开家人，把家庭重担丢给了Michelle，自己只顾竞选，却输得那么惨。当时我想：也许我不是这块料儿。我已经四十岁了，投入大量时间和精力的事情，似乎并没什么作用。但也正是那件事，让我度过了那一刻，以及其他任何时候，当我不知所措，它让我提醒自己：这是为了工作。如果你老在担心自己，老想着：‘我成功了么？我位置正确么？人们会欣赏感激我么？’ 你会灰心丧气，陷入困局。但如果你专注于工作，你将永远有出路。总有些事，是需要人去做的。”小编@人在深圳 “I first ran for Congress in 1999, and I got beat. I just got whooped. I had been in the state legislature for a long time, I was in the minority party, I wasn’t getting a lot done, and I was away from my family and putting a lot of strain on Michelle. Then for me to run and lose that bad, I was thinking maybe this isn’t what I was cut out to do. I was forty years old, and I’d invested a lot of time and effort into something that didn’t seem to be working. But the thing that got me through that moment, and any other time that I’ve felt stuck, is to remind myself that it’s about the work. Because if you’re worrying about yourself—if you’re thinking: ‘Am I succeeding? Am I in the right position? Am I being appreciated?’ – then you’re going to end up feeling frustrated and stuck. But if you can keep it about the work, you’ll always have a path. There’s always something to be done.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EipXCscUz&u=005trlAagw1f9yinmirzjj31kw11xadm )

>  “作为一名记者，我跑了许多特朗普集会，我没感觉到任何仇恨，也从未被人攻击，感觉人们是比对任何东西都更好奇。我觉得多数人支持他都只是因为他不是当权者的一员，或者说大家厌倦了政治。但也挺让人困惑的，因为即便我没感觉到他们恨我，但对说我应该被驱逐出境的人，他们又是支持的。即使是我最好的一个朋友，她爸也支持特朗普。这人让我到他家去，感恩节我就跟着去了。我朋友问她爸：‘爸爸，你怎么能支持那个人呢？我们的朋友Zahra就是个穆斯林哦。’ 她爸说：‘放心吧，他不会做他说的一切。’ 今天已经够难的了——过去的几周大家主要还是猜测，你隐约有种预感多数美国人会支持他。而那时我还可以希望，希望这预感是错的。但现在希望没了，我必须感觉不一样了，我必须感觉可能多数美国人不希望我在这儿。我觉得我再如何努力，也永远融不进这里了。即使他们对我很友好，即使他们邀请我去过感恩节，内心深处他们仍然相信美国是一个属于白人的国家。”小编@人在深圳 “I covered a lot of Trump rallies as a journalist. I didn’t feel any hatred. People were more curious than anything. I was never assaulted. I felt like most people were just supporting him because he wasn’t part of the establishment. Or because they were tired of politics. But it was confusing. Because even though I didn’t feel like they hated me, these people were supporting someone who said I should be banned from the country. Even the father of one of my best friends supports Trump. This man had me over to his house. I went to Thanksgiving with him. My friend asked him: ‘Dad, how can you support that man? Our friend Zahra is a Muslim.’ He told her: ‘Don’t worry. He won’t do everything that he says.’ Today has been difficult. These last few weeks, it was mostly speculation. There was suspicion that most Americans supported him but I could hope that it was wrong. But now that hope is gone. And I have to feel differently. I have to feel like maybe most Americans don’t want me here. And I feel like no matter how hard I try, I’ll never be part of the community. And even if they’re friendly to me, or if they invite me to Thanksgiving, deep down they believe that America is a country that belongs to white people.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EipuDyHWX&u=005trlAagw1f9yi2oi5wwj31kw11xdjd )

-----------------------

>  “部队里多数人是真心想做正确的事，因为跳向手榴弹而获得荣誉勋章的比其他任何人都多。它是一种文化：当官的最后吃，有水大家喝。这些人从小就当童子军，他们志愿参军的原因就是想做正确的事。可是，在战争中什么是正确的，从来都是不清不楚：你开枪早一步，一个无辜的人被杀了；你开枪晚一步，你少了一个好兄弟。所以很多人受的伤实际上是精神上的：多数回来的人都会觉得自己做错了什么，或者自己做得不够，或者战友牺牲得太多。在部队我最好的朋友叫Ronnie Winchester，他是你能想象到的最好的人。我22岁生日是在我们的军官训练课时度过的，那时大家都睡不着，饿得，因为每天的口粮限量供应。但Ronnie想给我一个难忘的生日，他把他的布朗尼饼插上蜡烛给了我。他就是这么好，但他死在了伊拉克。如果一个像Ronnie这样的人牺牲了，你会禁不住想：那我凭什么还活着？”小编@人在深圳 “The military is mostly filled with people who genuinely desire to do the right thing. More Marines receive the Medal of Honor for jumping on grenades than any other action. It’s a culture where officers eat last and everyone shares their water. These people grew up as boy scouts and girl scouts. The whole reason they volunteered was because they wanted to do the right thing. But the right thing is never clear in war. If you shoot too early, an innocent person gets killed. If you shoot too late, you lose a buddy. So a lot of our injuries are moral ones. Most of us come home feeling like we did something wrong. Or we didn’t give enough. Or that our friends gave too much. My best friend in the Marines was a guy named Ronnie Winchester. He was the nicest guy you can imagine. My 22nd birthday was during our officer training course. None of us had slept. We were all starving. We were only getting one ration per day. But Ronnie wanted to give me a memorable birthday. So he put a candle in his brownie and gave it to me. That’s how nice of a guy he was. Ronnie ended up getting killed in Iraq. And if a guy like Ronnie got killed, you can’t help but wonder why you deserve to be alive.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiaOk05FV&u=005trlAagw1f9wonha3edj31fi0ycdlm )

-----------------------

>  “有天晚上我跟我们营长Willy Buhl上校出去喝啤酒，他是个很关心下属的人，他是那种能记住每个下属名字和生日的领导。我们坐在酒吧，说起我们失去的每一个兄弟——好多我们营里的士兵退伍后自杀了。最近就有一个，特别糟：开枪自尽，而他老婆孩子当时就在楼下。我们发现很快我们营里退伍后自杀的人比在战场上死于敌手的还多。它就像一种流行病：一个老兵自杀，就会传得尽人皆知。我知道我们要做点什么了，我们要做得更好。然后我就联系了Ann Beeder博士，她是顶级的精神病学和公共健康方面的专家，我问了她一个问题：在退伍兵们寻求帮助的过程中，我们能不能把所有那些不和谐的因素去掉？而‘勇往直前’(Headstrong Proj)就是我们对那个问题的答案。我们想建立一种治疗方案，不需要花钱，也没有任何官僚，退伍兵们唯一的挑战就是到这里来，来除去PTSD（创伤综合症）留给他们的烙印。”小编@人在深圳 “I went out for beers one night with my battalion commander-- Colonel Willy Buhl. He really cared about us. He was one of those leaders who’d remember the name and birthday of every man in his battalion. So we’re sitting at the bar one night, and we’re talking about all the men we’d lost to suicide. A number of Marines from our battalion had killed themselves since we’d been home. And there had been an especially bad one recently. One of our guys had shot himself with his wife and kids downstairs. Colonel Buhl and I realized that there’d soon be a point in time when we’d lost more Marines to suicide than to enemy action. And I knew we had to do something. It’s an epidemic. Every veteran knows another veteran who’s taken their own life. We have to do better. So I approached a top psychiatrist and public health expert named Dr. Ann Beeder, and I asked her a question: Can we take all the friction out of the process of getting help? The Headstrong Project was our answer to that question. We wanted to create a treatment option with zero cost and zero bureaucracy, so that a veteran’s only challenge was showing up. All they have to do is overcome the stigma of PTSD.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EiaDNfbWT&u=005trlAagw1f9wokbr519j31hc0zkwn9 )

>  我想起李安的新作《比利·林恩的中场战事》，最让人伤感的一句台词：“你是个英雄哦！你不是还要返回战场么？” 这部电影现在正在影院上映，不要被各种关于它新技术的吐槽所干扰，去影院看看吧，自己看自己感受才是硬道理。感人至深的情感，清澈有力的思想，这也是“人在XX”存在的意义，更是我要向@人在纽约 学习的。晚安各位。 小编@人在深圳
![]( https://weibo.cn/repost/Ei1vUhXAG?uid=5015695726&rl=0 )

>  “在阿富汗我无数次想象着，想象着当我回到家会是什么样。想象中我构建了一个完美的世界：我要吃个大奶酪汉堡，痛痛快快洗个澡，和朋友们欢聚一堂——我们可以去海边玩一圈，只是为了叙叙旧。然后一切都还像我离开时那样，大家见到我开心得不得了，因为他们对我所做的牺牲心存感激。可是，当飞机落地，没人来接我——我妈请不起假；我离开期间我爸过世了；我家其他人又付不起旅费。我先去见了两个朋友，他们给我写过信。在阿富汗整个期间，我只收到过四封信，都是这两个朋友写的。所以我想马上、当面去告诉他们：对当时的我来说，那些信意味着整个世界。跟他们见面后，我意识到我太一厢情愿了。然后我就坐在自己的房间里，开始想：在阿富汗时我忙成那样，每天干不完的活儿，但现在它是那么不起眼。我想起所有那些我压抑住的事，我想起我救的那个小女孩，她现在过得怎样？她还活着么？要是她还活着，这是她想要的么？”小编@人在深圳 “In Afghanistan I spent so much time imagining what it would be like when I came home. I built up this perfect world. I imagined eating a big cheeseburger. And taking the longest shower. And meeting up with all my friends. Maybe we’d even take a trip to the beach just to catch up. And everything would be just like when I left. And people would be so happy to see me. Because they’d be thankful for the sacrifices that I made. But when my plane landed, nobody was there to meet me. My mom couldn’t afford to take off work. My father had died while I was gone. The rest of my family couldn’t afford to travel. One of the first things I did was visit the two friends who had written me letters. The whole time I was in Afghanistan, I only got four letters from two friends. So I had to visit them right away to tell them that those letters meant the world to me. But after those visits, I was pretty much by myself. So I sat in my room and I started thinking. I’d been so busy in Afghanistan. There was always a job to do. But now it was quiet. So I thought about all the things that I’d kept at bay. I thought about the little girl that I saved. And what her life is like now. And I wondered if she’s still alive. And if she is still alive, does she even want to be?”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ei1p8rrCc&u=005trlAagw1f9vjurn22gj31al0v2418 )

-----------------------

>  “在战争冲突地区当一个医护兵，要说对你没什么影响，那是不可能的。我曾倍感艰难，想忘记那个小女孩：那天两个人抬着一捆毯子冲进我们医护站，他们用普什图语(Pashto，阿富汗官话)喊叫着。我第一眼看到的是血糊糊的毯子，揭开后才看到那个小女孩。她踢皮球踩到了地雷，膝盖以下、胳膊肘以下、手以下都被炸没了，血肉模糊，都能闻到血腥味。她惨叫着，但我被训练得能够无视这些，我可以充耳不闻，只专注于止血、绑止血带、静脉注射。我给她打了超剂量的吗啡，我永远都忘不了，我就那样推着注射器，直到惨叫声停止。然后直升机来了，把她运走了。她活下来了。整个救治过程我都挺好，就像个机器人，我们训练的就是如何应对这种让人手忙脚乱的状况。可是，他们没有训练你，他们没有训练你当直升机走了，突然一切归于沉寂，你该如何是好。”小编@人在深圳 “ I don’t think it’s possible to be a medic in a conflict zone and not have something stay with you. Something that you didn’t have before you went. I have the hardest time forgetting this little girl. She was brought to our post one day. Two men ran toward us carrying a bundle of blankets. And they’re yelling in Pashto. And at first all I can see are these bloody blankets, but then I peel them back, and there’s this little girl inside. She stepped on a landmine while playing soccer and she’s gone below the knee, gone below the elbow, gone below the hand. And everything is seething. And I can smell the flesh. And she’s screaming. But I’m trained to drown it out. I’m trained so well that I almost don’t hear the screaming. I focus on our interventions. Stop the bleeding. Apply tourniquets. Administer the IV. I overdosed her on morphine. I’ll never forget that. I just kept pushing until the screaming stopped. And then a helicopter came and got her. And she lived. And I was fine throughout the whole thing. I was just like a robot. I’d been trained for chaotic situations. But they don’t train you for the aftermath. They don’t train you for when the helicopter has lifted off, and suddenly everything is quiet.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ei1gLgFsJ&u=005trlAagw1f9vipf1iiuj31kw11x43u )

-----------------------

>  “那晚我出现幻觉后，我们队的两个队员过来跟我说：你需要帮助。我说：不，我不需要。他们说：你需要，我们多数人都需要。正是这句话最终说服了我。我之所以不肯寻求帮助是因为我不想表现出脆弱。我父亲曾在越战中失去他的整个队伍，作为他的儿子，我接受过世界上最严格的训练，这辈子我从不退缩。所以我花了很长的时间才承认自己有问题。看到那些无家可归，或者醉生梦死的老兵，我会说那不是我。我有一份好工作，我有自己的家庭。我曾竭尽全力，想用身体上的疲累来解决自己的问题，我全身心投入工作，早上长距离游泳，晚上还跑长跑，心想只要不停止运动，压力总能化解。但还是不行，以失败告终。当初那两个队友说服我去接受治疗，那是我做过的最好的决定。过去我认为求助是软弱的表现，现在我意识到我真正的软弱是从不肯求助。”小编@人在深圳 “After I had the flashback that night, two of the guys on my team came up to me and said: ‘You’re getting help.’ I said: ‘No I’m not.’ And they said: ‘Yes you are. Most of us do.’ And that finally convinced me. I’d never gotten help because I never wanted to appear weak. I’m the son of a man who lost his entire team in Vietnam. I’ve been through some of the toughest training on earth. I never quit anything in my life. So it took me the longest time to admit that I had a problem. Whenever I saw a homeless vet, or an alcoholic vet, I’d say: ‘That’s not me. I’ve got a good job. I’ve got a family.’ I did my best to cope with my issues through physical exertion. I threw myself into work. I’d go for long swims in the morning and long runs at night. I thought if I never stopped moving, I could hold down my stress. But it finally caught up with me. And I broke down. And those two guys convinced me to go to therapy. And it was the best decision I’ve ever made. I used to think that I was weak for needing help. I realize now that my weakness was never getting it.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ei17Io31D&u=005trlAagw1f9vi405dobj31kw11xgqg )

>  “我噩梦不断，老是梦见自己被困在一辆燃烧的车里，然后就会尖叫着从梦中惊醒。我无法呼吸，根本睡不着。我疲乏过度，又经历了一场糟糕透顶的离婚。在特种部队当医护兵时，有天晚上工作时我产生了严重的幻觉：当时我们是去执行一次保障任务，所有人都在一辆敞篷货车后面，因为要夜视，周围黑漆漆地。这时有人打开手电调整装备，我看到我们的影子投射在墙上。突然之间我感觉我们是在一架直升机上，我努力打消这想法，但它是如此真实。我跟自己说'淡定，淡定'，我知道那不是真的，但我真的闻到了燃料的味道，也听到了飞机发动机的声音，然后机舱后门打开……再然后我就站在一栋楼的三楼了，我也不知道我是怎么到那儿的。那是我参加的最后一次突击，那周后来我们有段时间在训练。再后来我把自己关进一辆车里，放下枪，开始哭，我崩溃了。第二天，我开始寻求帮助。”小编@人在深圳 “I kept having these nightmares of being trapped in a burning vehicle. They were non-stop. I’d wake up screaming and I couldn’t breathe. I wasn’t sleeping at all. I was overworked and going through a horrible divorce. At the time I was working as a medic on a SWAT team, and one night at work I had a really bad flashback. We were about to serve a warrant. All of us were in the back of a truck and it was completely dark because we were preserving our night vision. And somebody turned on a red flashlight to adjust their equipment. And I'm seeing our shadows on the wall, and suddenly I think we're in a helicopter. And I’m trying to fight it but it seems so real. I’m telling myself, ‘Keep it together. Keep it together.’ I know it’s not real but I'm actually smelling the fuel and hearing the sounds of the turbine. And then the back door opened. And the next thing I know, I'm standing on the third floor of this building with no idea how I got there. And that was the last raid I ever did. We had a training session later that week. Afterwards I closed myself in a van, put down my rifle, and started to cry. I was stressed to the hilt. The next day I started looking for help.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ei0kWiTTR&u=005trlAagw1f9v5kyhoucj31kw11x781 )

>  “当时我和排长正在装甲车里，他想打开一个压力燃料罐，结果油一下喷得车里到处都是，溅到了野营炉上——他正用那个炉子热巧克力。火苗一下窜起来了，他手上的油罐失手落地，顿时遍地是火，他身上也跟着着火了。他抓着舱门，可就是打不开，我推他也推不动。车厢里到处都是火苗，太特么热了！就像把你的手放在火炉上烤，可是你又抽不走，因为现在是你的整个身体都在火里。火光通红，他在嚎叫。我脖子周围的风帽烧得开始收缩，越来越紧，我的制服开始融化，片片剥落直往下掉。我感觉自己也烧起来了，我受不了了，我放弃了。可我不想被活活烧死，我决定深吸一口热气，把肺烧焦，喉咙窒息而死——这时舱门打开了，有人听到我们的嚎叫，帮忙打开了舱门。”小编@人在深圳 “I was inside an armored carrier with my platoon commander. He tried to open a pressurized fuel container and it sprayed across the vehicle and hit a camping stove that he was using to make hot chocolate. It burst into flames. He dropped the fuel canister and fire covered the floor. Then he caught on fire. He grabbed onto the exit hatch and wouldn’t let go. I couldn’t pull him away. And he wouldn’t let go. And the vehicle is filling up with flames. It was so fucking hot. It’s like when your hand is on a stove except you can’t pull it away because it’s your whole body. And it’s so bright and I can hear him screaming. And the hood around my neck is shrinking and tightening. And my Gore-Tex uniform is melting and spreading and falling off my body. And I could feel myself burning and I couldn’t take it anymore. I gave up. I didn’t want to burn to death. I decided to take a deep breath to singe my lungs and close my throat. Then the hatch opened. Someone heard us screaming and opened the hatch.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhZaGEY6p&u=005trlAagw1f9v57ua8v9j31kw11xgtg )

>  “在部队我们被训练得思想要统一，一切都是如此标准化，你只管行动，甚至都不需要思考。如果我需要夜视镜，别人可以把他的背包丢给我，我能准确地知道该去哪个口袋找。我们就像是齿轮上的齿——这可能听上去不像是什么好事，但事实上并非如此。虽然没人想把自己当成齿轮上的一颗齿，但人是喜欢有组织的，这样我们的行为才是可预期的。我们所有人都是这样，倾向于在同一时间，出现在同一地点，日复一日。只不过这种倾向性在部队里被加快了而已。而且那感觉挺好，你清楚自己的位置，你和大家穿相同的制服，你很清楚自己做出了什么贡献，对你执行的任务，对你的团队，甚至对整个国家，你的价值都是一目了然的。但当你回到家，那些线变模糊了，你很难再找到自己的价值，不知道该把自己放在哪里合适，你也不知道该如何跟别人建立联系，不知道该如何变得有用。那感觉会很孤立无援，你所有想做的，就是重新回到队伍中去。”小编@人在深圳 “We were built to think alike. Everything is so standardized in the military that you can function without thinking. If I ever needed night vision goggles, somebody could throw me their bag, and I’d know exactly what pocket to find them in. We were like cogs in a wheel. And that may sound like a bad thing—but it’s not. Nobody wants to think of themselves as cogs in a wheel, but humans love structure. Our behavior is predictive. All of us tend to be in the same place, at the same time, every single day. The tendency is just accelerated in the military. And it feels good. It feels good to know your place. It feels good to wear the same uniform. It feels good to know exactly what you’re contributing to the mission, to the team, and to the country as a whole. Your value is so clear. But then you come home and the lines are blurred. It's hard to discover that value again. You’re not sure where you fit. You’re not sure how you connect to other people. You’re not sure how to make a difference. It can be very isolating. And all you want to do is be back on a team.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhXjG996G&u=005trlAagw1f9v18wous7j31eo0xsacm )

>  “我并没感觉有啥好，它会让我余生有烦扰，但老实说，那又何乐而不为呢。真正让我感到惭愧的，是当时我所知甚少。那时我还是个来自德州的孩子，去新兵训练营时还是第一次坐飞机，当时我有一种本能的愿望——我要给9/11报仇雪恨。当政府说9/11跟伊拉克有关时，我深信不疑，所以我完全支持伊战，我认为我们是在让坏人接受正义的审判。我不知道这中间还有什么玄机，我对伊拉克的人、文化，以及那个国家都是一无所知。很快我就要拿到中东历史的硕士学位了，了解得越多，感觉就越糟糕，真是让人羞愧。参军让我个人得到很多好处，从很多方面来看，它都是我做过的最大件事。但我本可以通过其他的方式来得到那些好处。我在伊拉克待了一年，那一年的痛苦经历将会影响我一生。但对伊拉克当地人来说，已经十年了，而他们还在经历这种痛苦，每天每时每刻。”小编@人在深圳 “I don’t feel good about it. It will bother me for the rest of my life and honestly I’m happy about that. I’m embarrassed by how little I knew. I was a kid from Texas. I flew on a plane for the first time when I went to boot camp. I had this visceral desire to seek vengeance for 9/11, and I believed our government when they told me that there was a connection to Iraq. So I fully supported the war. I thought we were bringing bad people to justice. I didn’t understand the nuances. I didn’t know anything about the people of Iraq, or the culture, or the country. And I feel ashamed about that. I’m getting my graduate degree in Middle Eastern history right now. And the more I learn, the worse I feel. I got so much personal benefit from being in the military. In many ways it was the greatest thing I’ve ever done. But I could have gotten those personal benefits from other means. I was in Iraq for one year. And the trauma of that year will impact me for the rest of my life. But for the people of Iraq, it’s been ten years. And they’re still being traumatized on a daily basis.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhX9sjO1N&u=005trlAagw1f9v0cv5dmrj31kw11xq6x )

>  “因为去伊拉克参战，我哥大的老师们当我是恐怖分子。但我坚信美国是对的，是值得效仿的楷模。我去伊拉克是去保障那儿的人有基本的人身自由。但当你真的到了那儿，你会发现你是在跟小孩们打仗——个个都是小孩，你看到的是小孩的尸体，而不是那些用飞机撞大楼的坏蛋。这些孩子在贫穷里长大，只不过进了错误的宗教学校(madrasa)，然后被一些巨特么有钱的人操纵，来执行别人的世界观。他们中没有一个人生来是用来恨的，也没有一个人生来就特么只觉得这世界美好得一塌糊涂。”小编@人在深圳 “I have professors at Columbia who view me as a terrorist for fighting in Iraq. But I believe that America is an example to be emulated, and I went over there to provide those people with basic human freedoms. But when you get over there you realize that you’re fighting kids. Everyone was kids. You see it when they’re dead. These weren’t the guys who were flying into towers. These were kids who grew up poor, stepped into the wrong madrasa, and were manipulated by people with a shit load of money into executing somebody else’s worldview. None of them came out of the womb hating. None of them came out of the womb thinking anything else but holy shit this is a bright beautiful world.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhWSkBjbr&u=005trlAagw1f9uzgqk9goj31kw11xn1s )

>  “每一个从战场回来的人都要填一个表格，是个标准的心理评估，上面会问你的用药情况、睡眠状况这些。我们提了信息自由法，为了看Stephen填的那张表。他打了勾，说他想到过自杀，但心理顾问只是给他安排了一个睡眠方面的调查，就把他送回了家。他用一根电线上吊自杀了。Stephen真不应该去当兵，他是个天性乐观的人。小时候我们常去野营，有一次他不见了，我们在树林里找到他时，他手里握着一只小花鼠。他从不想伤害任何东西，屋里有蚂蚁他都会弄出去。他从没跟我谈过那种战争，我不知道那对他的影响有多大，我也不能肯定是什么导致了他的死，但我觉得是PTSD（创伤后遗症）。虽然最近他老婆离开了他，他工作上也被降职了，但跟这些无关。且不说对错，我真的怪那些人，Stephen告诉他们他想过自杀，他都打了勾，他们仍然把他送回了家。要是有人跟你说他想自杀，好歹你得听一听吧！”小编@人在深圳 “Everyone who comes back from deployment fills out a form. It’s a standard psychological evaluation. It asks about drug use, sleeping habits, things like that. We filed a Freedom of Information Act to see Stephen’s. He checked a box that said he thought about suicide. And they sent him home. The counselor just scheduled a sleep study and sent him home. And he hung himself with an electrical cord. Stephen should have never been a soldier. He was a happy, go-lucky guy. We used to go camping all the time when we were little. He disappeared from the campsite once and we found him in the woods with chipmunks in his hand. He never wanted to hurt anything. If there were ever ants in the house, he would take them outside. He never told me about the war. I don’t know how it affected him. And I can’t say what caused his death. Personally I think it was PTSD. But his wife had recently left him. He’d gotten demoted. But it doesn’t matter. He told them he thought about suicide. He checked that box. And they still sent him home. So whether it’s right or wrong—I do blame them. If someone says they are thinking of suicide, you need to listen.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhRQzBsgO&u=005trlAagw1f9udk284srj31fs0yj78b )

>  “在伊拉克时我们有个连长，就叫他Johnson吧。他管着所有医护兵，记考勤、安排车队，还负责和其他单位协调。他跟秘书有染，不过这不重要。我们部署9个月时，有天晚上我们去执行一次护送任务，他决定跟我们一起去。那不是他的工作，他的工作就是待在办公室，但那天晚上他决定跟着去。车队行进途中，一辆卡车触发了简易爆炸装置，无线电里喊着‘快走，快走，快走’，我们奋力通过危险区，你能听见轻型武器射击出来的子弹打在我们车上‘叮叮当当’的声音，听起来就像《拯救大兵瑞恩》开场那一幕——我之所以讨厌那部电影，就是因为他们把那种声音模仿得太像了。我们一通过危险区，Johnson就让我们停在萨马拉桥上修车。那简直愚蠢至极，因为那座桥每隔一周就会被炸毁一次。但我们就那样坐在那座桥上，把我们的M-16对着黑暗处，大家在耳语‘你听见了么？’ 我们差点朝着自己的步兵开枪，因为我们不知道那是他们。我问Johnson为什么他非要跟我们一起来，他说：‘我两个儿子，我需要有故事讲给他们听。’ 那一刻我恨他入骨——因为我是不想有这种破经历，我签字入伍时，他们说我在医院工作，我想让自己安全，但不被允许。可他有选择啊，他偏不，就因为他想要战争故事。”小编@人在深圳 “We had a company commander in Iraq—let’s call him Captain Johnson. He was in charge of all the medics. He set the rosters, scheduled the convoys, and coordinated with other units. He was also fucking his secretary but that’s less important. We were nine months into our deployment, and Captain Johnson decides to go out on a convoy with us one night. That wasn’t his job. His job was to stay inside his office. But that night he decided that he wanted to go. And during the convoy one of the trucks hits an IED. And guys are screaming ‘go, go, go’ over the radio, and we’re trying to push through the hot spot, and small arms fire keeps bouncing off our vehicles: ‘plink, plink, plink.’ It sounded just like the opening scene in Saving Private Ryan. I hate that movie because they got that sound so perfect. And as soon as we were out of the area, Captain Johnson has us stop on Samarra Bridge to repair the vehicle. And it was so stupid to stop there. Because that bridge was getting blown up every other week. And we’re sitting on that bridge, pointing our M-16’s into the dark, and people are whispering ‘do you hear that?’ And we almost shoot at our own infantry because we don’t know it’s them. And I asked Captain Johnson why he came with us. And he told me: ‘I have two sons at home. I need stories to tell them.’ And I hated him so much in that moment. Because I didn’t want this shit. When I signed up, they told me I’d be working in a hospital. I wanted to be safe, but I wasn’t allowed to be. But he had a choice, and he chose not to be. Just because he wanted war stories.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhRDEd5T9&u=005trlAagw1f9ubiy2j40j31h40zfdje )

>  “训练时我就不太适应。有天晚上我出去喝酒回来晚了，比宵禁时间晚了3分钟，然后我们的高级教官就说他要惩罚我，因为很多医护兵都看到我回来晚了，影响不好。我就问他：‘难道你就是这样当头儿的么？别人看到了你就要惩罚我？’ 他听了很不爽，冲着我直吼，还罚我做一堆俯卧撑。可那时的我，醉得五迷三道，从头到尾骂个不停，骂他是'孬种'和‘畜生’。他报告给连长，连长又报告给营长，最后他们弄了个听证会，让我听听我骂的那些污言秽语。他们问我有没有什么要说的，当时我真的应该啥都不说，保持沉默，但我已经打了一份发言稿，关于教官如何不体现军队价值的。我一念完，所有人都抓狂了。军士长冲着我的脸狂吼，他看起来很像大明星Clint Easterwood——要是Clint Easterwood只有五尺高的话。他吼完一把把我的肩章揪下来，把我带离那个房间，表情又是厌恶又是得意地看着我说：‘算你有种！’”小编@人在深圳 [good]“I didn’t fit in too well in training. I came back from drinking one night and I was three minutes after curfew. My senior drill sergeant told me that he was going to punish me because a few medics had noticed I was late. So I asked him: ‘Do you decide what kind of leader you are based on who’s watching?’ He didn’t like that. He screamed at me and made me do a bunch of pushups, and me being a drunk-ass, I was calling him a ‘pussy’ and ‘motherfucker’ the entire time. So he reported me to the company commander, who reported me to the battalion commander, and I end up at this formal hearing where they make me listen to all this awful shit about myself. And then they asked me if I had anything to say. I’m pretty sure that I was supposed to keep quiet, but I had typed out this whole speech about how my senior drill sergeant didn’t embody Army values. So I read my speech, and when I finished, everyone was pretty mad. A command sergeant major started screaming in my face. He looked like Clint Eastwood if Clint Eastwood was only five feet tall. After he was done yelling, he ripped my insignia off my uniform, escorted me from the room, and with a mix of disgust and pride, said: ‘You’ve got some balls.’”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhQYFjqTE&u=005trlAagw1f9u9p0lmlzj31kw11xqa7 )

>  “我在学做一名顾问，妇女家庭暴力方面的，因为还在学，还没接过什么实际的案子。但最终我想帮那些受虐的妇女们清楚地认识到她们所处的状况。70%的家庭暴力都不为人知，妇女们选择沉默的原因很多：有些是缺乏自尊，觉得自己别无选择；有些就只是害怕；而很多人是真的爱着对方，她们一厢情愿地以为‘这只是个阶段’，认为忍一忍就过去了。这其中有很多理想化的成份。现在我在一家新娘美容院工作，在店里我们从来不叫女士们‘客户’，就叫她们‘新娘’。因为新娘这个身份很特殊，而结婚就是美梦成真。当她们试装时，你能从她们的脸上看到这一点——她们感觉自己终于找到了今后的幸福。所以，将来即便遭遇了家庭暴力，要让她们放弃这种想法真的会很难。”小编@人在深圳 “I’m studying to be a counselor for battered and abused women. I haven’t had any actual cases yet because I’m still learning. But eventually I want to help abused women clearly understand the situation that they’re in. Seventy percent of cases go unreported. There are a lot of reasons that women don’t speak out. Some have low self-esteem and feel like they have no other options. Some are afraid. But a lot of women just genuinely love their partners, and they convince themselves that it’s ‘just a phase.’ They think that things will get better. There can be a lot of idealism involved. I work at a bridal salon now. At our shop, we never call women ‘customers.’ We always call them ‘brides.’ Because brides are special. Marriage is a dream come true. I can see it in the brides' faces when they try on their dresses. They feel like they’ve finally found their ‘happily ever after.’ And it can be hard to give up on that idea. Even if they’re being abused.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhQs5jXQh&u=005trlAagw1f9u6wn7ng8j31kw11xn34 )

>  “我来自北卡罗来纳州的一个小镇，我们毕业的那个班只有5个人出来了。说是出来了，可我仍然一事无成，那感觉就像：嗯我曾有一个梦想，可它竟然狗屁不是。现在一说起自己，我真是无话可说，当人家问我在干啥，我竟无言以对。想想上大学时，我可以说我是个学生，在学影视专业。但现在我只是个实习生，在一个食品店里打工。跟人说起这个真是羞于启齿，我都有点害怕去见生人了。我也不知道为什么，和我一起工作的人都挺好，也都上过学，个个胸怀梦想，虽然我不会因为他们在一个食品店打工而觉得他们如何如何，但一说起自己，我还是会烦躁不安。”小编@人在深圳 “I grew up in a small town in North Carolina. Only five people in my graduating class even left the town. And I left but I haven’t done anything. I feel like: ‘Yah, I had this dream, but it was bullshit.’ And now there’s nothing to say about me. When people ask what I'm doing, there's nothing to say. Back when I was in college, I could say that I was a student. I was majoring in film and television. But now I’m just doing an internship and working at a grocery store. And it bothers me to tell people that. I’m actually afraid to meet new people. And I don’t know why. Because everyone who works with me is nice and educated and has dreams. And I don’t judge them for working at a grocery store. Yet it bothers me to tell people that about myself.”

>  “成功对我来说仿佛会侵犯别人，感觉像我在踢别人的小腿。我就要拿到硕士学位，但我家人都还在生存线上挣扎：我妈妈高中辍学，我的双胞胎弟弟自杀了，我家人都没钱。所以任何时候成功在即，我就感觉我把自己弄得高高在上，而把家人抛在了身后。这让我焦虑，我不希望自己比家人感觉更良好，所以通常我就会自暴自弃，又把自己打回原地。”小编@人在深圳 “Success feels like an aggressive act to me. It feels like I’m kicking someone in the shins. I’m about to get my masters degree, but the rest of my family is struggling to survive. My mom is a high school dropout. My twin brother committed suicide. Nobody in my family has money. So whenever I start to succeed, it feels like I’m putting myself on a pedestal and leaving them behind. It causes anxiety. I don’t like to feel better than them. So I usually self-sabotage and knock myself back down.”

>  “几个月前我朋友在游泳池里淹死了，当时我也在场，我们是出去玩，我在做吃的，出去打了个电话，等我回来，他已经脸朝下沉在水底。我只离开了几分钟，都不知道发生了什么，他也从没跟我说他不会游泳。我试了心肺复苏，救护车来时他还活着。我一个劲儿为他祈祷，给每个认识的人打电话，请他们一起祈祷，我还打了祈祷专线，大家都在教堂为他祈祷。我希望一切OK，这只是上帝对我的一次考验。我多希望自己能说：‘我把此生献给了上帝，奇迹终于发生了。’ 但我朋友还是走了，实际上我在祈祷时他已经去世了。这件事让我困惑不已，因为就在这之前，我曾感觉自己和上帝是如此接近：我去教堂做义工；做周中服务；我在阅读；捐钱多了；派对少了；我积极向上，处处留心，少说脏话。感觉自己和上帝是如此接近，在地铁站台上站着时我都感觉能跟他对话了。但最近一切都变难了，读圣经变得不再轻松，我也很怕再祈求任何事情，早上醒来我还是会说‘感谢上帝’，但除此之外的，变得很难了。”小编@人在深圳 “A few months ago, my friend drowned in a swimming pool while I was with him. We were just hanging out. I was cooking for us. Then I stepped away to take a phone call, and when I came back, he was face down at the bottom of the pool. I was only gone for a few minutes. I don’t even know what happened. He never told me that he couldn’t swim. I tried CPR and he was still alive when the ambulance came. I prayed so hard. I called everyone I knew and asked them to pray. I called prayer lines. Everyone prayed for him at church. I was hoping that everything would be OK and that this could just be part of my testimony. I was hoping I could say: ‘I dedicated my life to God, and here’s what happened.’ But my friend passed away. He’d actually been dead the entire time I was praying. And it’s been so confusing for me. Because right before this happened, I’d been feeling so close to God. I was volunteering at church. I was going to midweek services. I was reading books. I was giving more of my money. I was partying less. I was trying to stay positive, and be mindful, and use less bad words. And I felt so close to God. I’d have conversations with him while standing on the subway platform. But it’s been hard lately. It’s hard to read my Bible verses. I’m scared to ask for anything. I say ‘thank you’ when I wake up every morning, but anything beyond that is very difficult.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhOM54oZG&u=005trlAagw1f9tzd1fbfjj31kw11xjuu )

>  “十年前有个纪录片叫《不影响环境的人》(No Impact Man)，我是他们的拍摄对象——我尝试生活一年，尽可能少地对环境产生不良影响：去哪儿我们家都骑自行车，也不用纸制品。片子上映后很受人关注，它的成功让我无所适从。那之前我写过两本关于历史的书，都还不错，但看的人不多。突然之间，有人来采访我，表示祝贺，还请我上'早安美国'。再后来就开始有人攻击我，搞客（Gawker，美国八卦网站）上登了几篇文章说我故作清高、投机取巧，还说我把自己的价值观强加给家人。还有人说我根本就不是关心环境，只是为了赚钱。所有这些关注真的给我带来一种危机——平生第一次，我的‘人格’不再是我本人，真是让人心累：人家当我是英雄，我就想证明他们是对的；人家当我是孬种，我就想证明他们是错的。我反复自省，才认识到我谁都不是。人是很丰富的，可以博大精深，也可以细致入微，很难下定义。同样，你不可能就只是个英雄或孬种，一个词概括不了一个人。”小编@人在深圳 “Ten years ago I was the subject of a documentary called ‘No Impact Man.’ It was about my attempt to live for an entire year with as little environmental impact as possible. My family rode bikes everywhere. We used no paper products. And the film got quite a lot of attention. I wasn’t used to the success. I’d written two history books before then. And they were good books, but they didn’t have much of a readership. Now all of the sudden I was being interviewed, and celebrated, and invited on Good Morning America. And then people started attacking me. Gawker wrote several articles calling me self-righteous, and an opportunist, and said I was imposing my values on my family. People said I didn’t care about the environment and only wanted to make money. And all the attention really caused a crisis for me. For the first time, I had a personhood that was completely different than my person. And that was exhausting. When someone called me a hero, I wanted to prove them right. When someone called me a devil, I wanted to prove them wrong. It took a lot of self-examination to realize that I was neither. There is a fullness to a person that is gigantic and nuanced and indefinable. It was equally impossible to be a hero or a devil. I couldn’t be contained by a single word.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhNNVEhF4&u=005trlAagw1f9tv2jdaajj31kw11xaja )

>  “几年前我不得不做心脏直视手术，当从医生那儿得到这个消息，我完全进入了恐慌模式——突然世界上一切都消停了，除了我的恐惧。我以为我会在我的孩子们面前崩溃。我独自走进那家书店，寻找任何能让我平静下来的东西。最终我找到一本叫《活在当下》(The Power of Now)的书，很难形容当时那种感觉，但它教会了我如何活在当下，教会我要退后一步，静思细想，把‘思想’梳理出来，并在我和我‘内心的声音’之间保持一个距离，一旦我发现我从那种想法中抽离，它就变得不再那么恐惧。这张照片是手术前一小时拍的，我和孙子在一起，那一刻我心中不再有恐惧，我和他就那样被定格在那里。”小编@人在深圳 “A few years ago I had to have open-heart surgery. When I got the news from my cardiologist, I went into full panic mode. Suddenly there was nothing going on in the world except for my fear. I thought that I was going to fall apart in front of my kids. I ended up walking to the bookstore alone. I was looking for anything that might help calm me down. And I ended up grabbing The Power of Now. It’s not an easy thing to describe in words, but that book taught me how to stay in the moment. It taught me to step back and observe my thoughts, to label them as ‘thoughts,’ and to create a gap between myself and the ‘voice in my head.’ Once I realized that I am separate from my thoughts, it took away their power. This photo was taken an hour before the surgery. I’m with my grandson. And there isn’t a fear in my mind. I’m locked in that moment with him.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhNxM1GZT&u=005trlAagw1f9tu88rjc2j31kw11x42a )
