>  “当时是刚看完一场音乐会，我跟朋友正走路回家，这时过来两个警察——我们没大声喧哗，也没喝酒，但他们还是跟我朋友说他们要搜身。他们说他们在找一个5尺10寸高的黑人男子，凑巧这一片多数人都符合这一特征。那是个借口而已，这样他们就能搜查每一个街上的黑人男性了。那让人很不爽，我朋友可是个空乘，有大学学历的，穿的是领扣紧扣的带领衬衫。他想问为什么，但我跟他说别吭声，他们让你做什么你就做什么。我不想让事情闹大，不想看到他们掏枪，更不想让我朋友成为网上一个新的话题标签。”小编@人在深圳 “My friend and I were walking home from watching live music, and two police officers approached us. We weren’t being loud. We weren’t drunk. But they told my friend they needed to search him. They told us they were looking for a 5’10” black male, which happens to be the description of most men in this neighborhood. So that’s an excuse to search every black male who walks down the street. And that’s not right. My friend was a flight attendant. He had a college degree. He was wearing a button down collared shirt. He tried to ask, ‘Why?’ But I told him to be quiet. I told him to do as he was told. Because I didn’t want to escalate. I didn’t want the guns to come out. I didn’t want him to be another hashtag.”

>  “18轮的大卡车，我开了15年。有一天我撞了一位女士的本田思域，我压根儿就没看见她，还以为爆胎了呢。幸运的是没人受伤，但我发现我的视力开始下降。现在我的左眼已经失明大概七年，这对我的自尊心打击很大：过去我是很开朗的一个人，跟谁都能说得上话。现在呢，一碰到生人，感觉他们都不知道该往哪儿看好。他们的目光就那样来回扫，有时干脆盯着地，或者看向远处。朋友们都说只有我才这么介意，说我多虑了，但我又在想他们是不是只是为了安慰我，所以才那样说。”小编@人在深圳 “I drove an eighteen-wheeler for fifteen years. One day I hit a lady in a Honda Civic. I hadn’t seen her at all. I just thought I’d blown a tire. Luckily nobody was hurt, but I realized my vision was starting to go. I’ve been blind in my left eye for about seven years now. It’s been really hard on my self-esteem. I used to be very outgoing and would talk to anyone. Now when I first meet somebody new, it’s like they don’t know where to look. Their eyes go back and forth. Sometimes they’ll just look straight at the ground or off in the distance. My friends tell me that I’m the only one that cares about it. They tell me that I worry about it more than anyone else. But then I wonder if they’re just telling me that to make me feel better.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhIbtmuz6&u=005trlAagw1f9t6pqa942j31kw11xgr0 )

>  “25年前离的婚，他有了外遇，丢下了我和两个年幼的孩子。我花了很多时间很多年，但现在已经走出去了。为了孩子，我决定接受现实。他娶了那个女人，我们也重新聚在一起了，像一家人那样，虽然这对我来说仍然并不轻松。母亲节我是在孩子们的继母家里过的，很别扭，但我不想孩子们每次跟他爸爸度个假都担心伤害我的感情，我也不想让他们觉得什么都要分别庆祝两次，比如每个生日，或者大学毕业典礼，或者结婚。我女儿刚生了，这会儿大家都来了，因为有些并发症，大家都在照顾她。我忘不了25年前发生的事情，但像这种时候，我得表现得像没事人一样。”小编@人在深圳 “I got divorced twenty-five years ago. He had an affair. He left me with two small kids. It took a lot of time and a lot of years, but I’m OK with it now. For the sake of my kids, I made the decision to be OK with it. He’s married to the woman now. And we all get together as a family. It’s still not easy for me. I spent Mother’s Day at their stepmother’s house. That was weird. But I don’t want my kids to worry about hurting my feelings every time they spend a holiday with him. I don’t want them to feel like they need to have two separate celebration dinners for every birthday, or when they graduate from college, or get married. My daughter just had a baby, so we’re actually all in town together right now. There have been some complications so everyone is supporting her. I haven’t forgotten what happened twenty-five years ago, but for times like this, I need to be OK with it.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhI0ynMwO&u=005trlAagw1f9t5xv1mhkj31kw11xdja )

>  “在艺术方面我真是心碎了——我想成为一名电影演员，我想用我对艺术的敏锐来改变这个世界，但在意大利它是个封闭的体制，一年大概只有五部电影，根本没试镜的机会，想得到个角色，你必须得是导演的朋友。所以我去了英国，但那差点毁了我。在英国他们老让我演老外，通常我是个黑手党，但也演各种老外：西班牙服务生、土耳其服务生、法国服务生，他们还老让我戴胡子。所以我才来了美国。我申请的杰出人才签证，花了6000刀，光申请资料就有一本书那么厚，我得交十封推荐信，来证明我有多杰出。那玩意儿净是骗人的，照样没人关心你，也没哪家电视台会因此给你面试机会，人人都只认绿卡。我只能在一些小制作里找点活儿干，但现在好点了，我开始演些小角色。虽然还是演流氓，但有时我是搞笑的流氓，或者是有点感觉的流氓。我的下个角色是个科学家，他变成了僵尸。那电影里每个陌生人都像僵尸，但又没人真的是。陌生人像僵尸，嘿，有点道德的意味哈！”小编@人在深圳 “I’m artistically brokenhearted. I wanted to be a screen actor. I wanted to change the world through my sensitivity. But it was a very closed system in Italy. There are only like five movies per year. And there aren’t exactly auditions. You must be friends with the director to get a role. So I tried going to Britain. And that almost destroyed me. I was always cast as a foreigner. Usually I was a Mafioso, but I played all types of foreigners. I’ve been a Spanish waiter, a Turkish waiter, and a French waiter. And they were always making me wear a mustache. So I tried for America. I applied for an ‘extraordinary talent visa.’ It cost me $6,000. The application was the size of a book. I had to submit ten letters of recommendation to prove that I was extraordinary. What a scam that was. Nobody cares that I’m extraordinary. None of the television stations will audition people with this visa. Everyone wants to see a green card. I can only work on small productions. But things have gotten a little better. I’m getting some minor roles. I’m still playing gangsters. But sometimes I’m the funny gangster. Or the gangster with some sense. My next role is a scientist who turns into a zombie. In the movie, every stranger appears to be a zombie. But nobody is really a zombie. Strangers just seem like zombies. So, hey, there’s a moral message there.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhFQbzNTS&u=005trlAagw1f9svwvx4p5j31kw11xdkw )

>  “我是一个法律援助协会的调查员，我们给那些请不起律师的人提供合法辩护。我大学学的法律，但现行的机制跟学校教我们的还不太一样。理论上说，被告总是处于有利位置，除非被证明有罪，否则我们的当事人应该是无辜的。而公诉人有搜集证据的责任。但那只是理论，现实是：为了取得最大的优势，区代理人篡改了规则。他们关心的不是正义——嗯，应该说有些人是关心的，但我看到的都只在乎输赢。因为那个职位是竞选上来的，所以他们想要选民看到他们会严惩犯罪，这就要求更高的收监率，这就激发他们尽可能给更多的人定罪。他们最爱用的一招就是过度起诉，他们可能起诉十项罪名，但其中九项法庭都不会受理，可当事人冒不起这个险啊，这样当事人就会选择认罪，哪怕那项罪名跟案子只是沾边儿。现在我们就有个当事人，他喝多了，烂醉如泥，在地铁上。只是个简单的公共场合醉酒的起诉吧，但他的啤酒瓶从座位上掉下来摔碎了，于是他们就起诉他公共场合持械。他们也知道这很荒唐，但他们也很清楚当事人决不想为了这项罪名而对簿公堂，然后当事人就会认了那些他该认的罪。而这，正是他们想要的结果。”小编@人在深圳 “I work as an investigator for the Legal Aid Society. We provide legal defense to people who can’t afford it. I studied law in college, but I’m learning that the system doesn’t match up to what we were taught. According to theory, the defendant should always have the advantage. Our clients are supposed to be innocent until proven guilty. The burden of proof lies with the prosecutor. But that’s only in theory. In reality, the District Attorneys bend the rules of the system to gain maximum leverage. They don’t care about justice-- well, I’m sure there are some that do-- but the ones I’ve seen only care about winning. It’s an elected position, so they want to show voters that they are ‘tough on crime.’ And that requires higher incarceration rates. So they are incentivized to convict as many people as possible. One of their favorite weapons is to overcharge. They’ll charge a defendant with ten things. Nine of them would easily get thrown out in court, but the client just can’t risk it. So they’ll plead guilty to the one charge that even remotely applies to the case. We’re representing one client who passed out on the subway. It’s a simple public intoxication charge. But his beer bottle fell off his seat and broke, so they charged him with possession of a weapon. They know it’s ridiculous. But they know he’ll never go to trial with that charge on the table. So they’ll get their conviction. And that’s all that matters.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ehz35DrMv&u=005trlAagw1f9s2b884hmj31kw11xag8 )

>  “14岁那年父母把我从危地马拉带到这里的。七十年代移民不像现在是多大个事，来纽约后我曾加入一个足球队，队友来自十个国家呢。那时你去上班就是了，也没人问这问那。我妈就在希尔顿酒店做客房服务，一做四十年。我算幸运的，没吃多大苦，上飞机就来了。但今非昔比，现在就像人们说的，你得躲进边境的灌木丛，狂奔穿越沙漠，还得游泳过河，而这只是为了来美国挣钱养家糊口。我为他们感到难过。现在拉美人移民太难了，你可以抱怨，但从这儿有第一个感恩节就是这样：先是爱尔兰人，后来是波兰人，再后来是意大利人，二战时又是日本人，现在又轮到我们拉美人了。就是这样，谁来得晚，谁赔碎盘子。”小编@人在深圳 “My parents brought me from Guatemala when I was fourteen. Immigration wasn’t as big of a deal back in the 70’s. When I got to New York, I joined a soccer team with players from ten different countries. And you could just go to work and nobody asked any questions. My mother worked as a housekeeper at the Hilton for forty years. I was lucky. I didn’t have too hard of a time. I got to come over on a plane. But today it’s different. Right now, as we speak, people are hiding in bushes by the border. They’re running through deserts and swimming across rivers just to feed their families. I feel very bad for them. Things are very tough for the Latino immigrant. But it’s our turn. The last one to arrive has to pay for the broken dishes. You’ve got to blame somebody for the problems. It’s been like that since the first Thanksgiving. First it was the Irish, then the Polish, then the Italians. When the war came it was the Japanese. It’s just our turn.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhyQKms98&u=005trlAagw1f9s1d9ysx9j31kw11xdqp )

>  “我对电过敏，只要周围有电，就感觉像一千只蝎子在螫我，就像圣经里每一处对炼狱的描述。可是你又无处可逃，因为它无处不在。我只好在夹缝中求生，我记下了很多安全的地方，这附近的门廊我都试过了，这儿特别好，因为有很多铁栏杆插在地上。我穿了七层屏蔽服，还有纯银平角裤，还有导电袜。没人肯保护我，因为他们认为这都是我的凭空想象。他们认为他们可以决定我能吸收多少。有些人甚至用手机指我，虽然他们没打我，但那感觉就像他们在用拳头打我。即使我解释了这其中的科学原理，他们也觉得是我疯了。顽固得让人恼火。因为即使我不提所有这些量化的证据，只说我相信它伤害了我——好吧，我有权选择让自己暴露在多少电磁辐射中。”小编@人在深圳 [吃惊]“I have electrosensitivity. When I’m exposed to electricity, it’s like one thousand scorpions stinging me. It’s like every description of fire in the bible. There is no ‘off the grid.’ Because the grid is everywhere. So I live ‘between the grid.’ I have a lot of memorized safe spaces. I’ve tested all the stoops in the neighborhood, and this is an especially good one because it has a lot of wrought iron going into the ground. I wear seven layers of shielding clothes. I wear silver sterling boxers. I wear conductive socks. And nobody protects me because they think I’m imagining things. They think that they can decide how much I can take. Some people even point their cell phones at me. It’s like they’re punching me without punching me. Even after I explain the science, I get pigeonholed as crazy. The bigotry is maddening. Because even if I remove all my quantified evidence, and I say that I believe it hurts me-- that should be fine. I have the right to choose how much radiation I’m exposed to.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhyBf78nL&u=005trlAagw1f9rzt6ynoij31kw11xgt3 )

>  “九年级时情况开始变得很糟：跟人握手会感觉不舒服；也不能摸钱；如果餐具碰到了桌子，吃饭会吃不下去；尤其是门把手，最恐怖，摸它们感觉像是摸到了狗便便；最后连最爱的巴松管我都不吹了，床成了唯一让我感觉安全的地方。我一周不下床，学也不上了，还曾经一个月足不出户。我先后三次被送进精神病院，老实说，那反而是种解脱，像是对现实的一种逃离。现在能这样，我挺开心的，虽然还在吃很多药，但我好多了：一周出两次门，刚上完一堂巴松管课，很快就要去实习，我也正申请今年秋天去读音乐学院。”小编@人在深圳 “It started getting really bad in ninth grade. Shaking hands became uncomfortable. I couldn’t touch money. I couldn’t eat with utensils if they had touched the table. Door knobs were the worst. Touching them felt like touching dog poop. It got to the point where I couldn’t even play bassoon, and that’s what I love the most. My bed became my only safe space. I’d stay in bed for a week at a time. I dropped out of school. Once I didn’t leave the house for an entire month. I got committed to a psychiatric hospital three different times, and honestly that was a relief. It was like an escape from existing. But I’m happy with where I am now. I’m on so many medications but I’m doing much better. I’m leaving the house twice a week. I just finished a bassoon lesson. I’m starting an internship soon. And I’m applying to music schools this fall.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhxrQ2H1S&u=005trlAagw1f9rvklwt19j31hj0zpdm6 )

>  “感觉一天比一天糟——我正准备搬家，跟她爸出了点问题，第一次要靠自己，我都不知道我们将会住在哪里。但她总是想办法哄我开心：有一次她画了一道彩虹，放进邮箱，然后说我收到一封邮件。看见我在母亲节哭，她说：‘有我呢妈妈，妈妈你最好了，我会永远抱着你。’ 她在《嘎巴宝宝》里学了首歌，这样唱的：‘如果你试试，你就会喜欢’。然后这就成了她鼓励我的话，当我没勇气起床面对生活的时候。”小编@人在深圳 “Every day seems like a new low. I’m currently going through a transition with housing. I’ve got issues with her father. I’m on my own for the first time. I don’t even know where we’re going to live. But she’s always trying to cheer me up. One time she drew a rainbow, and put it in the mailbox, and told me I had mail. When she saw me crying on Mother’s Day, she said: ‘I got you, Mommy. You’re the best Mommy ever and I’m always going to hold you down.’ And she learned this song from the show Yo Gabba Gabba. It goes: ‘If you try it, you’ll like it.’ So that’s what she says to me whenever I feel like I can’t get out of bed.”

>  “我最大的烦恼是我都快要死了，却还没去做那些我想做的事。搞笑的是——我甚至都还没弄清楚有多少事是我想去做的，直到癌症确诊。简单些的比如：遇见个意中人、结婚、找份工作、有一间自己的公寓，甚至自己挑家具。这些过去都不吸引我，它们就像是大人们才会干的，反正迟早都会发生。但现在我超想去做，我想知道那感觉如何。”“My biggest worry is that I’m going to die and not do all the things I wanted to do. The funny thing is—I didn’t even realize how many things I wanted to do until I got diagnosed. Simple things like meeting a guy, getting married, getting a job, having my own apartment, and even picking out my own furniture. Those never seemed too interesting to me. They just seemed like adult things that were guaranteed to happen. Now I want to do them so bad. Because I want to know what they feel like.”Brandon:“I’m very sorry to report that shortly after her story was published, Sara’s cancer returned very aggressively. >  “那时我到了什么地步——去商店偷，打碎车玻璃偷，就差卖淫了。我露宿街头，有时几个星期都不洗澡。有天走在149号街，经过林肯医院时，我撞上了一个医药顾问，Crespo先生，他带我去弄了些吃的，还给了我些钱。他告诉我我不必再这样生活，第二天我就去了他说的美沙酮诊所。现在我不吸海洛因了，服美沙酮。也说不上好坏吧，至少这是医生开的药，而不是从毒贩那儿来的，也不用再嗑了上顿没下顿。现在我能工作，还能自己付账单，靠谱、有用了。美沙酮不像海洛因那么嗨，但也能过瘾，可它就像个液体的手铐，因为脱瘾过程太难受了，24小时不服药，骨头里就像着了火。他们每次只给一次的剂量，所以我得每天早上6点去诊所报到，到那儿你就会发现：已经有100号人在那儿排队了。”小编@人在深圳 “It got to the point where I was stealing from stores, breaking into car windows-- everything but prostitution. I was living in the streets. Sometimes I wouldn’t shower for weeks at a time. Then one day I was walking down 149th by Lincoln Hospital, and I bumped into a drug counselor named Mr. Crespo. He took me to get some food. He gave me a few dollars. And he told me that I didn’t have to live like this anymore. I went to the methadone clinic the next day. And now I’m hooked on that instead of heroin. It’s a mixed blessing. At least it’s coming from a doctor and not a pusher. I always know where my next fix is coming from. I can work now. I can pay bills. I can be reliable and productive. It doesn’t get you high like heroin, but it takes away the urges. But it’s like liquid handcuffs because the withdrawals are just as bad. If I stop for twenty-four hours, it feels like fire in my bones. And they only give you one dose a time. So I get to the clinic every morning at 6 AM, and there are already one hundred people in line.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhuZneVeI&u=005trlAagw1f9rkca0zv7j31kw11xdjk )

>  “我们在摇摆舞班上认识的，接下来两个月经常在一起：一起去喝东西，一起去音乐节，一起去散步。但什么都没发生，连个吻都没有。我快疯了，老跟闺蜜在电话里分析，想弄清楚他到底是咋回事。我觉得我的意思已经很明显了啊。然后，有天晚上我豁出去了，给他做饭，一气儿烧了五道菜，我们喝了好多酒，最后一起窝进沙发，就这还是什么都没发生！““那天晚上我走后才意识到我可能该吻她，从她脸上的表情判断出来的。但是，嘿，我是个现代人，女方也可以主动点。再加上我的上一段关系让我很受伤。但两个晚上以后我就弥补过来了。我们去一家意大利餐馆庆祝她生日，有个服务生给了她一个生日之吻，结果一下又窜出四个服务生来亲她，我有点嫉妒了，喝了好多香槟。晚饭后我们去了一家夜店，这时Nelly Furtado的《坏女孩》响起，我又练过摇摆舞，所以我就这样搂着她，来吧！”小编@人在深圳 “We met at a swing dance class. For the next two months, we spent a lot of time together: we went out for drinks, went to music festivals, went for walks around town. But nothing was happening. Not even a kiss. It was driving me crazy. I was always on the phone with my friends, trying to figure this guy out. I thought I was being pretty obvious. Then one night I pulled out all the stops. I cooked him a five course meal, we drank a lot of wine, and we ended up on the couch together. But still nothing!”“I realized after I left that night that I probably should have kissed her. Something about the look on her face. But hey, I’m a modern guy. A woman can make the first move. Plus my last relationship had hurt me a lot. But I made up for it two nights later. We went out to an Italian restaurant for her birthday. And one of the waiters gave her a birthday kiss. Then suddenly four more waiters are giving her birthday kisses. And I’m feeling a little jealous. And I’m drinking a lot of champagne. Then after dinner we went out to a club. And ‘Promiscuous Girl’ comes on by Nelly Furtado. And I’d been practicing my swing dancing. So I twirled her around like this. And then boom.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ehuyr9PII&u=005trlAagw1f9ri68v9z6j31kw11xai4 )

>  “那时我想成为重量级拳击冠军，Joe Louis是我的偶像。早在40年代，一个黑人像他那样人尽皆知真的很了不起。他是当时最受欢迎的黑人男子，他让你觉得你可以站起来，为了你自己，保护你自己。我17岁开始训练，第一场比赛是对阵一个白人，一分半钟不到，两拳，他就倒下了。用你的拳头把别人打得晕头转向满地找牙，当你知道你有这样的力量，那感觉棒极了！电影里谁最招人待见、观众最喜欢？赢得战斗的人，保护女人的人，保卫自己的人。”译者@人在深圳 “I wanted to be heavyweight champion. Joe Louis was my idol. Back in the forties, it was really something for a black person to have that kind of notoriety. He was the most popular black man alive. He made you feel like you could stand up for yourself. Protect yourself. I started training when I was seventeen. The first fight I had was with a Caucasian guy. It lasted less than a minute and a half. Two punches and he was down. It’s quite a feeling to knock somebody unconscious with your fists. To know you have that power. Who’s the person in the movie that everyone loves? It’s the one who wins the fight. The one who protects the woman. The one who protects himself.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhukOBDU9&u=005trlAagw1f9rhfn3sr4j31kw11xn1t )

>  “我21岁去的社区大学，当时我幡然醒悟，发现自己整日无所事事，一事无成——之前我每晚出去喝酒，一喝喝到凌晨四点；在做零售；约会的是个大人渣。我跟他说我想去念书，他说：‘现实点行不，你永远都考不过的，别浪费时间了。’ 所以一开始我想回去学校就是想证明别人是错的。我一堂课不拉，作业写得老认真，而不是胡七马抓敷衍了事。虽然很辛苦，但我发现我喜欢那种取得好成绩的感觉。然后我才真正为了自己而念书。以前我从未回头检讨过自己的过去。记得第一年有门课是人类学，有次作业是写一篇关于纽约夜生活的文，我就去了以前我每晚都去的那间酒吧，没喝酒，就在那儿看着，边看边做笔记。我看见个女孩在那儿玩啤酒乒乓（beer pong, 一种喝酒游戏），她跟我年龄相仿，一幅玩世不恭的样子，醉醺醺的，站都站不稳。她还没意识到那些男生为啥对她那么好，她花的钱估计也不是她自己挣的。那一刻我很庆幸，庆幸我不再是她，不再是那样一个女孩。”小编@人在深圳 “I went to community college when I was twenty-one. I just had an epiphany that I wasn’t really doing anything with my life. I was staying out drinking until 4 AM every night. I was working retail. I was dating a guy who was a total douchebag. When I told him I wanted to go to college, he told me ‘Let’s be real. You’re never going to pass. Don’t waste your time.’ So at the beginning my whole motivation for going back to school was to prove people wrong. I went to all my classes. I turned in well-written papers, not bullshit ones. And it was hard, but I discovered that I liked the feeling of making good grades. So I started doing it for myself. And I never looked back. I remember taking an anthropology course that first year, and one of my assignments was to write a paper on New York City nightlife. I went to the same bar that I used to go to every night. Except I wasn’t drinking. I was just watching and taking notes. And I saw this girl my age playing beer pong, and she didn’t have a care in the world, and she was stumbling around, and she didn’t realize why the guys were being so nice to her, and she was probably spending money that she didn’t have. And I remember feeling so glad that I wasn’t that girl anymore.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhpGr0H5E&u=005trlAagw1f9qx4sg5fmj31kw11xaha )

>  “我从不表露自己的感情，我们全家人都这样，老藏着掖着。我想是它让我成为一名好的急诊护士——从不把工作上的事带回家；可以在情感上抽离，只专注于要做的事。但它同时也使我在人际关系上很糟糕：去年在欧洲旅行时我遇到了Gavin，我们一起旅行了两周，他回来后还见了我的家人，然后我们还去了墨西哥一周。之后我们每天都说话。Gavin跟我正相反，他是个暖男，快乐而敏感，他甚至会跟陌生人说你看起来很棒。但当我们走得太近时，我退缩了，我不喜欢那种依赖别人的感觉。今年一月底Gavin在一次车祸中去世了，当时他独自一人在英国，我甚至都没及时发现，直到他去世后几天。我试图来面对这件事，就像一直以来的那样，尽力不去想或谈起它。但这次不灵了，这次我把工作变得更带个人感情了。如果一个病人在急诊室，受了类似的伤，我就总是问自己：‘如果这是Gavin呢？’”小编@人在深圳 “I don’t communicate my feelings. My entire family was like that. We’ve always sort of just swept things under the rug. I think that’s what makes me a good ER nurse. I don’t take things home with me. I can separate myself emotionally and just focus on what needs to be done. But it also makes me pretty bad at relationships. I met Gavin while traveling in Europe last year. We traveled together for two weeks, then he came home and met my family, and then we went to Mexico for a week. After that we talked every day. Gavin was the opposite of me. He was warm and happy and touchy. He’d even tell random strangers that they looked nice. But I pulled back the moment we got too close. Because I don’t like the feeling of being dependent on someone. Gavin was killed in a car crash at the end of January. He was alone in England and I didn’t even find out until days after it happened. I’ve tried to handle it like I always do. I try not to think about it or talk about it. But it’s not working so well this time. I’m taking things more personally at work. If a patient comes in the ER with similar injuries, I always ask myself: ‘What if this was Gavin?’”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhpfZkAaO&u=005trlAagw1f9qvbw3173j31kw11xgr6 )

>  “那是八年级升九年级的暑假，我们是那种搂搂抱抱的亲密伙伴，有时他会跟我说说话什么的。有天晚上，在他家的地下室，当时已经比较晚了，而且我们还喝了酒，他不停地问我想不想，我的心怦怦直跳，害怕得要命，我说：‘或许吧，或许吧，或许吧’，然后他说：‘哪有那么多或许，不如我们掷个硬币。’ 我的心一沉……做完以后，他说：‘我听到我爸在楼上，你得走了。’ 然后我就回家了，在日记里写了满满一页，用紫色三福笔，写了一遍又一遍：就当什么都没发生。好长一段时间，我都不开心，觉得那是我的错，然后我又觉得自己太敏感了。我花了五年，才意识到当时的那个决定真不是掷硬币那么简单。”小编@人在深圳   “It was the summer between 8th and 9th grade. We were make-out buddies. Sometimes he’d talk to me during the day. Other times he wouldn’t. We were in his basement late one night, getting drunk, and he kept asking me if I wanted to do it. My heart was racing and I was terrified. I kept saying: ‘maybe,’ ‘maybe,’ ‘maybe.’ Then he said: ‘No more maybes. Let’s flip a coin.’ My stomach sank. After we finished, he said: ‘I think I heard my dad upstairs. You need to leave.’ I went home and filled up a whole page in my journal. I wrote in purple sharpie, over and over: ‘It didn’t happen.’ For the longest time I felt like it was my fault for feeling hurt. Like I was being overly sensitive. It took five years for me to realize that consent is not a coin flip.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhoToFS1n&u=005trlAagw1f9qtf1qn1wj31kw11xwkd )

>  “我爸是个法西斯，他在墨索里尼的部队里被训练成了一个恐怖分子。他简直是反人类：爱尔兰人他叫爱尔兰佬，黑人他叫黑鬼，犹太人他叫犹太佬。他的主要武器就是痛苦：他蹂躏我，把我锁进储藏室，用扫帚把打我，还把我送去医院好多次，还威胁我说要当街打爆我的头。我吸收了很多他的坏情绪，有时我也会发出他的那种声音。当我恼羞成怒骂骂咧咧时，我听起来就像他一样，那是他钻在我的身体里跟我说话。但我没有变成他，是我爷爷挽救了我。我奶奶也是个法西斯，跟我爸一个样，她能一边手捻玫瑰念珠一边咒骂这个世界。但我爷爷是个简单的人，他和我们住在一起，他拥抱我亲吻我，总是跟我说：‘你爸是个疯子’。我就这样摇摆在两个极端：一头是爷爷的爱，一头是爸爸的恨。我爷爷知道如何去爱，但我爸爸不懂得爱，因为他的心被恐惧占满了。15岁那年，有一次我走过去给了我爸爸一个大大的拥抱，可他就那样耷拉着胳膊，手臂僵硬。我说‘我爱你爸爸’，他身体开始发抖。他身体里有个被吓坏的孩子，他想去爱，也想被爱，只是不知道该如何去爱。”小编@人在深圳     “My father was a fascist. He was trained to be a terrorist in Mussolini’s army. He was anti-everybody. The Irish were ‘micks,’ black people were ‘niggers,’ and Jewish people were ‘kikes.’ His main weapon was pain. He raped me, locked me in closets, beat me with broom handles. He sent me to the hospital many times. He'd threaten to blow my brains out in the middle of the street. I absorbed a lot of his emotional energy. Sometimes his voice still comes out of me. When I’m really angry, and cussing myself out, I sound just like him. It’s him inside me, speaking to me. But I didn’t become him. My grandfather saved me. My grandmother was a fascist like my father. She counted her rosary beads and condemned the world, but my grandfather was a simple man. He lived with us. He always told me: ‘Your father is a nut.’ He hugged me and kissed me. I swung between two extremes: the love of my grandfather and the hate of my father. My grandfather knew how to love. My father couldn’t love because he was too filled with terror. He didn’t have the tools to love. Once when I was fifteen, I walked over to my father and gave him a big hug. He kept his arms stiff by his side. I said ‘I love you Dad,’ and his body started trembling. There was a terrified child inside of him. He wanted to love. And he wanted to be loved. He just didn’t know how.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhojdjPd1&u=005trlAagw1f9qquqmb20j31kw11x47n )

>  “三年前我停止嗑药的，当时我已经到了一种绝望的境地：知道自己不对，可就是停不下来。有天早上我哥叫我跟他一起去教堂，从那儿我认了上帝。记得那个牧师问有谁愿意自告奋勇站出来时，我哭了。从那儿开始我再没嗑过药。那之后不久，我在一个约会网站上认识了我女友，她彻底改变了我。那时她比我条件可好多了：有工作，有财产——她是个不轻言放弃的人。因为她，我想重新做人。事实上三小时后我就要去MTA面试，简历我给他们送过47次。我需要那份福利和津贴，那样我们就能要孩子了。我女友跟我说我这样做应该是为了我自己，我跟她说：是的，是为了我自己，但也是为了我们，感恩有你。”小编@人在深圳  “I quit drugs three years ago. I was in a desperate place. I knew I was doing the wrong thing but I still couldn’t stop. Then one morning my brother asked me to come to church with him, and I came to know God. I started crying when the preacher asked if anyone wanted to come forward. And I haven’t done drugs since. Not long after that I met my girlfriend on a dating website. And she’s changed my life completely. She’s got her shit together. She’s got a job, she owns property--- she doesn’t quit. I want to be a different man because of her. I’ve actually got an interview with the MTA in three hours. I sent them my resume forty-seven times. I need the pension and benefits so we can have children. She tells me that I should be doing it for myself. I tell her: ‘I am doing it for myself, but because of us, and thanks to you.’”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhnlPrjPB&u=005trlAagw1f9qmoy4iwzj31kw11xaf2 )

>  “我走遍世界，一直靠自己的作品谋生。我结过14次婚，从不缺钱花，因为我有天分。天分比钱不要好太多，因为它一直跟着你呢。举个栗子：1970年，在巴西圣保罗的希尔顿酒店，有天我跟一个日本模特共进晚餐。有个德州的家伙坐在旁边一桌，他点了个牛排，但上一次他退一次，嘴上还不停嘟囔：‘还是德州的牛排好’。第二次退回去以后，主厨出来了，我听见他用葡萄语说：‘老子非宰了他不可！’ 作为一个加利西亚人(Galician)，我还是很了解拉丁人滴：要是一个法国人说他要宰了你，你根本不用担心，因为法国人是天生的好情人，而所有的好情人都是软蛋。相信我，我好几个前老婆都是法国的，我深知这一点。但如果一个拉丁人说他要宰了你，那你就该闪了。所以我走过去那桌，给那个德州佬买了瓶酒，先跟他聊德州——德州我也很懂，我在那儿参加过钓鱼比赛。聊了几分钟，我才跟他说：‘你敢再点一次牛排，你会被砍刀砍死。’ 他听我的，赶紧溜了。整个餐厅的人都出来了，拿着手鼓，给我唱歌。他们还拿来酒水，全场免费喝，还说呢：‘钱在这儿不顶事儿了啊。’ 日本模特也佩服我佩服得五体投地。瞧见了没？天分，这就是天分！”小编@人在深圳 “I’ve always lived off my artwork all my life. I’ve lived all over the world. I’ve had fourteen common law wives. I’ve never needed money because I’m talented. Talent is better than money because it’s always with you. Let me give you an example. Back in 1970 I was getting dinner with a Japanese model at the Sao Paulo Hilton in Brazil. This guy from Texas was sitting at the table next to me, and he’s trying to order a steak, but he keeps sending it back to the kitchen. He keeps saying: ‘The steaks are better in Texas.’ After the second time he sends it back, the master chef comes out, and I hear him say in Portuguese: ‘I’m going to kill this man!’ Now being a Galician myself, I know the character of the Latin American people. If a French person says he’s going to kill you, you don’t have to worry. The French are lovers and all lovers are cowards. Trust me—several of my former wives are French. I know this. But when a Latin American tells you that he’s going to kill you, it’s time to leave. So I walked over to the man’s table and bought him a bottle of wine, and I talked with him about Texas. I knew all about Texas because I competed in fishing tournaments there. After a few minutes of talking, I tell the man: ‘If you order one more steak, you’re going to get killed with a machete.’ So he took my advice and he left. The entire restaurant staff came out and started singing to me with tambourines. They brought out free wine and a full spread. They said, ‘Your money is no good here.’ The Japanese model was so impressed. See what I mean? Talent.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhmLp3tnY&u=005trlAagw1f9qj7fxx4bj31ey0xz0xi )

>  “我们在大学认识的，他走路送我回家，五年，每天。我们无话不谈：生几个孩砸，如何养育他们，我们各自在家里扮演什么样的角色，去哪儿生活，甚至去哪儿度假。所以我们的生活真没什么是意料之外的。很多夫妻似乎只讨论那些重要的事情，如果他们必须要做出重大的决定。然后就会有那种时刻，突然间觉得‘以前我并不是真的了解你’。然后做决定就会有压力，然后一触即发，大吵一架。很幸运这些我们都免了，因为以前都讨论过了。现在我们结婚15年，仍然每天晚上下班一起回家——实际上我们现在就正走在回家的路上呢！”小编@人在深圳 “We met in college. He walked me home from school every day for five years. We would talk about everything: how many kids we wanted, how we wanted to raise them, our roles in the home, where we wanted to live, and even where we wanted to go on vacation. So there really haven’t been many surprises. A lot of couples only seem to talk about important things if they’re forced to make big decisions. And there can be this moment of: ‘I didn’t really know you.’ And there’s pressure to make a decision. And that’s when the biggest arguments seem to happen. We've luckily managed to avoid that because it’s all been discussed before. We've been married for fifteen years but we still walk home together from work every night. We're actually doing that right now.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhlQq7q12&u=005trlAagw1f9qfyqka78j31kw11xgul )

>  “我不是奥巴马，也不是克林顿。他们俩都有一种吸引人的自然风度。但一个是我老公，一个曾是我老板，我知道他们要想表现出这种风度有多累。那可不简单，要说什么他们都得准备和练习先——不是说他们装腔作势，而是说要展现出你最好的一面也是很不容易滴。你得用一种人人都能听懂的方式沟通，而这对一个女人来说更难。因为，跟谁学呢？如果你竞选参议员、总统，你能学的多数人都是男的，而他们那一套对你来说并不适用。人们会以一种不同的眼光来看女性，不是说这不好，只是说这是事实。这一点很有趣。你去出席一些活动，会有男性在你面前讲啊讲，他们像是在爆重磅消息，叫喊着要如何赢得选举。人们喜欢这样。而我也想这样做啊，我也在乎这些，但我知道我不能太激动太煽情。我喜欢挥舞手臂，但显然那有点吓人。我也不能老是用喊的，那会给人的印象是太吵、太闹、太这太那。有趣吧，因为我始终相信，那些在前排的人喜欢我这一点。”小编@人在深圳 “I’m not Barack Obama. I’m not Bill Clinton. Both of them carry themselves with a naturalness that is very appealing to audiences. But I’m married to one and I’ve worked for the other, so I know how hard they work at being natural. It’s not something they just dial in. They work and they practice what they’re going to say. It's not that they're trying to be somebody else. But it's hard work to present yourself in the best possible way. You have to communicate in a way that people say: ‘OK, I get her.’ And that can be more difficult for a woman. Because who are your models? If you want to run for the Senate, or run for the Presidency, most of your role models are going to be men. And what works for them won’t work for you. Women are seen through a different lens. It’s not bad. It’s just a fact. It’s really quite funny. I’ll go to these events and there will be men speaking before me, and they’ll be pounding the message, and screaming about how we need to win the election. And people will love it. And I want to do the same thing. Because I care about this stuff. But I’ve learned that I can’t be quite so passionate in my presentation. I love to wave my arms, but apparently that’s a little bit scary to people. And I can’t yell too much. It comes across as ‘too loud’ or ‘too shrill’ or ‘too this’ or ‘too that.’ Which is funny, because I’m always convinced that the people in the front row are loving it.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhlrK4LJQ&u=005trlAagw1f9qddsspyej31kw11x442 )

>  “当时是在哈佛的一间大教室里参加法学院入学考试，我和我朋友，房间里就我们两个女生，我很紧张，那时我才念大四，也不知道自己能考成啥样。等考试开始时，有些男生开始起哄：‘你们不需要在这儿，你们有很多其他的事可以干。’ 他们越喊越起劲儿，有个家伙居然说：‘你抢了我的饭碗，那我惨了，我只好去当兵，被派去越南，然后我死定了。’ 他们并不是随便说笑，当时的气氛挺紧张，明显是对人不对事冲着我们来的。但我不能分心，我不想考砸。我只能充耳不闻，就那样低着头，等着考官进场。我知道那会被认为是冷漠、冷酷，甚至冷血，但作为一个小女生，你必须学着控制自己的情绪。其实那并不容易，你既要保护自己，保持镇静，又不能显得自己与环境格格不入。我想有时候我是显得把自己包裹了起来，如果我给人那种感觉，那也只能怪我。但其实我并不觉得自己是那样的，我的朋友、家人也不那样看我。可要是我真给人那种感觉，那还真怪不得别人。”小编@人在深圳 “I was taking a law school admissions test in a big classroom at Harvard. My friend and I were some of the only women in the room. I was feeling nervous. I was a senior in college. I wasn’t sure how well I’d do. And while we’re waiting for the exam to start, a group of men began to yell things like: ‘You don’t need to be here.’ And ‘There’s plenty else you can do.’ It turned into a real ‘pile on.’ One of them even said: ‘If you take my spot, I’ll get drafted, and I’ll go to Vietnam, and I'll die.’ And they weren’t kidding around. It was intense. It got very personal. But I couldn’t respond. I couldn’t afford to get distracted because I didn’t want to mess up the test. So I just kept looking down, hoping that the proctor would walk in the room. I know that I can be perceived as aloof or cold or unemotional. But I had to learn as a young woman to control my emotions. And that’s a hard path to walk. Because you need to protect yourself, you need to keep steady, but at the same time you don’t want to seem ‘walled off.’ And sometimes I think I come across more in the ‘walled off’ arena. And if I create that perception, then I take responsibility. I don’t view myself as cold or unemotional. And neither do my friends. And neither does my family. But if that sometimes is the perception I create, then I can’t blame people for thinking that.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhgqX0U5D&u=005trlAagw1f9pscg17iqj31kw11x42h )

>  “我从不是最好的学生，但幸运的是这是个关系驱动的世界。我在做销售，学识渊博很重要是没错，但我的工作主要就是让客户喜欢我，比喜欢别人更多。我们的所有竞争对手卖的东东都差不多，中间的差异微乎其微，所以最终归结于一点：客户对谁更有好感？而我，想让那个人是我。但这意味着大量的工作，因为关系不是一蹴而就的，我的手机得时刻开机；我回邮件得快，立刻，马上；我总是回复‘谢谢’；要是读到一篇文章，让我想起跟客户的一段谈话，我也会一并发送给他。”小编@人在深圳 “I was never the best student. But luckily it’s a relationship driven world. I’m in sales. And it’s important to be knowledgeable, but my job is primarily to get clients to like me more than the next guy. All of our competitors sell very similar products. The differences between us are very small. So it comes down to one thing: ‘Who does the customer like more?’ And I want that to be me. But it's a lot of work. Relationships don’t just materialize. I’m always on my phone. I answer emails immediately. I send ‘thank you’ notes for everything. And if I ever read an article that reminds me of a conversation we had, I’m sending it along.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhglmFvq2&u=005trlAagw1f9ps1tyidrj31kw11x4e6 )

>  “第一次见到Jack时，我还心想：总算是碰到个正常点的同志了，他不愤世嫉俗，也不冷嘲热讽，他懂得享受生活。那时他是个五年级老师，精力旺盛，一说起工作，总是兴奋不已。他自己编剧，让孩子们选择心仪的角色，他会花几个小时给他们写台词，然后我就装作学生家长，坐在观众席看他们的演出。那演出可欢乐了，事实上我们在一起都充满了欢乐。但我们只是约会，因为我总觉得自己可以挑个更好的——那时我是个律师，收入很高，总感觉Jack配不上我。我还是跟他分手了，跟一个性感的21岁小年轻好在了一起。Jack跟我还是朋友，我们甚至还住在一起。但他的心理医生跟他说再也不要跟我约会了，于是他也和别人好上了。然后他就染上病了，我们俩都染上病了，但Jack是那个死掉的人。要是那时我不是一个那么差劲的人，他应该不会死。要是那时他能‘配得上’我，他也永远不会得艾滋。搞笑的是，从小到大我都觉得不会有人爱我，当一个这么好的人爱着我，我却离开了他，去跟别人上床。Jack去世是30年前，我几乎每天晚上都会梦到他，在梦里他还是活生生的。有那么一刻，我不再因为他的死而责备自己，但通常我都在请求他的原谅。有些夜晚他原谅了我，但其他的夜晚他没有。”小编@人在深圳 “The first time I met Jack, I thought to myself: ‘Here’s a gay guy who’s not cynical, who’s not sarcastic, who enjoys life.’ He had so much energy. He was a fifth grade teacher and he’d always get so excited when he talked about his work. He’d produce these plays where he’d let the kids choose their own characters. He’d spend hours writing out their dialogue. And then I’d pretend to be one of the fathers and go sit in the audience. It was so fun. We had so much fun together. But the whole time we were dating, there was always part of me that thought I could do better. I was a fancy lawyer. Jack never seemed ‘cool enough’ for me. And so I left him for a gorgeous twenty-one year old. Jack and I remained friends. We even continued living together. But his therapist told him never to date me again. So he dated other people. And he got sick. Both of us got sick, but Jack was the one who died. And he might have lived if I hadn’t been such a bad person. If he'd been 'enough' for me, he'd never have gotten HIV. The funny thing is-- I’d grown up thinking that I’d never be loved. Then a wonderful person loved me. And I left him to have sex with somebody who wasn’t a wonderful person. Jack died thirty years ago. I dream about him almost every night. It always feels good to see him alive. For a moment, I don't have to blame myself for his death. I usually ask him for forgiveness. And some nights he forgives me. But other nights he doesn’t.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ehg3c1IdI&u=005trlAagw1f9pqnv36u0j31kw11xgrf )

---- current solving page 34
>  “每天吸毒，吸了二十年，自我感觉很拽。工作时也吸，它能让我嗨起来，但仍不耽误事，能浇混凝土，还能盖房顶，感觉自己无所不能。但毒品毁了我的婚姻，直到我老婆离开几年后我才意识到这一点。毒品让我有一种满足感，把什么都不当回事：我老婆的感受我没当回事，她的需要我也没当回事，反正那些显而易见的情绪，都被毒品掩盖了。我告诉自己：如果我没看到问题，那它就不是个问题。我老说她这说她那，从没问问她是咋想的，从没想过问一句：‘亲爱的，我知道有些地方不对劲儿，我能做些什么改变呢？’”小编@人在深圳 “I smoked dope every day for twenty years. I thought I was pretty slick. I could smoke while working. I could get high and still run my company. I could pour concrete. I could roof a building. I felt like I could do anything. But it ruined my marriage. I didn’t even realize it until years after my wife left me. But the dope ruined my marriage because it made me content. Nothing could bother me. Her feelings didn’t bother me. Her needs didn’t bother me. The dope put an emotional cover over what should have been obvious. I told myself that if I didn’t see the problem, then it didn’t qualify as a problem. All I ever did was give her advice. I never asked for it. I never once felt the inspiration to say: ‘Darling, I know there’s something wrong. What can I do differently?’”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhfGL8IjE&u=005trlAagw1f9pp0no4h1j31kw11xah4 )

-----------------------

>  “德州有片狭长地带，我从小在那儿的一个农场长大。有一天正开着我爸的拖拉机，我为自己感到难过，我要去过我想要的生活。当时我被法学院开除了，打不了橄榄球，也打不了网球，唯一擅长的就是表演——高中演戏我都演主角。所以趁着收获的季节我攒了足够的钱，买了一辆小型红色雅马哈，开去了达拉斯，为了进入演艺界。在达拉斯我演了一些戏，在《屋顶上的提琴手》里我还得到一个巡演的角色。然后我又骑着摩托去了好莱坞，我想成为一个电影明星！到那儿两个月，我得到了我的第一个大角色，一周500块，六周，当时我心想：‘牛X！这可是好莱坞哦！’ 我演的是个牛仔，摩托党混混，丫最后挂了，被草耙叉死的，从嬉皮党手上解救老大的马子的时候。你猜我是怎么得到这个角色的？我进去试镜，告诉他们我会这样演这个角色，就像现在这样，看到了么？斗鸡眼儿！从头到尾！你知道斗鸡眼儿骑摩托有多难？那简直是不可能的！但哥哥我，做！到！了！不幸的是，那个电影最终成了一部最糟糕的电影。”小编@人在深圳 “I grew up on a farm in the panhandle of Texas. One day I was driving my father’s tractor, feeling sorry for myself, and trying to figure out what I was going to do with my life. I’d flunked out of law school. I couldn’t play football or tennis. The only thing I’d ever been good at was performing. In high school, I’d played the lead role in both the junior and senior plays. So I saved up enough money during the harvest season to buy a little red Yamaha motorcycle. Then I drove to Dallas so I could go into show business! I did some plays in Dallas, then I got a touring role in Fiddler on The Roof, then I rode my motorcycle to Hollywood to be a movie star! I got my first big role two months after I arrived. They paid me $500 a week for six weeks. I thought, “Man! This is Hollywood!’ My character was a cowboy outlaw in a motorcycle gang. He ended up getting killed by a pitchfork while trying to rescue the leader’s girlfriend from a hippie commune. You know how I got the part? I walked into the audition and told them I’d do the whole part cross-eyed. Just like this. You know how hard it is to ride a motorcycle cross-eyed? Almost impossible. But I did it! Unfortunately it ended up being the worst reviewed movie ever made.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EheOfjdWC&u=005trlAagw1f9pl1xgqjzj31kw11xwiv )

-----------------------

>  “我像个野人一样长大，4岁继父开始虐待我，14岁我妈把我赶出了家。我嗑药成瘾，爱上了个毒贩，我们还生了个女儿。他打我，但我无处可去。19岁那年，我决定逃离这一切，我心想：‘不能再这样下去，我要离开波多黎各’。在来纽约的飞机上，挨着我坐的那个家伙吸海洛因，他让我也试试。结果到纽约后我反而变得更糟了，甚至更难了，因为在这儿我是孤孤单单一个人。最后我流落街头，居无定所。为了活下去，我做过我不得不去做的事，你懂的。政府把我的孩子们都带走了。那么多年，我迷失了自己。现在我重新做人了，不沾毒品，也在工作，还去教堂。但我内心很挣扎，各种情绪，我都不知道它们打哪儿来的，反正就是控制不了它们。跟人在一起时，感觉还好点。但那些过去总是会回来找我，我跟自己说：‘你以为你是谁？你作恶多端，甚至都不知道该如何正确说话。’ 我深陷在过去，总是难以自拔。但耶稣原谅了我，他知道我是个罪人，但他依然爱我。他并不在乎我的过去，他在改变我的想法。他在帮我重新开始，从头来过。没有他，我再没任何可以依靠的了。”小编@人在深圳 “I grew up, like, savage. My stepfather abused me starting at the age of four. My mother threw me out when I was fourteen. I became addicted to drugs. I fell in love with a drug dealer and we had a daughter. He hit me but I had nowhere else to go. I tried to get away from everything when I turned nineteen. I thought: ‘I’m leaving Puerto Rico and I’m going to change.’ But on the plane to New York, the guy next to me was a heroin user. And he convinced me to try it. And things got worse in New York. It was even harder because I was alone. I ended up in the street. I was jumping from house to house. I was doing what I had to do to survive, you know. The government took my children away. I was lost for so many years but I’m a new person now. I’m sober and I’m working and I’m going to church. But I struggle a lot. I have all these emotions and I don’t know where they come from. It’s like I can’t control them. And when I’m with other people, I feel less. My past always comes back to me. I say to myself: ‘Who do you think you are? You’ve done so many bad things. And you don’t even know how to talk right.’ I can never get away from the things that I’ve done. But Jesus forgives me, you know? He knows that I’m a sinner person and he still loves me. My past does not matter to him. He is changing my thinking. He is helping me start new. Without him, I would have nothing to hang onto.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ehe5jmST3&u=005trlAagw1f9phy9a6ypj31kw11xqb3 )

-----------------------

>  “世界不再像过去那样回应我了。过去我习惯了成为人们关注的焦点，大家对我都很好，我从没意识到它在多大程度上是因为我的年轻和美貌，还以为那是因为我有活力有魅力。我不得不接受现实：女人越老，别人对你的关注越少，从四十来岁开始，到五十多岁更是直线往下掉。要想吼住人们的对你的关注是越来越难，谈话中关于你的内容也是越来越少，更多的是谈事情。这曾让我很困扰，觉得像被忽视或抛弃了，但现在我已经过了那个阶段，你得有这样的涵养，习惯不再被人们关注。过去大半辈子我都是个演员，到哪儿都得让人关注。但现在我在做手语翻译，我挺喜欢的，因为人们关注我再不是因为我本人。”“The world doesn’t respond to me like it used to. Throughout my life I had learned to anticipate a certain pattern of focus and friendliness. And I never realized how much of that was based on my youth and physical appearance. I thought it was because of my energy and personality. But I’ve had to accept that a woman becomes less and less visible as she ages. It begins to fade in your 40’s, and drops off in your 50’s. You have a harder time holding people’s attention. The conversations become less about you, and more about the transaction. It used to really bother me. I would feel abandoned or ignored. But I’ve grown out of it. There’s a certain grace to letting go of the need for attention. I was an actor for most of my life. I was all about getting attention. But now I’m working as a sign language interpreter, which I love. Because it isn’t about me at all.”小编@人在深圳
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhddIh82e&u=005trlAagw1f9peapk5inj31kw11xgp7 )

-----------------------

>  “我出生在委内瑞拉，两年前搬到这儿来哒。我长大想当委内瑞拉总统，改变好多东西，让世界变得更美好。你知道吗？在委内瑞拉，有时候他们互相开枪，想打死对方，这不行，我要改变它。我还会制定规则，不准推人，还有，不准对别人动坏念头。我还会制定一个规则，这样就不会有那么多树被砍伐。我还会制定一个规则，反对人们杀死很多动物，因为动物吃虫子，虫子多了可不得了！我还会确保我们不浪费水或食物，或者，如果有食物吃剩下，我们一定要把它放进垃圾桶。现在我还不能当总统，因为我只有八岁，但一年级我就跳级了。”“I was born in Venezuela. I moved here two years ago. I want to be President of Venezuela to change things and make better the world. Did you know that sometimes in Venezuela people shoot each other on purpose? I will change that. Also there will be rules against pushing people or thinking bad thoughts about people. I will make a rule so that there will not be too much cutting or killing of trees. And there will be a rule against killing too many animals because animals eat insects, and we can’t have too many insects. I will also make sure that we don’t waste water or food. Or if there is food left over, we have to be sure to put it in the trash. I can’t be president now because I’m only eight. But I did skip first grade.”小编@人在深圳
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Ehd2CnvTs&u=005trlAagw1f9pdg07xlwj31kw11x79r )

>  “我在做一次音乐学习之旅，和African Roots。这不是为了上学，或其他任何东西，只是为了我自己。我想自己一个人，独自旅行一年，只带着衣服和我的鼓槌。我已经省了6000块，我计划边旅行边打工。第一站是纽约，我在这儿待了两星期了，看了十场音乐会，花了300块，我得更加小心了。我还要搭大巴去底特律，我找到个地儿收留我，作为交换，一天干几个小时活儿。然后我还要去芝加哥、圣路易斯、孟菲斯和新奥尔良，然后古巴、巴西、秘鲁，再然后，回家回法国。我想尽量多了解些音乐，但这只是此行的一半目的。我还想知道我是否能做到——我有点担心自己会感到孤独，但这正是我想弄清楚的——我想知道自己是否能独自一个人。”“I’m on a tour to study music with African roots. It’s not for school or anything. It’s just a personal project. I want to travel alone for an entire year with just clothes and my drumsticks. I’ve saved $6000 and I plan to work along the way. My first stop was New York. I’ve been here two weeks and I went to ten concerts. I’ve already spent $300 so I need to be more careful. I’m about to catch a bus for Detroit. I found a place where I can live in exchange for a few hours of daily work. Then I’m going to Chicago, St. Louis, Memphis, and New Orleans. Then Cuba. Then Brazil. Then Peru. And after that I’ll go home to France. I want to learn as much about music as possible. But that’s only half the reason for the trip. I also want to learn if I can do it. I am a little afraid that I’ll get lonely, but that’s something I want to figure out. I want to know if I can be alone.”小编@人在深圳
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EhbY80Ldq&u=005trlAagw1f9p8pnes2aj31kw11xjvk )

>  2016 年 10 月 5 日“五年级我就暗恋他了，但当时我心想：‘我们会保持朋友关系很长时间吧’，因为通常我不是那种喜欢早恋的人。但我又想：‘不如试一试吧！’ 我开始跟他打情骂俏，说些‘你看起来好赞’，或者‘我喜欢你的发型’之类的话。后来我们上了不同的高中，开始频繁发信息，每隔一段时间我就发个心啊吻啊什么的，他要穿正装也会发张照片给我看下。反正一切进展顺利。有天我预约了矫正牙齿，在他学校附近，我们就说好在星巴克见面。他妈妈开车把他放下，我们就沿着河散步。后来坐在长椅上，看见他掷硬币，我还以为他很无聊呢，但就在那之后，他吻了我。”“I’d been harboring a crush on him since 5th grade. But I thought: ‘I’m gonna be in the friend zone for a long time.’ Because I’m normally not the kind of person who’s liked in that way. But I thought, ‘Go for it.’ So I started flirting. I’d say things like, ‘You look nice.’ Or ‘I like your hair.’ Then we started going to different high schools, so we started texting a lot. And every once in a while I’d use a heart emoji. Or a kiss emoji. And if he ever had to dress in a suit, he’d send me a picture. So things were going well. Then one day I had an orthodontist appointment near his school and we decided to meet at Starbucks. After his mom dropped him off, we went on a walk by the stream. Then we sat on a bench. And I saw him flip a coin. So I thought he was bored. But right after, he gave me a kiss.”译者：@人在深圳Facebook: http://t.cn/RVZGEB4Tumblr: http://t.cn/RVZGEB5Twitter: http://t.cn/RVZGEBLInstagram: http://t.cn/RVZGEBb欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EbCAfombu&u=005trlAagw1f8ivz59075j31kw11xjzx )

>  2016 年 10 月 3 日“我父亲是个好人。他有正经工作，也从不抽烟喝酒。但我母亲的情况并不稳定，我们经常因此被赶出公寓。她把我们所有的积蓄都用来买毒品了。在我上六年级的时候，她用一把砍刀捅了我父亲的肚子。我永远也忘不了那个声音，它就如同吸盘吸壁一样。还有一次她向我父亲脸上泼碱液，致使他脸部脱皮。然而自始至终我父亲都没有离开，因为他不希望把我们单独丢在母亲身边。我没有跟我的精神病治疗师提过我母亲，因为我不希望他把我与她相提并论。我很讨厌外人这么看待我。有些人说我就是我母亲的翻版，因为我会变得狂躁暴力，而且我也曾经捅过人。但我与她并不一样。我有寻求帮助并接受治疗，我一直在服用碳酸锂缓释片、阿普唑仑一类的抗焦虑狂躁症药物。我现在懂得去爱自己了，但我不喜欢不用药时自己的状态。在那种情况下周围的任何人与事都会惹恼我，我就像中了邪一样。”“My father was a good man. He always had a job. He never drank. He never smoked. But my mother was never stable. We were evicted so many times. She spent all our money on drugs. When I was in sixth grade, she stabbed my father in the stomach with a butcher knife. I'll never forget that sound. It sounded like a suction cup. Then another time she threw lye on his face and his skin came off. But my father stayed through it all because he didn’t want us to be alone with her. I don’t tell my psychiatrist about my mother. I don’t want him to look at me like I’m her. I hate when people do that. Some people say I’m just like her. Because I get violent. I stabbed somebody too. But I’m not like her. Because I got help. I’ve been on Lithium, Xanax, everything. I love myself right now. But I don’t like myself when I’m not on my medicine. Because everyone pushes my buttons. Everything bothers me. I get evil.”译者：Lanny李小豆Facebook: http://t.cn/RV7ABJSTumblr: http://t.cn/RV7ABJoTwitter: http://t.cn/RV7ABJ6Instagram: http://t.cn/RV7ABJa欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=EbrzgvGP9&u=005trlAagw1f8hjci56x8j31kw11xwij )

>  2016 年 3 月 21 日“我的工作是帮助不在住业主维护房产。我想很多人都认为长岛的业主房东们都是有钱人，但其实我大部分的客户都只拥有一两套房产而已，且常常都是遗产继承的。我的职责其中之一就是协助驱赶非法入住的人。现在有不少职业做非法入住工作的人，你甚至都不能把他们叫做罪犯。他们懂得法律，所有的行为都合乎法制。如果你抓到某人闯进你的房子——那是违法的‘破门而入’，但是如果你碰巧住在另一个州，而有人闯进你的房子住了六个月都没被你知道的话，那这个人就成为了你的租客，不管他有没有得到你的允许。若你想把他们赶走，必须要走法律途径，得花很多钱，所以一般直接用钱打发非法入住的人会便宜一些。法律本身其实并不坏，最初相关法例颁布的目的，是防止不讲道理的房东，在还未走正当程序之前就要赶走住户。然而，与其他任何一条法律都差不多，总有人会钻空子。现在我手上有一个非法入住的人在一幢旧楼里免费住了六年了，一分钱房租也没交过。他穿着考究，开门时待人彬彬有礼。我们同意给他 8 万美元让他离开，他却要价更高。”“I help maintain properties for absentee landlords. I think most people imagine landlords to be rich guys on Long Island. But most of my clients only own one or two properties. A lot of times they were inherited. Part of my job is helping to get squatters out of the buildings. There are professional squatters out there. You can’t even call them criminals. They know the laws and they’re working within the system. If you catch somebody breaking into your house-- that’s ‘breaking and entering.’ But if you happen to live out of state, and somebody breaks into your house and you don’t notice for six months, then that person becomes your tenant. It doesn’t matter if you gave them permission or not. If you want to evict them, you have to go through the legal system, which is very expensive. So it’s usually cheaper to pay the squatters off. The laws themselves aren’t bad. They were enacted to keep predatory landlords from evicting people without due process. But like all laws, there are people who have figured out how to abuse them. I have one squatter who has been living rent free in an old building for six years. He hasn’t paid a dime. He’s well dressed. He’s always very polite and professional when he answers the door. But we’re offering him $80,000 to leave and he’s asking for more.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RtJqfUJTumblr: http://t.cn/RtJqfUXTwitter: http://t.cn/RtJqfUSInstagram: http://t.cn/RtJqfUi欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=E1GuqCxrO&u=005trlAagw1f6fc2dxyztj31kw11xte7 )

>  2016 年 3 月 20 日“我闯了祸。我在我们数学考试的时候打了我的同学，因为他当时叫了我的绰号，平时他也总是叫。老师问我：‘为什么你要打他？’我回答说：‘因为他叫我青蛙脸。’之后我坐了十分钟禁闭。虽然我闯了祸，但到家后妈妈还是再给了我一次机会。下次再有人叫我青蛙脸，我就会直接告诉老师。”hit my classmate during our math exam because he was calling me names like he always does. The teacher said: ‘Why did you hit him?’ And I said: ‘Because he called me frog face.’ And then I had to sit alone for ten minutes. And then when I went home I got in trouble but Mommy gave me one more chance and next time if someone calls me frog face I’m just going to tell the teacher.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RtMdsVLTumblr: http://t.cn/RtMdsVATwitter: http://t.cn/RtMdsV2Instagram: http://t.cn/RtMdsVy欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约

>  2016 年 3 月 18 日“我刚过了三十五岁生日。每一件事情现在对我来说都是个大问题。我的小狗在一月份去世了；我辞去了自己的工作；我把自己的头发给剪掉了；昨晚我和男朋友大吵了一架，所以现在我也不知道会发生什么。我感觉自己就要崩溃了。我从来都不是那种‘想象着自己未来的孩子’、‘幻想着自己将来的婚礼’、或者‘构思着自己的婚纱’的女生，但是我现在已经三十五了，我禁不住就纳闷‘这些事是否真的还会发生？’、‘什么时候才会发生？’、以及‘到底是和谁一起呢？’。我从十八岁起就开始做酒保了，我早已经习惯了这份工作。它很有保障，我不可能搞砸的，一杯‘曼哈顿’仅有一种做法。我辞去工作的原因就是想切断自己的后路。我想利用自己的美容学位在发型设计行业里发展。但是我已经面试了好几家美发店，没有得到任何结果。我真的要失去自信了。我感觉自己周围的一切都在塌陷。我认为自己十七年来只做一个酒保就是因为害怕自己会有这样的感觉。”“I turned thirty-five recently. Everything is one big question for me right now. My dog died in January. I quit my job. I chopped off my hair. I got in a huge fight with my boyfriend last night and now I don’t know what’s going to happen. I feel like I’m about to fall apart. I’ve never been the type of girl who thought too much about kids, or dreamed about her wedding day, or thought about her wedding dress. But I’m thirty-five now. And I can’t help but wonder if it's ever going to happen. And when is it going to happen? And who is it going to happen with? I’ve been a bartender since the age of eighteen. I got used to it. It was safe. I couldn't mess up. There’s only one way to make a Manhattan. And the whole reason I quit my job was to pull the rug out from under myself. I wanted to use my cosmetology degree and pursue a career in hair styling. But I’ve interviewed with several salons now, and nothing has come of it. I’m really losing my self-confidence. I feel like everything is crashing down around me. I think I spent seventeen years stuck as a bartender because I was so afraid of feeling like this.”Facebook: http://t.cn/R5XNDKSTumblr: http://t.cn/R5XNDKXTwitter: http://t.cn/R5XNDKaInstagram: http://t.cn/R5XNDKo欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DAl8wfjUP&u=005trlAagw1f4vt05iim9j31kw11xn2k )

>  2016 年 3 月 16 日“我的第一任妻子 Eileen 在她 48 岁的时候突然就去世了。有大概一年多的时间，我都过得精神恍惚。我们在一起的时候没要孩子，而我本来就不擅长社交，自己的性格不是如此，同时也不够果断。我当初能够遇到 Eileen 的唯一原因就是我们俩在同一个办公室工作。殡仪馆每个月都会举办一场活动，你可以去参与，然后找人说说话。那给了我一定的帮助，但是除此以外我真的很孤单。那时我唯一真正的爱好是爱尔兰舞蹈，我曾经试着要把这个爱好给坚持下去，但跳舞会让我满脑子想的都是 Eileen，所以我便放弃了。我是在无意之间发现的步行，完全是偶然。也不知道是谁在办公室里留下了一本手册，是关于一个名叫‘阿巴拉契亚山脉俱乐部’的组织。他们全由志愿者们组成，会在卡兹奇山组织步行活动，我在周末就会加入。步行并不是件非常艰难的事，但是能够完成一件事的感觉还是好极了。同时这项活动也有利于认识朋友。在别人身旁步行时，你也没有特别多其他的事情可做。我从此爱上了步行，开始前往其他国家旅游，并在当地步行游览。我在一次佛罗伦萨外围的游览中认识了我现在的妻子。”“My first wife Eileen passed away suddenly when she was 48. I was in a fog for a year or so. We didn’t have any children together. And I’m just not good at meeting people. I don’t have that personality. I’m not assertive enough. The only reason I’d been able to meet Eileen was because we worked at the same office. The funeral parlor held an event once a month, where you could go and just talk. That helped a little. But other than that I was pretty lonely. The only real hobby I had was Irish dancing. I tried to keep it up, but it reminded me too much of Eileen, so I quit. I discovered walking by accident. It was a fluke. Somebody left a brochure at the office for something called the Appalachian Mountain Club. It was run by volunteers. They’d organize walks in the Catskills. I started going on the weekends. It’s not like they were hugely difficult, but it felt great to accomplish something. And it was really conducive to meeting people. There’s not much else to do when you’re walking next to somebody. I loved it so much that I started travelling to other countries and doing walking tours. I met my current wife on a tour outside of Florence.”Facebook: http://t.cn/R5xM0H9Tumblr: http://t.cn/R5xM0HoTwitter: http://t.cn/R5xM0HKInstagram: http://t.cn/R5xM0HN欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DzL5yvmpR&u=005trlAagw1f4rdux58azj31kw11x46n )

>  2016 年 3 月 13 日“我的工作是教未满十岁的孩子们踢足球。我现在正在给四岁的孩子们设计一些训练活动。我们一般都试着让孩子们在活动中感受到自己在对世界做出改变。其中一项活动中，我们会想象自己正在建造一座白雪村庄。在另一项活动中，我们将摧毁一艘海盗船。然后，我们也有幽灵海盗、太空海盗等等的训练活动，有很多海盗就是了。我们想让一切都尽量保持政治正确，因为家长们会在一旁观看训练，而击败海盗则是件每个人都能够赞同的事。”“I teach soccer to children under ten. Right now I’m sketching out some drills for the four year olds. We try to do things in a way where the kids feel like they’re making a difference. For one of the drills, we imagine that we’re building a snow village. For another drill we have to destroy a pirate ship. Then there’s a drill with ghost pirates. And another one with space pirates. Lots of pirates. We want to keep things politically correct because the parents watch the practice. Attacking pirates is something that everyone can get behind.”Facebook: http://t.cn/R5tg4kzTumblr: http://t.cn/R5tg4k7Twitter: http://t.cn/R5tg4khInstagram: http://t.cn/R5tg4kZ欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DyZwBoEC9&u=005trlAagw1f4ljvwlqscj31kw11xwom )

>  2016 年 3 月 12 日“我现在主要就把心思放在世界和平上，让所有的人都能爱护彼此。我是一个真正意义上的好哥们儿。我就是那个独一无二的好哥们儿。好吧，我是众多独一无二的好哥们儿中的一员。好哥们儿可以有很多种：黑人、白人、印第安人，而好哥们儿一定会是那个在别人需要帮助的时候伸出援手的人。好哥们儿会挺身而出说：‘那是不对的。’许多女性也可以是好哥们儿，但我们不叫她们好哥们儿，我们叫她们好姐们儿。”“I’m just working on universal peace and getting everybody to love each other. I’m an official brother man. I’m the one. Well, I’m one of the ones. There are all kinds of brother mans: black, white, Indian. A brother man is somebody who helps when people need help. A brother man will stand up and say: ‘That’s not right.’ A lot of women are brother mans too. But we don’t call them brother mans. We call them sisters.”Facebook: http://t.cn/R55NLQnTumblr: http://t.cn/R55NLQuTwitter: http://t.cn/R55NLQRInstagram: http://t.cn/R55NLQE欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约

>  2016 年 3 月 11 日“成就一直以来都是我的麻醉药。也许因为我是家里的老二，所以为了博得赞赏我愿意去做任何事情。我记得自己小时候在钢琴前坐下，一练就是好几个小时，手掌压着网球试图做到正确的手位，又或者是尽力去比我姐姐牢记住更多的曲子。大学的时候我怀了孕，并在大二的时候生下了我的儿子。我是个未婚妈妈，却并不想成为众多辍学者中的一员。我想取得些成就，我想证明自己不但能够成功，还能够抚养出一个出色的孩子。我准时毕了业，为自己感到如此地自豪，自己从没有接受过任何来自他人的帮助。此后，我进入了销售行业，全身心投入了工作。每次我达成一个目标时，它就像是一剂麻醉药；每次我达到自己的指标时，都会沉浸在喜悦中。过去的几年里，我每周都会工作六十到八十个小时，手下有一个三十人的销售团队。但是我们公司三周前被收购了，而我也被辞退。现在我想着，也许是时候喘口气了。我整个人生都是围绕着自己和我的孩子，他的确成为了一个出色的人，而我也为自己打下了坚实的基础。我想，终于是时候对我自己说：一切都会好的。”“Achievement has always been a drug for me. Maybe it’s because I was a middle child and would do anything for recognition. I remember being a child and sitting at the piano for hours, with tennis balls under my hands, trying to get the right finger positions. Or trying to memorize more songs than my older sister. I got pregnant in college and gave birth to my son during my sophomore year. I was an unwed mother. I didn’t want to be a statistic. I wanted to achieve something. I wanted to prove that I could succeed and raise a great kid. I graduated on time. I was so proud of myself. I never accepted any help from anyone. I went into sales and I threw myself into work. Every time I reached a goal, it was like a drug. There was a sense of euphoria every time I hit my numbers. For the last few years, I’ve been working sixty to eighty hours a week. I led a sales team of thirty people. But my company got acquired and three weeks ago I got laid off. And I’m thinking that maybe it’s time to take a pause. For my whole life, it’s just been me and my child. And he turned out great. I’ve laid a strong foundation. I think it’s time to finally realize that things will be OK.”Facebook: http://t.cn/R5q524ETumblr: http://t.cn/R5q524nTwitter: http://t.cn/R5q524gInstagram: http://t.cn/R5q524u欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DyG4AfX0B&u=005trlAagw1f4j5zy47ghj31kw11xk1b )

>  2016 年 3 月 10 日“我不再如以前一般享受着对他人举止的观察了。每个人都表现得好像他们正在舞台上表演那样。以前人们初到格林尼治村的时候都很拘谨。没有人能确定自己是否属于这里，我们都不知道自己是不是艺术家。现在每个人都表现出他们正在贡献着些什么的姿态，毫不害臊、骄傲自恃，也是可惜了，因为一切最美的艺术都来源于那些没有归属感的人。艺术是你证明自我存在价值的一种方式。在我年轻的时候，一个我很敬重的人告诉我说我是一个艺术家。那是我这辈子所能经历过的最糟糕的事情了。我走进博物馆或美术馆时，不再怀着敬畏感，反而觉得自己是一个‘艺术家’。我的手臂会交叉着，我喜欢的作品就是‘好的’，我不喜欢的作品就是‘差的’。我不再觉得脆弱，失去了自己的谦逊。而成长，也就在那同一时间止步了。”“I don’t enjoy observing people as much as I used to. Everyone acts like they’re on stage. People used to come to The Village sheepishly. Nobody was sure if they belonged. We didn’t know if we were artists. These days everyone walks around like they’re contributing something. There’s no angst anymore. There’s too much certainty. And that’s a shame. Because all the best art comes from people who feel like they don’t belong. Art is a way of proving your existence. When I was a young man, a person that I respected told me that I was an artist. It was one of the worst things that could have happened to me. I stopped walking into museums or galleries with a sense of awe. I walked in feeling like an ‘artist.’ My arms would be crossed. If I liked a piece, it was ‘good.’ If I didn’t like a piece, it was ‘bad.’ I didn't feel vulnerable anymore. I lost my humility. And that’s when growth stops.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqgaD81Tumblr: http://t.cn/RqgaD8rTwitter: http://t.cn/RqgaD8BInstagram: http://t.cn/RqgaD83欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DvuLHpLeI&u=005trlAajw1f3uyy7ci59j31kw11xn52 )

>  2016 年 3 月 10 日“目前我只是录音棚助理，基本上就是清洁厕所、做做准备工作还有削削铅笔。我只是得证明自己会不遗余力地把事情做好，然后每周录音棚没人的时候，我就能得到几小时的练习时间。此后，我会成为策划助理，那时我才能真正地在进行录音的时候旁听。我最终的目标是成为一名制作人。音乐产业像是男孩子们的天下，我大学的专业只有三个女生，而我现在工作的录音棚也只有另外一位女性。我不知道为什么没有更多的女性投身音乐界。对我来说，这份工作真的太完美了。我自己并不是一个表演者，但是我很热爱音乐，所以在音乐产业里工作能够让我在不登上舞台的同时协助创作音乐。而且，机会实在是太多了，每首‘泰勒·斯威夫特’的歌曲的背后都有三四十号人呢。”“Right now I’m an assistant at a recording studio, which basically means cleaning the bathrooms, doing prep work, and sharpening pencils. I just have to prove that I’ll go out of my way to get things done. Then each week I get a few hours of practice time when the studio is empty. Next I’ll become an assistant engineer, and I’ll actually get to sit in on the recording sessions. The ultimate goal is to become a producer. Audio is a bit of a boys’ club. There were only three girls in my program at college, and there’s only one other woman at my studio now. I’m not sure why more women don’t pursue it. It’s perfect for me. I’m not much of a performer but I love music. So working in audio allows me to help create music without having to get on stage. And there's plenty of opportunity. Every Taylor Swift song has thirty or forty people behind it.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqWo8I7Tumblr: http://t.cn/RqWo8IwTwitter: http://t.cn/RqWo8I2Instagram: http://t.cn/RqWo8Ih欢迎关注我们，更多故事尽在@人在纽约
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DsRGvlcuB&u=005trlAagw1f3art23gogj31kw11xae2 )

>  2016 年 3 月 8 日(2/2) “我遇见她的时候是学校的安全主任。她当时则是一位老师，但她一直不断地向上奋斗。她当上了校长，她转去了中央办公室工作，她取得了她的博士学位。最终，她成为了纽约教育界首屈一指的黑人女性。她总是为下一个目标努力着。我还是学校保洁员的时候，我们结了婚。她赚的钱比我所赚的多五倍，最初这很困扰我，在受到了心理辅导之后我才说服了自己：她并不是‘将就’着和我过。我从小到大都被灌输着男人应该是整个家庭的担当的想法，但是最终我认识到金钱并非唯一的担当途径。我能够通过做家务来支持她，或者是通过接送孩子上学，又或者是通过去机场接送她。她的工作成就了整个家，所以我能担当的就是让她的工作不那么劳累。终于，她也启发了我去为自己争取更多。是她说服了我重回到大学校园。”(2/2) “I was working as a school safety officer when I met her. She was a teacher. But she kept working her way up. She became a principal. She went to work in the central office. She got her doctorate. Eventually she became the highest-ranking black woman in New York education. She was always taking that next step. I was working as a custodian when we got married. She was making five times more than me. It bothered me at first. It took some counseling to convince me that she hadn’t ‘settled’ for me. I’d been raised on the idea that the man was supposed to provide. But eventually I came around to the idea that money wasn’t the only way to provide. I could support her by doing chores, or taking the kids to school, or picking her up from the airport. Her work benefited all of us, so I could help provide by making her job easier. And eventually she inspired me to want more for myself. She’s the one that convinced me to go back to college.”Facebook: http://t.cn/Rq0dBNxTumblr: http://t.cn/Rq0dBN6Twitter: http://t.cn/Rq0dBNiInstagram: http://t.cn/Rq0dBNJ
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DsAIExmcs&u=005trlAagw1f38w2tyvs6j31kw11x7ax )

>  2016 年 3 月 8 日(1/2) “我直到自己五十岁才开始上大学。那时候我的工作是保洁员，而到最后这份工作也变得无聊了，每一天你都能在同一地点、同一时间看到我清理礼堂、打扫教室、清洁厕所。我没有任何满足感。于是，我开始在夜间和周末前往大学上课。那段日子很艰难，因为我总是非常地累，也总会有我不想做作业或者因为下雨而不想去学校的时候。但是我的教授们不断地告诉我说：‘你寻找的不再是一份工作。你寻找的是一份事业。’五年前我本科毕业了，又过了两年半我取得了自己的硕士学位。现在我在当初自己做保洁员的学校做家长协调员。我能够在孩子的校内学习成效方面为家长提供咨询服务，这加倍了我的自信心。过去我往往对发表自己的看法有所顾虑，因为我会觉得自己抒发意见还不够格，但是现在我会在大街上与家长们停下来打招呼——确保他们孩子的学业都走在正轨。有些同事在被分配到很重的工作量时，会说：‘为什么我非得做这个？’而我总想着：‘我真有幸能够做这个。’我在教育部工作已经有三十年了，因此明年我就能退休享受福利了，但是我并不想这么做，因为我爱我现在的工作，每天都是不一样的。”(1/2) “I didn’t go to college until I was fifty. I was working as a custodian and it just got tiresome. You could find me in the exact same place, at the exact same time, every single day. Clean the halls, clean the classrooms, clean the bathroom. I wasn’t feeling fulfilled. I started going to college classes on the nights and weekends. It was difficult because I was always tired. There’d be times when I didn’t want to do an assignment or I didn’t want to go to school because it was raining. But my professors kept telling me: ‘You’re not looking for a job anymore. You’re looking for a career.’ I graduated five years ago with my BA. Then 2.5 years later I got my Masters. Now I’m a parent coordinator at the same school where I worked as a custodian. I get to counsel parents about how their children can get the most out of school. My confidence has doubled. I used to be unsure about speaking up, because I didn’t feel qualified to offer my opinion, but now I’ll stop parents on the street—just to make sure that their child is on the right track. Some people in my position get stressed when they’re given a heavy workload, like: ‘Why do I have to do this?’ I always think: ‘I get to do this.’ I’ve been working in the Department of Education for thirty years, so I could retire next year with benefits. But I don’t want to. Because I love my job. Every day is different.”Facebook: http://t.cn/Rq01sz4Tumblr: http://t.cn/Rq01szbTwitter: http://t.cn/Rq01szUInstagram: http://t.cn/Rq01szy
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DsAf6dupO&u=005trlAagw1f38tz1n35pj31kw11x7c9 )

>  2016 年 4 月 23 日昨天傍晚 Susie 去世了。五年前，她意想不到地闯入了我的生活。我看见她的那天晚上正在布鲁克林摄影，而她则高冷地蹲坐在一户人家门前的楼梯上。于是我便坐了下来轻轻地抚摸她。几分钟之后，她的主人告诉我说，他已经无法再照顾她了，问我能不能够照顾她。那个时候我身无分文，仍然借宿在一个朋友家的沙发上。而每一个我询问过的人都告诉我说现在并不是养狗的‘好时机’。然而我实在是被 Susie 给迷住了，我们整个相遇的过程看起来是如此地命中注定，以致于我决定要领养她。那是我人生中所作出的最佳决定之一。那个时候 Susie 已经十二岁了，没有任何特别高的需求，而在此之前我也从来没有养过小狗，一切都是全新的体验。我也因此第一次在人生中感受到了来自于一只小狗的无法名状也无条件的爱。短短几周后，Susie 生命中唯一关心的事便是尽量地靠近我了。此后我每天工作完毕都有一次愉快的重聚在家里等着我。而我也领悟到世间鲜有比一只兴奋不已的小狗在家门口欢迎你更幸福的事了。在过去几年间，我的未婚妻 Erin 建立起了她自己与 Susie 的纽带。你们大都知道 Erin 发起的名叫‘Susie 的老龄犬’的非营利组织，意在帮助老龄犬找到一个温馨的寄养家庭。老龄犬往往很难找到人领养它们。由于幼龄犬的需求量非常之高，太多的老龄犬最终只能被安乐死或者一辈子留宿在收容所里。在过去的几年里，‘Susie 的老龄犬’帮助几百只老龄犬找到了寄养家庭，关注这个页面的是热情而又活跃的一群人。说真的，有一大半来我书籍签售会的人们见到 Erin 比见到我更激动。所以这几天挺伤感的，但是 Erin 和我都很感激 Susie 在我们的生命中留下的印记。她是个与众不同的伙伴。她启发了我对小狗们的宠爱。她帮助 Erin 找到了自己的人生理想。因此，某种意义上来说，她永远都不会离我们而去。我鼓励大家都能去关注‘Susie 的老龄犬’，并考虑给予老龄犬一次机会来让它改变你的生活。Susie passed away yesterday evening. She came into my life quite unexpectedly five years ago. I was photographing in Brooklyn one evening when I saw the coolest little dog sitting on a stoop. I sat down to pet her, and after a few minutes, her owner told me that he was unable to care for her anymore. He asked if I could take her. I was broke at the time. I was sleeping on a friend’s couch. And everyone that I asked told me that it was ‘not the right time’ for a dog. But I was so charmed by Susie, and the whole encounter seemed so fated, that I offered to take her.It was one of the best decisions I ever made. Susie was twelve years old at the time and didn’t need much. I’d never had a dog before. It was a new experience. I was introduced for the first time to a dog’s unexplainable and unconditional love. After a few weeks, it seemed that Susie’s only concern in life was staying as close to me as possible. There was now a joyous reunion waiting for me at the end of every workday. And I learned that there are few greater blessings than a wildly happy dog greeting you at the door.Over the last few years, my fiancée Erin developed her own relationship with Susie. As many of you know, Erin started a nonprofit called Susie's Senior Dogs, which seeks to place older dogs in loving homes. Older dogs have the hardest time getting adopted. Because there is such a demand for young dogs, so many senior dogs are either euthanized or forced to spend the remainder of their lives in a shelter. Over the past few years, Susie's Senior Dogs has placed several hundred senior dogs into homes. There is a warm and active community of people who follow the page. In fact, I think that half the people who come to my book signings are more excited to meet Erin than me.So it’s been a tough few days, but Erin and I are both very thankful that Susie came into our lives. She was such a special friend. She was my introduction to the love of dogs. And she helped Erin discover her purpose in life. So in a way she’s going to stick around forever. I encourage everyone to follow Susie's Senior Dogs, and consider allowing an older dog to change your life as well.‘Susie 的老龄犬’ Facebook 主页：http://t.cn/Rq0I7jbFacebook: http://t.cn/Rq0I7jGTumblr: http://t.cn/Rq0I7jqInstagram: http://t.cn/Rq0I7j4
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DstYs2J4x&u=005trlAagw1f382anj7n0j30qo0hsdgm )

>  2016 年 3 月 7 日“我年轻的时候把所有的游行和示威都参与遍了，连我的黄色大众汽车上都有着和平反战的标志。我记得自己在七十年代时躺在长岛高速公路上抗议着肯特州立大学的五四屠杀。够疯狂吧？我也知道的。只是我们以为那样就能停止战争了，我想在某种程度上那确实起了作用吧。我还在一次位于华盛顿的示威中被拘捕过。我甚至连我们具体抗议的是什么都不记得了，但当时我们人数多到他们不得不把我们赶进‘RFK 球场’。我还记得华盛顿的人潮——环顾四周，你所能看到的都是与你同心的人。而 95 号州际公路上不计其数的巴士都在驶向同一个地方。我因此误以为世界真的正在改变，却不知道自己住在泡沫之中：我所有的朋友都是犹太人、中产阶级或者受过教育的人；我甚至都不认识任何拥有枪支的人；我以为每个人都向往着和平以及更好的环境，我以为没有人对他人心怀憎恨。然后尼克松凭借着他的‘南方战略’当选了总统。他煽动起了如此多的仇恨与种族主义，而我也终于意识到：‘我的天哪。有些人真的是无可救药。’再然后，我们这一代人开始结婚、生子，逐渐减少了对这个世界的关心，其中也包括我吧。你真的没法阻止这一切，不得不开始更专注于自我。人生在世，每个人都只有那么多精力可以消耗。”“I went to every march and protest there was when I was young. I had a peace sign on my little yellow Volkswagen. I remember lying down on the Long Island Expressway in seventy-something to protest Kent State. Crazy, I know. But we thought that would end the war. I guess it did in a way. Once I was arrested at a protest in Washington. I don’t even remember exactly what we were protesting. But there were so many of us that they herded us into RFK stadium. I remember those crowds in Washington. You looked around and all you could see were people who agreed with you. Zillions of buses on I-95 all going to the same place. And it really made me think that the world was changing. But I was living in a bubble. All my friends were Jewish, middle-class, and educated. I didn’t even know anyone who owned a gun. I thought everyone wanted peace, and a better environment, and that nobody hated anyone. Then Nixon got elected using his Southern Strategy. He tapped into so much hatred and racism. And I realized: ‘My God. People are fucked up.’ Then my generation started marrying, having kids, and started caring less about the world. And probably me too. You can’t help it really. You have to become more self-involved. You only have so much energy you can expend in the world.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqpY5mOTumblr: http://t.cn/RqpY5m0Twitter: http://t.cn/RqpY5mlInstagram: http://t.cn/RqpY5mW
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DslmtDTGD&u=005trlAagw1f3709zzsy8j31kw11xdp1 )

>  2016 年 3 月 6 日(2/2) “他是我的外甥。每周有那么两三天，我会在我姐姐工作的时候来照看他。昨晚我们一起去看了一场戏剧，而今天我们就是上街买点东西。做舅舅还挺不错的，因为我在享受他的陪伴的同时，却不用担心要抚养他的负担。我们在一起玩得很开心，他有一套自己的讽刺幽默感。他洞察力极强，总是在问各种各样的问题。他会注意到街上的谁是不是心情糟糕，并指出来。这倒真的督促了我多上心。”(2/2) “He’s my nephew. I watch him two or three days a week while my sister is at work. Last night we went to see a play and today we’re just running errands. It’s nice to be an uncle because I can enjoy his company without feeling the burden of providing for him. We have a lot of fun. He’s got his own sarcastic sense of humor. He’s very inquisitive. He’s always asking about things. He’ll notice if people on the street are feeling bad, and he’ll point them out. It really forces me to be present.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqpXIukTumblr: http://t.cn/RqpXI3PTwitter: http://t.cn/RqpXI3vInstagram: http://t.cn/RqpXIuF
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DsjxA54n5&u=005trlAagw1f36s8l2orpj31kw11x47k )

>  2016 年 3 月 6 日(1/2) “我想要成为一名工程师，因为这样你就可以利用各种技术来帮助别人了。但是首先我得掌握好除法竖式。我想做的事其中一件就是给军人们制造更便宜的假肢。有一天我觉得无聊就在谷歌上搜索了一下，我看到假肢要花 3500 美元。也许我能够使用同样的方法来制造，但利用的是资源回收后的材料。”(1/2) “I want to be an engineer because you get to mess around with technology and help people. But first I need to get better at long division. One thing I’d like to do is make cheaper prosthetics for people in the army. One day I was bored so I googled them and saw that they cost $3500. Maybe I can make them the same way but with recycled materials.”Facebook: http://t.cn/Rqp4SMnTumblr: http://t.cn/Rqp4SMmTwitter: http://t.cn/Rqp4SM3Instagram: http://t.cn/Rqp4SMu

>  2016 年 3 月 5 日“在我们的女儿出生之前我们经历过五到六次流产。她是双胞胎中的一个，但另一个还是流产了。因此，我们把她称为我们的奇迹宝宝。她出生的时候我已经四十岁了。我们在很多方面都很亲近。我们总是一起去露营、登山。她一直以来都很喜欢小动物及其他的生物。小时候的她总是会捉些小蛇、青蛙和昆虫等等。她也求过我们养一只小狗，而当我们最终给了她一只小狗后，她给它取了名叫‘妹妹’。如今，她在俄亥俄州的兽医学院学习，经常寄些照片给我们，上周她还接生了一对双胞胎山羊。我已经到了快退休的年纪，但是在她的生活稳定下来之前，我打算继续工作。在此之后我才能放松下来。我们已经为她支付了本科的学费。兽医学院的学费她自己贷了款，而我们都同意由她自己来还贷。但是你懂的，以防万一我还是会继续工作的。直到她有稳定的生活，然后我就能放松了。”“We had five or six miscarriages before we had our daughter. She was a twin, but the other one miscarried. So we call her our miracle baby. I was forty when she was born. We were close in every way. We’d always go camping and hiking together. She’s always loved animals and creatures. When she was little, she’d always pick up snakes and frogs and insects. She begged us for a dog, and when we finally got her one, she called it her ‘sister.’ Now she’s in vet school in Ohio. She sends me pictures all the time. She delivered twin goats last week. I’m getting to the point where I’d like to retire, but I’m going to keep working until she’s in a place where she feels secure. Then I can finally relax. We paid for her undergrad already. She took out loans for vet school, and we’ve agreed she’s going to pay them back herself. But you know, just in case, I’m going to keep working until she feels secure. Then I can relax.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqCszE4Tumblr: http://t.cn/RqCszEqTwitter: http://t.cn/RqCszE5Instagram: http://t.cn/RqCszEb

>  2016 年 3 月 4 日“我的工作是分发报纸。我本来打算在高中毕业后只工作几个月的，但结果我一做就是三年。我不想自己一辈子都困在一个没有前途的工作里。我应该去读大学，但说起来容易做起来难。每次只要发生任何细枝末节的变化，我就会推迟。我不清楚，也许我是有抑郁吧。小时候我会整晚不睡地研究软件，我会下载程序、更改源代码，然后试着运行，我就是会对即将发生的事情产生好奇。而如果代码无效，我会不断尝试。我对此特别钟爱，觉得乐趣无穷。有时我会整晚不睡。最近，我试着重新研究软件代码，但是我再也感觉不到任何的乐趣了。做什么都感觉是项工作。”“I distribute newspapers. I only planned on working for a few months after I graduated high school, but that turned into three years. I don’t want to be stuck in a dead end job my whole life. I should go to college. I just have a hard time following through. The moment any little thing goes wrong, I just put it off. I don’t know, maybe I’m depressed. When I was a kid, I’d stay up all night messing with software. I’d download a program, change the source code, and try to run it. I just wanted to see what would happen. If it didn’t work, I’d keep trying. I loved it. It was fun. Sometimes I’d stay up all night. Recently I tried to do it again, but nothing felt fun anymore. Everything just feels like work.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqCDqdCTumblr: http://t.cn/RqCDqd9Twitter: http://t.cn/RqCDqd0Instagram: http://t.cn/RqCDqdp

>  2016 年 3 月 3 日“没人知道我吸烟的事实，所以我确保自己离开宾馆走了两条街。我正试着让自己冷静下来。我们的年度大会就在今晚，而我是整个大会的负责人。我筹办这个大会已经好几个月了。在此以前，我在家休整了好长一段时间来照顾我的孩子们，而我重新开始全职工作才仅仅一年。我想留下一个好的印象。我们机构从未有过女性担任领导，所以这真的是件大事，也是我人生中的大事。这无关于我的丈夫或我的孩子们，这是真真正正我自己掌控的事。而我也想要获得成功，我想要我的孩子们知道：我是妈妈，但我也仍然是我自己。”“Nobody knows that I smoke so I made sure to walk a couple blocks from the hotel. I’m trying to calm myself. Our annual general meeting is tonight and I’m in charge of the whole thing. I’ve been planning it for months. I took a long time off to raise my kids, and I’ve only been back working full time for a year. I want to make a good impression. Our organization has never really had a woman in leadership before, so it’s a big deal. And it’s a big deal for me. This isn’t about my husband or my kids. It’s something just for me that I can embrace fully. And I want to succeed. I want my children to know that I’m Mommy, but I’m still myself.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqCKjNKTumblr: http://t.cn/RqCKjNSTwitter: http://t.cn/RqCKjNoInstagram: http://t.cn/RqCKjNX

>  2016 年 3 月 3 日“我以为自己会在这儿发达。我有工商管理硕士和工程学硕士学位。在巴西的时候我为一家大型的房地产开发企业工作过，负责土地征用。他们会告诉我说：‘Bruno，给我们找些机会来。’而我则会找到好的地产谈判价格。我带来了巨额收入，觉得自己很有分量。当我和富人及政治家们交谈时，我会觉得自己是他们的同侪——不是傲慢的那一面，而是我不会在与他们交谈之时觉得自己低他们一等。纽约真的打击了我的自信心。我来的时候向五十多家公司递交了申请，也许有一百多家，但是没有一家录用了我。八月份我的小女儿就要出生了，所以我现在正努力地做着房地产经纪人的工作，但是这份工作也不容易。目前我只谈妥了一笔交易，还是和另外一名经纪人平分的。也许这都是因为我的英文还不够好。前不久我建议了一位有钱的女士在展示她的公寓之前先打扫一下，因此冒犯了她。我把一些积了灰尘的地方给她看了看，而她却告诉我说别再来找她。那让我很难受，因为我曾引以为豪的人际技能，如今似乎也不复存在了。但是我觉得事情终于开始出现转机了。我有两笔交易排定在这个月。而昨天我花了一整天和一位来自中国的女士在一起，她几乎说不了几句英语，但昨天的最后她告诉了我说：‘我信任你。’”“I thought I would thrive here. I’ve got an MBA and a Masters in Engineering. I worked for a major real estate developer back in Brazil. I was in charge of land acquisitions. They would tell me: ‘Bruno, go find opportunities for us.’ I’d locate good properties and then negotiate a price. I generated a lot of revenue. I felt powerful. When I spoke to rich people and politicians, I’d feel like their equal. Not in an arrogant way. But I did not feel inferior when I spoke to them. Coming to New York has really challenged my confidence. I applied to over fifty companies when I arrived. Maybe one hundred. But nobody hired me. I have a new daughter coming in August, so now I’m trying to work as a real estate broker. But that has been very difficult too. I’ve only closed one deal so far, and I split that with another broker. Maybe it’s because my English is not perfect. Recently I offended a wealthy lady by suggesting she clean her apartment before showing it. I showed her some dust and she told me to never come back. That was really tough for me because I was really proud of my people skills. And now it seemed that even those had left me. But I think that things are finally beginning to turn around. I have two closings scheduled this month. And yesterday I spent all day with a lady from China, and she barely spoke English, but at the end of the day, she told me: ‘I trust you.’”Anyone who needs a broker can contact Bruno here: bruno.marmo@elliman.comFacebook: http://t.cn/RqCSc4ETumblr: http://t.cn/RqCSc4QTwitter: http://t.cn/RqCSc4RInstagram: http://t.cn/RqCSc48

>  2016 年 3 月 2 日“我的专业是会计，去年五月毕业之后就搬到这里来了。但是四个月过去之后我仍然没能找到一份工作。我把自己的简历寄去了大概三十多个不同的地方，等待电话回复。到最后我真的是没办法再等下去了，于是便亲自去了囊括所有汽车经销商的商业区，开始挨个向他们询问会计方面的就职机会。我一直都很喜爱汽车，过去我总是会和我爸一起看《消费者报告》，所以我认为自己干这行会很适合。宝马的那位女士有点冷漠。然后我去了奥迪，他们的人很不错、非常友好，但是他们当时没有任何职位空缺。之后我去了捷豹路虎——他们也是我的第一选择，所以我一直都在为此努力——而他们也让我坐下，直接在那里就面试了我。我在那里呆了一下午，之后他们说：‘我们目前看起来很满意，你能明天就开始吗？’我跑着到外面给我的父母打了电话。我爸爸为我感到非常地骄傲。我也为自己感到自豪。”“I graduated last May with an accounting degree and moved to the city. But four months had passed and I didn’t have a job yet. I’d probably sent out my resume to thirty different places. And I couldn’t afford to keep waiting for people to call me back. So I went to the strip with all the car dealerships, and started going door-to-door to see if they had any openings in accounting. I’ve always loved cars. I used to always read Consumer Reports with my dad. So I thought it would be a good fit. The lady at BMW was a bit standoffish. Then I went to Audi. They were great. Super welcoming. But they didn’t have any positions at the moment. Then I got to Jaguar/Land Rover—which was my first choice, so I was working up to it— and they sat me down right there for an interview. I was there all afternoon, then they said: ‘We like what we see. Can you start tomorrow?’ I ran outside and called my parents. My dad was so proud of me. I was so proud of myself.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqC6EIvTumblr: http://t.cn/RqC6EfsTwitter: http://t.cn/RqC6EIPInstagram: http://t.cn/RqC6EIh

>  2016 年 3 月 1 日(2/2) “想让人们对你的作品感到满意是一股巨大的推动力。任何对此持异议的艺术家不是自私的便是自闭的。艺术是一种沟通，它并不与你承认自己渴望听众相矛盾。一次公开演出就是一个奇迹。你从来都不会知道是谁在注视着你，但是你却能感受到存在于你自己、听众们和两百年前谱下这些音符的作曲家之间的沟通。然而，让音符见鬼去吧。音符是不重要的，它们只是作曲家们唯一的沟通桥梁，真正重要的是音符与音符之间及其背后所蕴含的。我作为钢琴家的职责是去领悟。为什么作者要把那个音符放在那里？我首先需要明白那个音符之前的片段。而当那发生之时——当我能够穿越回到两百年之前与一位作曲家心领神会时，即便我是完全自己一个人，那份沟通的感受却是和我在一大群听众面前演奏的感受如出一辙。”(2/2) “Pleasing people is a huge drive. Any artist who tells you otherwise is either selfish or autistic. Art is a communication, and it’s not incompatible with your integrity to desire an audience. A public performance is a miracle. You never know who’s watching, but you feel a communion between yourself, the audience, and the composer who wrote the notes two hundred years ago. But fuck the notes. The notes are not important. They were the composer’s only means of communicating. The important thing is what’s between the notes and behind the notes. My job as a pianist is to interpret. Why did the composer put that note there? I need to understand the moment preceding the note. And when that happens—when I can reach back two hundred years and connect to a composer’s humanity, even if I’m completely alone, it’s the same feeling of communion as when I perform in front of an audience.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqK0djoTumblr: http://t.cn/RqK0djSTwitter: http://t.cn/RqK0djKInstagram: http://t.cn/RqK0dj9
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DrHA90t7S&u=005trlAagw1f324nrzejgj31kw11xjvu )

>  2016 年 3 月 1 日(1/2) “我是一名钢琴家。周四晚我会演奏自己最后一场音乐会。然后我就会开始休假。我的一些朋友认为我现在就离开简直是疯了，但是我不想成为一个每年举办两百场音乐会的演奏机器。这需要我展现极高的效率，而高效率是会让你精疲力竭的。在林肯中心或者卡内基音乐厅演奏时的压力是巨大的——大家花钱买了票，你也因而必须尊重你的观众们。如果你正在驾驶一架载有四百名乘客的波音 777，你是不会去尝试任何新技巧的，你是不会把它当作乐趣或者实验来看待的，你也不会有时间沉浸在自己的梦想和新意中的。你需要从大众眼前隐退，好让自己有空间成长。我不会说适时地放空自己会让你变成一位‘更好’的音乐家，因为我不喜欢‘更好’这个词，听起来太好胜了；但是这确实会让你变得更人性化，而不是机械化，就好像探索一片新大陆一样。休假给了你空间去让‘已知’ 以外事情的发生成为可能。”(1/2) “I’m a pianist. I’m playing my last concert Thursday night. Then I’m taking a sabbatical. Some of my friends think I’m crazy to step away now, but I don’t want to become a two-hundred-concert-per-year performing machine. It requires too much efficiency. And the efficiency burns you out. There is a lot of pressure when you perform at Lincoln Center or Carnegie Hall. People pay for those tickets and you must respect your audience. If you’re piloting a Boeing 777 with four hundred people on board, you aren’t going to try new maneuvers. You aren’t going to have fun or experiment. You don’t have time to stay in your dreams or ideas. You need to step back from the public eye so you have space to grow. I won’t say that taking time off makes you a ‘better’ musician, because I don’t like the word ‘better.’ It sounds competitive. But it does make you less of an automaton and more human. It’s like exploring a new continent. Time off is a space where you allow things to happen other than the known.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqKK6joTwitter: http://t.cn/RqKK6jSInstagram: http://t.cn/RqKK6ja
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DrGMEgVWU&u=005trlAagw1f3212r1nibj311x1kwgsp )

>  2016 年 2 月 29 日“我正打算着建立起一段稳定的恋爱关系，然而，让我预想这件事的发生都非常困难。我已经不再年轻了，也没有一个家庭，实在是提供不了什么。再加上，我已经很久没有谈过恋爱了，所以几乎都不知道该怎么办。我在一家销售中心工作，所以一整天周围都是人、摩肩接踵。这还不算太坏。当我回到家，弄好晚餐之后——这才是真的寂静。这时候我才意识到我现在的处境并非我所想要的，而我也不知道如何才能摆脱困境。”“I’m looking to establish a solid relationship with somebody. But it’s hard for me to imagine it happening. I’m not a kid anymore. I don’t have a home. I don’t have a heck of a lot to offer. Plus, it’s been a long time since I’ve had any sort of relationship, so I’ve kind of lost track of how to deal with all that. I work at a sales center so I’m surrounded by people all day, elbow-to-elbow. It’s not so bad then. But then I go home, fix dinner, and bang—it all shuts off. That’s when I realize that I’m not in the situation that I want to be in. And I’m not sure how to get out of it.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqSoeOPTumblr: http://t.cn/RqSoeO7Twitter: http://t.cn/RqSoeOhInstagram: http://t.cn/RqSoeOw

>  2016 年 2 月 26 日“我们是在缅因州的夏令营认识的。我第一次见到他时，他穿着衣服正在游泳池做炮弹跳水。我们第一次接吻是躺在一张蹦床上。今年夏天我们会回去这个夏令营举办婚礼。我们完全是走火入魔的节奏，所有的来宾都会睡在木屋里，同时我们也会有篝火、烤棉花糖、套圈游戏、乒乓球以及寻宝活动。”“We met at summer camp in Maine. >  2016 年 2 月 25 日“孩子们都搬了出去。我们过去这二十五年如一日，如今终于都结束了。突然间就只剩下我们两个人了，没有其他的东西让我们去专注，这因此也成为了一个我们重新发现自我的过程。我们刚刚买了登山背包，打算环游世界，而且我们准备说走就走。”“The kids have moved out.
