>  2016 年 2 月 25 日“我十九岁的时候我们就结了婚。我那时很年轻，她比我稍大一点，所以我不介意凡事听她的。最初的十到十五年里，一切都好。然后我记得有一天自己环顾四周，发现房子里没有一件家具是我自己挑选的。我突然就不再用‘好的，亲爱的’、‘好的，亲爱的’、‘好的，亲爱的’来回答她所有的吩咐了，而这也是我们争吵的开端。最终，我们不论为什么事情都会吵起来。为了要不要在厨房里安装轨道灯，我们吵了六个月。到了最后，我们之间几乎不再说话。我们坐在同一间房里，除了讽刺挖苦之外什么话都不说。更不要提性了，她对此已毫无兴趣。事情糟糕到我为了避免回家，只能整晚呆在办公室里。我保证如果你问我妻子的话，她绝不会和你讲那糟糕的十年，她会告诉你我找了一个女朋友之后就搬了出去。”“We married when I was nineteen. I was young. She was a bit older, and I was fine doing things her way. Things were good for the first ten or fifteen years. Then I remember looking around one day and realizing that there wasn’t a single piece of furniture in the house that I’d picked out. And suddenly I stopped answering all her commands with, ‘Yes dear,’ ‘Yes, dear,’ ‘Yes,dear.’ And that’s when the fighting started. Eventually we were fighting about everything. We argued for six months about whether to put track lighting in the kitchen. We hardly ever talked toward the end. We’d sit in the same room and not speak a word unless it was a snide comment. And forget about sex. She didn’t believe in that anymore. It got so bad that I’d literally stay in the office all night to avoid going home. I’m sure if you asked my ex-wife though, she won’t tell you about the ten years that sucked. She’ll tell you about when I got a girlfriend and moved out of the house.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RqSZTxzTumblr: http://t.cn/RGNBlimTwitter: http://t.cn/RqSZTxZInstagram: http://t.cn/RqSZTx7

>  2016 年 2 月 24 日“我妻子得乳腺癌最初是在 1999 年，然而去年又再次复发，并且已经扩散到骨头里了。去年我过得一团糟，只要我不在忙，就会忍不住地开始哭泣。之后我把这一切都交给了上帝，且真正地和他对了话。我说：‘全交给你了。’而从那以后，我感觉好多了。我们仍抱有希望。我们认识一个罹患骨癌的人病情恶化到她的骨头都开始断裂，而上个月她体内已经检测不到癌细胞了，所以我们是有希望的。某种意义上这件事也完善了我。我想让她的时光尽可能地愉快，所以每当有冲突时，我都不再像以前那样强硬了。我会退让，即使错的是她。我会退让，直到我们都冷静下来之后再重新审视。”“My wife first got breast cancer in 1999. Then it came back last year, and it’s in the bones now. I was a mess last year. Any time I wasn’t busy, I’d just start crying uncontrollably. Then I handed it over to God. I actually spoke to him, and said: ‘It’s all yours.’ And I’ve felt better since then. We’re hopeful. We know somebody whose bone cancer got so bad that her bones were breaking, and last month she tested completely clear. So we’re hopeful. It’s made me a better person in a way. I want her time to be as good as possible, so whenever there’s a confrontation, I don’t push it like I used to. I’ll just back away from it. Even if she’s wrong. I’ll back away and we’ll revisit it later when everyone is calm.”Facebook: http://t.cn/Rq6g3MWTumblr: http://t.cn/Rq6g3M0Twitter: http://t.cn/Rq6g3MOInstagram: http://t.cn/Rq6g3Ml

>  2016 年 2 月 24 日“我一直想在时装领域出人头地，也许成为杂志社的一名时装设计。然而我只是一家制药公司的办公室助理。但我还是得说，我觉得因为我，我们办公室整体变得更加赏心悦目了。我经常给大家支招，而大家也开始打扮了起来。有些姑娘们正在尝试新的唇彩。我们都越来越放得开了。”“I always wanted to be someone in the fashion industry. >  2016 年 2 月 23 日“小时候我可奇怪了。我喜爱复古的服饰，以为自己只要在开学第一天穿上一条 1950 年代的黄色太阳裙和搭配的上衣，整个六年级的人就都会喜欢上我了。到我进了高中之后，我意识到所有其他奇怪的孩子们都在戏剧小组，于是我便开始把自己所有的业余时间都花在戏剧部。我担任的是服装设计师。说是服装设计师，其实我就是把别人免费送给我们的几箱蹩脚货都整理好的那个人而已。”“I was a weird kid. I loved vintage clothes. I assumed that if I wore a 1950’s yellow sundress and matching jacket on the first day of school, everyone in sixth grade would love me. When I got to high school, I realized that all the other weird kids were in theater, so I started spending all my free time in the theater department. I was the costume designer. And by costume designer, I mean the person who organized the boxes of free shit people gave us.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RGs2ZrmTumblr: http://t.cn/RGs2ZrRTwitter: http://t.cn/RGs2ZrnInstagram: http://t.cn/RGs2ZrE

>  2016 年 2 月 22 日“我的圆号前不久坏了。金属因为磨损到太薄，所以失去了原本的音质。我感觉自己就像个寡妇一般。最好的圆号都是手工制造的，所以每一管圆号都有细小的差别。那管圆号我演奏了二十年了，伴我经历了研究生的岁月、我的第一份工作、所有我参与过的重大比赛，并最终让我如愿以偿得到了歌剧院的工作。我了解它所有的不足之处，能够巧妙地利用它。我还没找到能替代它的圆号。这管新圆号我已经用了七个月了，我们一见钟情，但是我演奏得越多就越担心。我还不太适应它的吹嘴，但是即使这段关系最终没能修成正果，我也相信自己会找到另一管圆号的。希望常在嘛。”“My horn died recently. The metal wore too thin and it lost its resonance. I feel like a widow. The best horns are handmade, and each one is a little different. I’d been playing it for twenty years. It was with me through my graduate degrees, my first job, all my major competitions, and when I finally got my dream job at the opera. I knew all its deficiencies. I could do so many things with it. I haven’t been able to replace it yet. I’ve had this new horn for seven months. There was an immediate attraction, but the more I play, the more I worry. The mouthpiece doesn’t quite seem to fit. But even if this relationship doesn’t work out, I’m sure there will be another. Hope springs eternal.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RGFzTJETwitter: http://t.cn/RGFzTJnInstagram: http://t.cn/RGFzTJR

>  2016 年 2 月 22 日“八年前我们不得不带着两个行李箱和我们的宝宝离开俄罗斯。我的丈夫是一名记者，当时他正在报道车臣的事件。他所犯下的唯一罪行就是说出了真相。克格勃的人到了我们家拿走了我们所有的证件。他们剥夺了我们的公民身份。我们不得不以红十字的旅行文件出逃。我们不得不从头来过。我们俩当时都不会说英语。我的丈夫在俄罗斯是一名非常有地位的记者，但是在这里他只能修理游泳池。现在他拥有健壮的肌肉，但是却非常沮丧。我为自己则感到骄傲。我来这里的时候是 30 岁，那时我觉得非常孤单，什么也没有，但是我教会了自己英语、教会了自己开车。大都会歌剧院给了我这个在服装店缝纫的工作。虽然那时候我还不会说英语，他们还是给了我这个机会。我还记得在这里开始工作了几周后，我的一个同事给了我一条不再合她身的连衣裙。那是我第一次觉得自己与这个国家不再分离。我有了归属感。”“We had to leave Russia eight years ago with two suitcases and our baby. My husband was a journalist. He was making reports about Chechnya. His only crime was telling the truth. The KGB came to our house and took all of our papers. They took our citizenship. We had to leave the country with Red Cross travel documents. We had to start over. Neither of us could speak English. My husband was an important journalist in Russia, but here he fixes swimming pools. Now he has big muscles but he’s very sad. I am very proud of myself. I was 30 years old when I came to here. I felt very alone. I had nothing. But I taught myself English. I taught myself to drive. The Metropolitan Opera gave me a job as a stitcher in the costume shop. They gave me a chance even though I didn’t speak English. I remember after a few weeks of working here, one of my coworkers gave me a dress that didn’t fit her anymore. It was the first time that I did not feel separate from this country. It felt like I belonged.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RGuu9AnTumblr: http://t.cn/RGuu9AETwitter: http://t.cn/RGuu9AmInstagram: http://t.cn/RGuu9Au

>  2016 年 2 月 21 日“我的父母在还未成年的时候就有了我弟弟和我。我母亲在很早的时候就抛弃了我们。我父亲告诉我们说她有躁郁症。我还记得自己九岁还是十岁的时候和我弟弟一起去公共图书馆试图查明‘躁郁’是什么意思。之后的几年，我妈在我们的生活中偶尔出现、后又消失。她从来没有长时间地陪在我们身边。我的父亲也没有好到哪里去。他几乎从来都不在家。我弟弟和我不得不自己照顾自己。学校是我唯一的出路，我参与了一切活动：舞蹈队、学生会、荣誉社团等等，甚至是举重。我是我们家第一个上大学的人，之后我在哥伦比亚大学读了研究生，而现在我是大学低收入家庭学生的辅导员。我和我父母中任何一方都不再说话。我妈每过一段时间会发短信给我，但我从不回复。她喜欢想象她自己在我取得成功的过程中起了作用。她的办公室里到处都是我的照片。她和她的同事讲的都是关于我的事，就好像她一直都是我生活中的一部分那样。而我不想她拥有这种满足感，因为所有的一切都是‘尽管有她’，而不是‘因为有她’。”“My parents were teenagers when they had my brother and me. My mother abandoned us early on. My father told us she was manic-depressive. I remember going to the public library with my brother when I was nine or ten, trying to find out what ‘manic depressive’ meant. Mom came in and out of our lives over the next few years. She never stayed long. My father wasn’t much better. He was hardly ever home. My brother and I had to raise ourselves. School was my only outlet. I did everything: dance team, student council, honors society, even powerlifting. I was the first from my family to go to college. I went to graduate school at Columbia, and now I’m a college counselor for low-income students. I don’t talk to either of my parents. My mom sends me texts every once in awhile, but I don’t answer. She likes to imagine that she played a part in my accomplishments. She has pictures of me all over her office. She tells her coworkers all about me as if she’d been part of my life. And I don’t want her to have that satisfaction. Because it was all in spite of her. Not because of her.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RGRnWSdTumblr: http://t.cn/RGRnWSDTwitter: http://t.cn/RGRnWSgInstagram: http://t.cn/RGRnWSe

>  2016 年 2 月 21 日“我有段 25 年的婚姻和五个孩子，但是我却放任自己在做选择时被情感而左右。我有过婚外情，但都是自己的内心在作怪。我认为自己有种渴望，就是想看见自己在别人眼中是个优秀的男人。我的妻子人也很不错，直至今日她依然很不错，但是 25 年的婚姻之后事情都安定了下来，而当另一个人出现在你生活中并让你感觉与众不同的时候——这感觉就像猫薄荷一样，你会想要更多，你会想要说：‘什么时候我们共进午餐吧。’然而最终，你还是你，无论别人让你自我感觉如何。那终究只是种感觉。而我只希望自己没有去追随它。”“I was married for 25 years and had five children, but I allowed myself to make decisions based on emotional glitches. I had affairs. But they were affairs of the heart. I think I had a hunger to see myself as a great man in someone else’s eyes. My wife was a fine person, and she still is, but after 25 years of marriage things become settled. And when somebody else comes along and makes you feel like something special—it’s like catnip. You want more of it. You want to say: ‘Let’s get lunch sometime.’ But in the end, you are what you are no matter how somebody makes you feel. It’s just a feeling. And I wish I hadn’t chased it.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RG8l5aQTumblr: http://t.cn/RG8l5aYTwitter: http://t.cn/RG8l5aHInstagram: http://t.cn/RG8l5aT

>  2016 年 2 月 20 日“我直到 51 岁才开始跑步。那个时候，我就是个窝囊废，什么都不是。我的婚姻散了场，只有周末才能见到自己的孩子们。我的睡眠也不好，每天早晨 5:30 就醒了，很大可能性是在之前的一晚喝得酩酊大醉，所以我决定自己不妨出去散个步。在公园里走的时候，我总是能看见这些跑步的人。于是我决定自己也试一试。几周之后，我就已经能够跑下六英里了。一年之后，我试着跑一场马拉松，在二十英里处我遭遇了瓶颈，但是在我呕吐完并撒了一泼尿之后，我又找回活力跑完了全程。从那以后，我便在不断地跨越瓶颈。十七年间我跑过十六场马拉松，直到我的医生告诉我说因为心脏问题我不得不停止。在那之后，我开始每天行走十英里。现在我 91 岁了，我的膝盖骨总是错位，而我的平衡也经常出问题，但是我依然比年轻时候的自己要自信。以前我是个窝囊废。”“I didn’t start running until I was 51 years old. I was a wimp at the time. A nothing. My marriage had fallen apart. I was only seeing my children on the weekends. I wasn’t sleeping well. I was waking up at 5:30 AM every morning, probably after a long night of drinking, and so I decided that I might as well go for a walk. As I walked around the park, I’d always see these runners out there. So I decided to give that a try. After a few weeks I could run six miles. After a year, I tried to run a marathon. I hit a wall at the twenty-mile mark, but I threw up and took a leak, then I found the energy to finish. I’ve been pushing through walls ever since. I ran sixteen marathons in seventeen years, until my doctor told me that I had to stop because of my heart. After that, I started walking ten miles a day. Now I’m 91 and my kneecap keeps collapsing, and I have trouble with my balance. But I’m still more confident than I ever was when I was younger. I was a wimp.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RG8pDLZTumblr: hhttp://t.cn/RG8pDL2Twitter: http://t.cn/RG8pDLwInstagram: http://t.cn/RG8pDLA
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Dlg5Hs4dF&u=005trlAajw1f1p4zyo299j31kw11xgvd )

>  2016 年 2 月 19 日“我一直在做演员，而最近我觉得自己的生活已经变得枯燥。我们需要钱来付房租、学费等天底下所有的账单，我们也很快想要一个孩子，因此我们真的非常需要积蓄。前不久我们在吃披萨时促膝而谈，讨论了我们的经济状况。她让我相信自己并不是个蠢货。”“我往往是我们俩之间比较务实的那个。我告诉他说：‘这不是你的问题。这都是暂时的。’我们只需要从最基本的事情开始解决就行了。Eric 需要表演和拍电影，而他做这些事情的时候我最开心了。我们只需要做一点小小的改变能解决账目的问题了。他非常有才华，但他也太多次答应别人做事却不求回报了。没有人会要求一位律师免费为其工作，但是演员和艺术家们却经常收到这样的请求。如果 Eric 喜欢那个人的话，他会为其工作 80 个小时都不求回报。因为你对自己从事的工作非常热忱，所以做一些无偿的项目也并无不妥，但是你必须要拥有强烈的感召。每一次机会，我们都要问问自己的热忱是不是比拿报酬更可贵。”“I’ve been working as an actor and I’ve been in a bit of a rut recently. We need money for rent, school, every bill under the sun. And we want to have a kid soon, so we should really be putting money away for that. We sat down over pizza recently to figure out our finances. She helped convince me that I’m not an idiot.”“I tend to be the more practical one in the relationship. I told him: ‘This isn’t you. This is just right now.’ We’ve just got to start from the basics and figure things out. Eric needs to be acting and making films, and I’m happiest when he’s doing those things. We just need to make a few small adjustments to make the numbers work. He’s extremely talented, but he agrees to do too many things for free. Nobody would ever ask a lawyer to work for free. But actors and artists get asked all the time. And if Eric likes the person, he’ll work for 80 hours with no compensation. It’s fine to do unpaid projects because you’re passionate. But you have to feel really strongly about it. In each case, we’ve got to ask if the passion is worth more than the dollars.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RGQTwiOTumblr: http://t.cn/RGQTwijTwitter: http://t.cn/RGQTwiCInstagram: http://t.cn/RGQTwiK

>  2016 年 2 月 18 日“我是在加拿大的一个小镇上长大的。我从来都不是那种拥有很多朋友的人。我更符合那种只拥有‘一个好朋友’的类型，而且通常都是和一个女生，所以我从来都没有真正地和一大群人打成过一片。我很害怕社交场合。我认为音乐才是我连接自己与人类情感的方式，而这种连接却是那时的我日常生活中所得不到的。过去我们的客厅里有一架古老的立式钢琴，我每天都会练习五到六个小时。很多时间我都是自己一个人。最初，音乐是我逃避的去处，但是最终，它所给予我的自信，让我与他人的相处变得更为自在了。”“I grew up in a small town in Canada. I was never the type who had a lot of friends. I was more the type that had ‘a friend.’ It would usually be a girl. So I never really felt connected with the larger group of kids. I was intimidated by social gatherings. I think music was my way of connecting with human emotion in a way that I wasn’t getting in everyday life. We had an old upright piano in the living room. I’d practice for five or six hours every day. I spent a lot of time alone. Music was my escape at first. But in the end it gave me a confidence that made it easier to relate to other people.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RGTguXYTumblr: http://t.cn/RGTguXHTwitter: http://t.cn/RGTguXRInstagram: http://t.cn/RGTguXT

>  2016 年 2 月 18 日“我觉得年轻的时候你每天都在变化，但是现在我十五岁了，就开始真正成为一个人了。所有的事情都渐渐慢了下来，而我正像一座泥雕一样开始晾干。这挺吓人的，因为我开始在意到别人将如何来看待我，了解到别人将对我形成的看法。”“但是这并不一定正确。变化也许会慢下来，但是也会变得更加着意。在你这个年龄，你会经历不同以往的事情，并扮演不同的角色，就像一个演员一样。然而，你能思考出那么多东西已经让我很自豪。你非常擅长处理复杂的情绪。我唯一害怕的事情是你的学习驾照和来拱白菜的猪。”“I feel like when you’re young, you change every day. But I feel like now that I’m fifteen, I’m becoming a person. Everything is slowing down and I’m starting to dry like a mud statue. And it’s scary. Because I’m realizing the way that people are going to see me. And I’m learning the things that people are going to think about me.”“But that’s not necessarily true. Change may slow down, but it becomes more deliberate. At this age you get to experience different things and try different personas, just like an actress. But it makes me proud how much you’re thinking through these things. You’re very good at managing complex emotions. Only thing I’m worried about is your learner's permit and the dogginess of boys.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RGTInrGTumblr: http://t.cn/RGTInrqTwitter: http://t.cn/RGTInrbInstagram: http://t.cn/RGTInr5

>  2016 年 2 月 17 日“在高中的时候我认识一个总是抱怨自己有焦虑症的女孩子。那会儿我不时地会取笑她，因为在我看来这根本就是子虚乌有，所以我也默认这是件子虚乌有的事情。我处理的办法就是试着说服她这是件子虚乌有的事。前不久我打电话给她向她道了歉。自从我父亲死后，我就患有非常严重的焦虑症。这绝对不是子虚乌有，而是无端地对于子虚乌有的事抱有难以名状的恐惧。”“I knew a girl in high school that always complained about having anxiety. I used to make fun of her a little bit. It looked like nothing to me. So I assumed it was nothing. And I dealt with it by trying to convince her that it was nothing. I called her recently to apologize. I’ve had really bad anxiety ever since my father died. And it’s definitely not nothing. It’s the indescribable fear of nothing.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RGYuMCgTumblr: http://t.cn/RGYuMCkTwitter: http://t.cn/RGYuMCrInstagram: http://t.cn/RGYuMCe

>  2016 年 2 月 17 日“我们把这个巨大的博物馆里所有的地方都走遍了。博物馆是你能看见艺术品和动物的地方。这家博物馆里的东西有耶稣啊这样的，我还看见了一个人正在砍头的雕塑。我一直在画这些雕塑，但是我画不好嘴唇，还有他们的手只有三个手指而不是五个，因为这样画起来简单些。我也许不应该给你看这一幅，因为……我不想说出来。你能看见他们的……他们的……他们的……屁屁。”“We walked all around this big museum. A museum is a place where you can see art or animals. This museum has stuff like Jesus and I saw a statue of somebody cutting a head. I’ve been drawing the statues but I’m not good at drawing lips, and the hands have three fingers instead of five because that’s easier. I probably shouldn’t show you this one because… I don’t want to say it. You can see their… their… their…. BUTTS.”Facebook: http://t.cn/RGYq68HTumblr: http://t.cn/RGYq68YTwitter: http://t.cn/RGYq68QInstagram: http://t.cn/RGYq68T

>  2016 年 2 月 14 日“我教授普通教育发展的课程已经 21 年了，成功帮助超过 300 名学生取得了他们的证书。我最近有一位学生——他已经 50 岁了，却只有六年级的文化水平。他坐在班级的最后，什么话也不说，只是默默地看着。一天，有一道很难的代数题没人能够答上来，他自告奋勇到黑板上试着解题，并且解对了，而且是在所有人的面前。第二天我到达的时候，他已经坐在班级的最前面了。课后我递给了他一大本复习提纲，告诉他说：‘若你给出四分之一的努力，我就会给出剩下的四分之三。’我告诉他说他能在任何时候打断我向我提问。他也确实这么做了，几乎每过几个小时他就会来找我——在餐厅、在我打牌的时候、在我看电影的时候。九个月后他参加了考试并且通过了。他太自豪了。他说他迫不及待地要告诉自己的女儿了。几个月过后，我坐在访客室这里时，一位年轻女子不停地向我张望，望到我女朋友都开始觉得烦了。最终她向我走来，和我说：‘非常感谢你帮助我的父亲获取他的普通教育发展证书。’当时的那个感觉简直妙不可言。”（黑泽尔顿联邦惩教所，西弗吉尼亚州）“I’ve been teaching the GED course for 21 years. I’ve helped over 300 students get their certificates. I had one student recently—he was 50 years old and only had a 6th grade education. He sat in the back of the class and didn’t say anything. He just watched. But then one day there was a tough algebra problem that nobody could figure out. He volunteered to come up and tried it on the board, and he got it. In front of everybody. The next day when I arrived, he was sitting in the front. After class I handed him a huge study guide, and told him: ‘If you’ll give 25 percent, I’ll give you 75 percent.’ I told him he could interrupt me at any time to ask me questions. And he did. It seemed like he was coming up to me every few hours-- in the cafeteria, while I was playing cards, while I was watching movies. After nine months he took the test and passed. He was so proud. He said he couldn’t wait to tell his daughter. A few months later I was sitting here in the visiting room, and this young woman kept looking at me. So much so that my girlfriend was starting to get upset. Eventually she walked over to me, and said: ‘Thank you so much for helping my father get his GED.’ It was the best feeling in the world.”(Federal Correctional Complex: Hazelton, West Virginia)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGjwpiJTumblr: http://t.cn/RGjwpiiTwitter: http://t.cn/RGjwpi6Instagram: http://t.cn/RGjwpix

>  2016 年 2 月 13 日(4/4) “当 Donald 最终被抓获的时候，他们给他提供了一份认罪协议，这样我就不用坐牢了，但是他拒绝了。他告诉我的表兄说：‘如果我不能拥有她，那谁都别想。’Donald 拒签协议的同一天，他们便在法院逮捕了我。我的公设辩护人让我签下了一个控辩交易，他告诉我说不会有刑期，但是在宣判的时候，我听到法官提到了坐牢，我就慌了。当法官询问我是否被允诺了什么才作为交换签下了这个交易的时候，我说了：‘是的！’公诉人当时气疯了，她认为我让她颜面扫地。在庭审的时候，她主张要判我终身监禁。陪审团从来都没有听到家暴的事情，他们只听说了毒品的事情，他们没有意识到真正的受害者是我、我的孩子们和我哥。如今我已经坐了二十年牢了，但所幸还是有个美好的结局的。我发誓自己在答应这次采访的时候根本还不知道，但是总统奥巴马刚刚给予了我特赦。我就要回家了。”（大都会拘留中心，布鲁克林）(4/4) “When Donald finally got caught, they offered him a plea deal so I wouldn’t have to go to jail. But he refused it. He told my cousin: ‘If I can’t have her, nobody will.’ They arrested me at the courthouse on the same day Donald refused his deal. The public defender told me to sign a plea bargain. He told me no jail time. But at the sentencing, I heard the judge mention jail and I panicked. When the judge asked me if I’d been promised anything in exchange for the deal, I said: ‘Yes!’ The prosecutor was so mad. She thought I made her look bad. She pushed for a life sentence at trial. The jury never heard about the abuse. They only heard about the drugs. They didn’t realize that the true victims were me, my children, and my brother. I’ve been in prison for twenty years now. But this has a happy ending. And I swear, when I agreed to this interview, I didn’t even know this yet. But President Obama just granted me clemency. And I’m going home.”(Metropolitan Detention Center, Brooklyn)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGj7BsDTumblr: http://t.cn/RGj7BssTwitter: http://t.cn/RGj7BsFInstagram: http://t.cn/RGj7Bse

>  2016 年 2 月 13 日(3/4) “有一天晚上情况糟到我拿起了一把枪对准了他。我不会用枪，连保险栓是不是开着也不清楚。这时，我儿子走进了房间并试图站在我俩的中间。Donald 一下子跃过了他，把手枪抢了过去，并用枪柄砸伤了我。这件事发生之后，我再次试图逃跑。在 Donald 学习他的飞行课程的同时，我把所有的东西都打包进了我租的一辆搬家卡车里，迅速驱车离去，快得以致于拖车的部分在高速公路上脱了节。当 Donald 发现我人不见了之后，他派一群暴徒到了我哥家，在他全家人面前殴打了他。他们打完他之后告诉他说我母亲将是下一个。于是我就回去了。此后 Donald 便不再相信我。他开始逼我和他一起出差，不给我任何的选择。他会说：‘快打包。我们有活儿要干了。’他把我牵扯进了他所有的勾当，在他贩毒的时候逼我站在一旁，逼我打电话给别人并为他传递信息。他还让我运毒。他说什么我就做了什么。”（大都会拘留中心，布鲁克林）(3/4) “One night it got so bad that I got a gun and pointed it at him. I didn’t know how to use it. I didn’t even know if the safety was on. My son walked into the room at the time and tried to stand between us. Donald jumped over him, grabbed the gun, and pistol-whipped me. After that I tried to run away again. While Donald was taking flying lessons, I packed everything into a U-Haul and drove away so fast that the trailer came apart on the highway. When Donald discovered I was gone, he sent some goons to my brother’s house and beat him up in front of his entire family. When they finished beating him, they told him that my mother was next. So I went back. After that Donald didn’t trust me anymore. He made me start traveling with him. He didn’t give me a choice. He’d say: ‘Pack your bags. We’ve got business.’ He involved me with everything. He made me stand there while he dealt the drugs. He made me call people and relay messages for him. He had me make deliveries. I did everything he told me to.”(Metropolitan Detention Center, Brooklyn)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGjP6NoTumblr: http://t.cn/RGjP6NpTwitter: http://t.cn/RGjP6N9Instagram: http://t.cn/RGjP6NN

>  2016 年 2 月 13 日(2/4) “有一天我走进 Donald 的办公室，看见他正在把一包可卡因交给别人。我立刻转身离开了。之后他出来告诉我说，他这么做只是为了让自己的公司运转起来，他说他需要筹得 25,000 美元来负担费用。那个时候我很幼稚，我甚至打电话给我母亲让她帮忙安排一次小企业贷款。而 Donald 贩毒却开始越贩越多，并把我蒙在鼓里。他开始经常跑腿，开始每个月出两次差。在我分娩我们第一个孩子的那天，他开车把我送到医院说要去停车，却直到第二天才回来。家暴也变得越来越恶劣，他会把水泼在我身上、会用打火机烫我。在我怀着我们第二个孩子的时候，Donald 把电话机砸向了我的脑袋。在我入狱之后的一天晚上，我们看了一部关于蒂娜·特纳的电影，名叫‘与爱何干？’。其中有一个镜头是艾克·特纳扯着蒂娜的头发，沿着走廊拖着她，而她的儿子们则哭着看着这一切发生。我简直无法相信。我感觉自己就像在看一部记录自己生活的影片。”（大都会拘留中心，布鲁克林）(2/4) "One day I walked into Donald’s office and saw him handing off a package of cocaine. I turned around and left immediately. He came out later and told me that he was just doing it to get his business off the ground. He said he needed to raise $25,000 to cover expenses. I was naive at that point. I even called my mother and asked her to help arrange a small business loan. But Donald started dealing more and more. He kept it from me. He started running a lot of errands. He started taking trips twice a month. The day I went into labor with our first child, he dropped me off at the hospital and went to park the car. He didn’t come back until the next day. The abuse got worse and worse. He’d throw water on me. He’d burn me with a lighter. When I was pregnant with our second child, Donald hit me in the head with a telephone. After I got to prison, we watched a movie one night about Tina Turner, called ‘What’s Love Got To Do With It?’ There’s this one scene where Ike is dragging Tina down the hallway by her hair, and her sons are watching the whole thing and crying. I couldn’t believe it. I felt like I was watching a movie about my life.”(Metropolitan Detention Center, Brooklyn)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGlUDpSTumblr: http://t.cn/RGlUDpXTwitter: http://t.cn/RGlUDp6Instagram: http://t.cn/RGlUDpa

>  2016 年 2 月 13 日(1/4) “我遇见 Donald 的时候是二十六岁。他追我追得非常猛烈。他每天都会打电话给我。他会邀请我和他一起去巴哈马群岛。他会给我买各种各样的东西。他甚至会在周末把他的复古科尔维特借给我开。我那时还入世未深，并不习惯如此多的关注。他拥有自己的景观设计公司——包括他自己的大楼等等。他讨得了我全家人的喜欢，连我妈都喜欢他，而她可不是轻易就能被说服的。所以我便爱上了他。家暴直到我怀上了我们第一个孩子才开始。一天晚上我们正躺在床上，而他叫我给他倒一杯水。当我和他说了‘不’之后，他就对着我的脸揍了一拳。他说：‘当我叫你做一件事情的时候，你最好乖乖地去做。’我当时就试着离开了。我跑回了我在纽约的家，但是他跟着我到了纽约并求我原谅他。他说他不想我们的孩子在成长的过程中没有父亲。”（大都会拘留中心，布鲁克林）(1/4) "I met Donald when I was twenty-six. He pursued me relentlessly. He’d call me every day. He’d invite me to come to the Bahamas with him. He’d buy me all kinds of things. He would even loan me his vintage corvette for the weekend. I was just starting out in life. I wasn’t used to all that attention. He had his own landscaping company—with his own building and everything. He wooed my whole family. Even my mother liked him, and she isn’t easily persuaded. So I fell for him. The abuse didn’t start until I was pregnant with our first child. We were lying in bed one night and he asked me to get him a glass of water. When I told him ‘no,’ he punched me in the face. He said: ‘When I ask you to do something, I expect you to do it.’ I tried to leave right away. I ran back to my family in New York. But he followed me and begged me to forgive him. He said he didn’t want our child to grow up without a father."(Metropolitan Detention Center, Brooklyn)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGl7FY9Tumblr: http://t.cn/RGl7FYKTwitter: http://t.cn/RGl7FYCInstagram: http://t.cn/RGl7FYN

>  2016 年 2 月 12 日“我已经六十二了，还有三年就出狱了。我贩卖的是海洛英，很多很多海洛英。我手下当时有四十个人。如果你在三十四年前问我坐牢是什么样子，我是根本无法想象的。这里的每天都是一模一样的。所有我关心的人都不在了。我母亲去世了，我父亲也去世了，还有我的哥哥和姐姐。如果让我回顾这一切，我会疯的。我只有让自己忙碌起来，一天一天地熬。我参与了监狱系统里所有的自助项目。我是‘具有影响力的男士’项目的主要推动者，我们传授行为技能、财务管理和企业家精神。在我负责的五年里，一共有 250 人成功毕业，而其中只有一人再次锒铛入狱。我会告诉他们说：‘别让我成为你们的未来。’而如果要我对所有这次采访的读者们说一句话，那我想为我自己造成的伤害而道歉。如果我能够回到当初改正自己的错误的话，我一定会的。这也是过去这 34 年里我一直在做的事。我是在巴尔的摩的廉租房里长大的，所有我认识的人都身无分文。当时的我只是利用自己仅有的资源试图改善自己的生活。但我选错了路。如果是我导致了自己之后的几代人误入歧途的话，我很抱歉。我不是故意想给整个社区带来痛楚的。我也真的认为自己出狱后，是能够给社会谋福祉的。”（坎伯兰联邦惩教所，马里兰州）“I’m sixty-two now. I have three more years. I sold heroin. A lot of it. I had forty people working for me. If you were to ask me thirty-four years ago what it was going to be like in prison, I couldn’t have imagined. It’s been the same thing every day. Everyone I care about is gone. My mother passed. My father passed. My brother and sister. If I look backwards, I’ll lose my mind. I just try to keep busy and take it one day at a time. I’ve done every self-help program in the system. I’m the lead facilitator for the Men of Influence program. We teach behavioral skills, financial management, and entrepreneurship. In the five years that I’ve been in charge, we’ve graduated 250 people, and only one has come back to prison. I tell them: ‘Don’t let me be your future.’ And if I could say one thing to everyone who reads this interview. I want to apologize for the harm that I caused. If I could go back in time and correct it, I would. But that’s what I’ve been trying to do for the past 34 years. I grew up in the Baltimore projects. Everyone that I knew had nothing. I was trying to improve my life with the information that I had at the time. I grabbed the wrong rope. I’m sorry if I caused generations behind me to go astray. It wasn’t my intention to bring pain to the community. And I really think that when I’m released, I can be an asset to society.”(Federal Correctional Institution: Cumberland, Maryland)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGWuXKbTumblr: http://t.cn/RGWuXKUTwitter: http://t.cn/RGWuXKyInstagram: http://t.cn/RGWuXK4

>  2016 年 2 月 11 日“我认识一个在保险公司工作的人。我会给她一些钱，然后她会把一切用来开通虚假信用额度所需要的信息给我。我会制作虚假驾照，然后进入商店开通信用额度。你一次性可以购买价值 1 万美元的东西，然后再以额度面值的 70% 转卖。我也会在他们的名下租用汽车，更换车架号后再以虚假的车主身份转卖。你可以把假的车主证打印在精美的羊皮纸上、加上水印，没有人会仔细看的。此后，即使我已经毁坏了他们的信誉，我仍然能够利用他们的信息。我能够打印出一些印有他们姓名的假支票，然后去银行提现。我的支票使用了磁性墨水和其他所有的东西。我全部都是在网上学的。我一直确保着自己的情感与其分离，从来没有过多地去了解这些人。对我来说，他们只是些名字罢了。不带任何私人的情感。再加上，他们全部都是公务员，所以我何必要有负罪感呢？难道政府对奴隶制度有过一点负罪感吗？”（坎伯兰联邦惩教所，马里兰州）“I knew a person who worked for an insurance company. I’d give her some money and then she’d give me all the information I needed to open fake credit lines. I’d create fake driver’s licenses and then go into stores and open up lines of credit. You can buy about $10,000 worth of stuff at a time, and then sell it for 70% of face value. I’d also rent cars under their name, change the VIN number, and then sell them with fake titles. You can print a fake title on nice parchment, add a watermark, and nobody looks too close. Then even after I destroyed their credit, I could still use their information. I could print up some fake checks with their name on it and cash them at banks. My checks had magnetic ink and everything. I learned it all on the Internet. I tried to stay emotionally detached. I never learned too much about the people. They were just names to me. Nothing personal. Plus, all of them were government employees. So why should I feel guilty? Does the government feel guilty about slavery?”(Federal Correctional Institution: Cumberland, Maryland)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGWRIRoTumblr: http://t.cn/RGWRIRCTwitter: http://t.cn/RGWRIR9Instagram: http://t.cn/RGWRIRS

>  2016 年 2 月 10 日“我是因为大量经销可卡因而被定罪的。警方提供了给我一个与他们合作六十个月的机会，但是我拒绝了。至今我的家人仍然对此耿耿于怀，他们说我把街上的兄弟们看得比他们还重要。但是我实在是不能再拖另一个人下水，所以他们判了我五个终身监禁。我已经在这儿待了二十年了，看到一些年轻人已经三番两次地回来过了。我试图教导过他们，但是根本没用。他们似乎只对如何才能用更高明的手段犯罪感兴趣。图书馆永远都是空荡荡的，没有一个年轻人好好地利用了这些项目。我鼓励他们利用自己在牢里的时间拿到普通教育发展证书，但他们却嘲笑我。他们连长者也不知道尊重。可卡因彻底改写了他们的人生。这些年轻人当中太多人眼睁睁地看着自己的父亲母亲在街上吸毒，太多人的父母也都坐了牢。这些孩子们都被迫着学会了自己照顾自己，所以旁人的话都不会去听。我对我的孩子们做了一模一样的事。我儿子被人杀害了，我女儿也不得不自己照顾自己，因为她母亲被判了十三年牢。但是她是少有的例外，她有充分的理由悲痛，但是她却提都不提。她现在在弗吉尼亚大学拿着 4.0 的绩点。”（艾伦伍德联邦惩教所，宾夕法尼亚州）“I was convicted of distributing a large amount of crack cocaine. I was offered sixty months to cooperate, but I turned it down. My family is still mad about that. They say I chose the streets over them. But I couldn’t bring someone else down with me, so they gave me five life sentences. I’ve been here twenty years. I’ve seen a lot of these younger kids come back two or three times already. I try to guide them but it’s no use. They only seem interested in finding a better way to do bad. The library is always empty. None of these young guys take advantage of the programs. I encourage them to get their GED’s while they’re here, but they laugh at me. They don't respect their elders. Crack changed everything. So many of these young men saw their mothers and fathers doing drugs in the street. So many of their parents went to prison. These kids were forced to raise themselves. So they aren’t about to listen to anyone. I did the same thing to my kids. My son got murdered. My daughter had to raise herself because her mom is doing thirteen life sentences. But she’s the exception. She's got every excuse to be bitter, but she doesn't even talk about it. She’s got a 4.0 at the University of Virginia right now.”(Federal Correctional Complex: Allenwood, Pennsylvania)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGOYPm9Tumblr: http://t.cn/RGOYPmoTwitter: http://t.cn/RGOYPmSInstagram: http://t.cn/RGOYPma

>  2016 年 2 月 10 日(2/2) “其实也不是什么黑社会。在波多黎各并没有像 Bloods 和 Crips 这样的黑帮，我们也就是在街区范围内的小组织。没有帮派、没有入会仪式，我们只是在一起长大的而已。我有两个表兄和两个姐夫也在组织里。我们有分工：望风的、贩毒的、跑腿的、领队的、动粗的，但是这些头衔并没有妨碍我们之间的关系。我们都在一起打篮球。我们会为整个街区举办派对。我们就像家人一般。我们的街区只有一个入口和一个出口，所有的房子都挨得挺近的，连草坪都没有。在一切都结束的那个夜晚，我能听到周围的门被撞坏的声音，直升机就在我们头顶。我不停地接到来电说：‘他们抓了这个人、他们抓了那个人、他们抓了你的表兄。’我就一个人坐在客厅中央，抽着烟。突然间，我听到了一阵脚步声从楼梯传来。我听到了电锯的声音，而火星从我的门上溅落。我上前去开门，但是却被闪光弹击中，而后八个人冲了进来。那晚他们抓了所有人。他们甚至都没把我们带去监狱。他们就把我们集中到了一个篮球体育馆。”（黑泽尔顿联邦惩教所，西弗吉尼亚州）(2/2) “It wasn’t really a gang. There aren’t Bloods or Crips in Puerto Rico. It was a neighborhood thing. There were no colors. There was no initiation. We just grew up together. I had two cousins and two brother-in-laws who were in the organization. There were ranks: watchers, dealers, runners, leaders, enforcers. But the ranks didn’t really get in the way of the relationships. We all played basketball together. We threw block parties for the whole neighborhood. It was like a family. There was only one entrance and one exit to our neighborhood. The houses were all close together. There were no lawns. On the night it ended, I could hear the doors breaking down all around me. Helicopters were overhead. I kept getting calls saying: ‘They got this person, they got that person, they got your cousin.’ I just sat in the middle of the living room, smoking a cigarette. Suddenly I heard a bunch of footsteps coming up the stairs. I heard the sound of a power saw and sparks started coming off my door. I went to open the door but I got hit with a flashbang, and eight guys rushed in. They got everyone that night. They didn’t even bring us to a jail. They brought us to a basketball stadium.”(Federal Correctional Complex: Hazelton, West Virginia)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGNjgDDTumblr: http://t.cn/RGNjgkvTwitter: http://t.cn/RGNjgDeInstagram: http://t.cn/RGNjgDF
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DjDf14DcL&u=005trlAajw1f1crrqo5xxj31kw11xn0b )

>  2016 年 2 月 10 日(1/2) “我开始贩毒的时候正在读大学。我当时一边去学校读书，一边在一家打印店工作。在我的公寓楼下有一个毒窝，而经营的人正是和我一起打篮球的那个人。他告诉我说：‘我有一晚有空缺。我想把它先留给你。’我轮到的是周五，晚上六点到清晨六点。我们卖了大麻、海洛因和可卡因。那第一晚我就赚到了 500 美元。那时我 19 岁，我的女朋友对此很迟疑，但是我用那笔钱给她买了几双高跟鞋，并和她保证说自己会继续在打印店工作的。几周之后，周六和周日也都有了空缺，然后周三也有了空缺。我开始每周 2000、然后 3000、然后 5000 这样地赚。我去给自己大学下一学期注册，却发现队伍实在是太长，所以我便再也没有回去过。我不再需要每天早晨 7 点起床。我可以想什么时候起，就什么时候起。我赚的钱让我感觉到自己的强大。当我开始说话的时候，别人会闭嘴。我能给一个老太太 100 美元来付电费。我能给小孩们 50 美元去看电影。那位最初提供给我这个差事的人拥有一幢房子，还有孩子、轿车和一辆摩托车。他干这行都二十年了也没出过问题，所以我想：‘为什么我不能和他一样呢？’”（黑泽尔顿联邦惩教所，西弗吉尼亚州）(1/2) “I was in college when I started. I was going to school and working at a print shop. There was a drug point outside of my apartment building. I played basketball with the guy who ran it. He told me: ‘I’ve got one night open, and I’m going to offer it to you first.’ My shift was on Friday, 6pm to 6am. We sold weed, heroin, and crack. I made $500 that first night. I was nineteen. My girlfriend wasn’t sure about it, but I bought her some high heels with the money, and I promised her I’d keep working at the print shop. After a few weeks, Saturday and Sunday opened up too. Then Wednesday. I started making 2k, then 3k, then 5k per week. I went to register for my next semester of college, but the line was too long, so I never went back. I didn’t have to wake up at 7 AM anymore. I could wake up whenever I wanted. The money made me feel powerful. People would stop talking when I began to talk. I could give an old lady $100 to pay her light bill. I could give kids $50 to go to the movies. The guy who first offered me the job had a house, and kids, and cars, and a motorcycle. He’d been working for twenty years with no problem. I thought: ‘Why can’t that be me?’”(Federal Correctional Complex: Hazelton, West Virginia)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGNci0ATumblr: http://t.cn/RGNci02Twitter: http://t.cn/RGNci0LInstagram: http://t.cn/RGNci0U
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DjAmar8Yj&u=005trlAajw1f1cf1bqnx5j31kw11xgoc )

>  2016 年 2 月 9 日“我在监狱里组织过很多的课程。有一个我创办的课程叫做‘创意教养’，是这里最热门的课，等候名单非常地长。我自己并没有孩子，但是我注意到大部分男人对待他们的孩子非常温柔，我因此想到了这个点子。大部分时候，我们就是做一点东西然后寄给孩子们。我们有涂色活动——父亲们会给图画的一半涂上颜色，而孩子们会涂另一半。我们会写睡前故事——大多数人写的都是和体育运动有关的，但是我们会确保每个故事都有一个道理。有的时候我们会拍一些好笑的照片然后把它们寄给孩子们——有一个男人的女儿特别喜爱‘小马宝莉’，他是个特别健壮的人，混过黑社会等等的，但是他把自己的头发梳成了羊角辫并扮成了一匹马。还有一节课，我们为患了癌症的孩子们制作了一些卡片。我让我的家人联系了一家医院办起来的。我们制作了大约 200 张卡片。医院让我们不要写‘希望你会好起来’这样的话，因为这会让那些孩子们想起他们正在经历的病痛。于是，我们便试着把焦点放在圣诞节上。我的单位里一共有 150 人，其中 60 人报名上了这个课程。因为课室太小，所以很多人都只能在门外面等着。”（黑泽尔顿联邦惩教所，西弗吉尼亚州）“I’ve organized a lot of programs in prison. One of the classes I started is called Creative Parenting. It’s the most popular class here. The waiting list is really long. I don’t have any kids myself, but I noticed that most guys are really soft for their kids. So that gave me an idea. Mainly we just make stuff and send it to the kids. We’ll do coloring projects where the father will color half the picture, and the kid will color the second half. We write bedtime stories. Most of the guys write about sports, but we make sure that every story has a moral. Sometimes we’ll take funny photos and send them to the kids. One guy’s daughter was really into My Little Pony. He was a tough guy. He was in a gang and everything, but he put his hair into pigtails and pretended to be a horse. We did another class where we made cards for kids with cancer. I had my family set it up with a hospital. We made about 200 cards. They didn’t want us to write ‘I hope you feel better,’ because that reminds the kids of what they’re going through. So we tried to keep it focused on Christmas. There were 150 guys in my unit, and 60 signed up for that program. A lot of the guys had to wait outside because the room was too small.”(Federal Correctional Complex: Hazelton, West Virginia)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGCSMjJTumblr: http://t.cn/RGCSMjxTwitter: http://t.cn/RGCSMjIInstagram: http://t.cn/RGCSMjM
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Djsvatl1h&u=005trlAajw1f1bgcvtkkgj31kw11x7a2 )

>  2016 年 2 月 9 日“我爸管不住我。我母亲是个酒鬼，所以是他独自把我们抚养长大的。四岁的时候我把我们家的房子烧成了灰。我不喜欢我哥哥的毛绒玩具，于是我就点火把它给烧了。之后一年，我在我爸的脸上揍了一拳。五年级的时候，我把一张桌子扔向了我的老师。十二岁的时候我就离家出走了。我爸把所有的办法都试过了。他带我去看了几位心理医生。他们诊断说我有间歇性暴躁症，所以就给我开了药，但是药物对我仍然没有什么帮助。没有人能够控制我，在我发怒的时候他们不得不把我缚住。我爸从来没能成功让我明白他讲的道理，因为只要他提高嗓门，我就会暴怒。他也试过奖励我，会说些类似于：‘只要你在学校里表现好，我就会带你去看球赛。’这样的话。他会开车跟着校巴以确保我不会逃课，但我还是会从后门口逃走。我的两个兄弟们从来都没有闯过祸。只有我，我受到过好多次袭击指控，我总是打架，从来没变过。我会觉得自己的头马上要爆炸了，我会眼冒金星，狂暴起来。我爸大约每个月来看我一次，而我们便会谈论这件事，就好像我们现在谈话这样。他总是问我同一个问题：‘还有其他什么我本来能做的事情吗？’我告诉他说：‘没有了。能做的一切你都做过了。’”（黑泽尔顿联邦惩教所，西弗吉尼亚州）“My dad couldn’t handle me. My mother was an alcoholic so he raised us on his own. I burned our house to the ground when I was four years old. I didn’t like my brother’s stuffed animal, so I set it on fire. The next year I punched my dad in the face. I threw a desk at my teacher in fifth grade. I ran away when I was twelve. My dad tried everything. He took me to psychologists. They diagnosed me with Intermittent Explosive Disorder, so they put me on medication. But it didn’t help much. Nobody could control me. They’d actually have to hold me down when I went into a rage. Dad could never get a point across because if he raised his voice, I’d explode. He’d try to give me incentives. He’d say things like: ‘If you do good in school, I’ll bring you to a ball game.’ He’d follow the school bus to make sure I didn’t skip, but then I’d just run out the back exit. Neither of my brothers ever got in trouble. It was just me. I’ve gotten multiple assault charges. I fight. That’s what I do. I feel like my head is going to burst and I see stars and I snap. My dad comes to visit about once a month, and we talk things over, just like we’re doing now. And he asks me all the time, ‘What else could I have done?’ I tell him: ‘Nothing. You did everything you could.’”(Federal Correctional Complex: Hazelton, West Virginia)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGCMXZHTumblr: http://t.cn/RGCMXZ8Twitter: http://t.cn/RGCMXZQInstagram: http://t.cn/RGCMXZT
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DjrF0l9tO&u=005trlAajw1f1bcn99sx0j31kw11xdj1 )

>  2016 年 2 月 8 日“我以前是个好学生。参与过橄榄球、空手道、篮球等各种各样的活动。我从来都不翘课。我第一次卖毒品是在自己十二三岁的时候。我也不是专职干这个，只是在自己需要钱用的时候。我妈妈在一个只有一间卧室的公寓里抚养着我们四个孩子，所以我们没有买衣服的钱。我只需要足以不让人们针对着我的钱、足以让我走路时不被停下来的钱。但是随着我渐渐长大，我为了合群而花的钱也越来越多。女孩子们进入了我的生活，我想要给她们留下深刻的印象。于是我开始交易更多的毒品，而其他的活动则渐渐淡出了我的生活。高中毕业后，我开始试着学习护理学。我用贩毒赚来的钱交了学费。但是两年之后我分了心，开始重新贩毒。我以为自己能够一心二用，但这根本不可能，你不可能同时去做一件好事和一件坏事，坏事总会占据上风的。世上根本没有罗宾汉。没有人想听你说自己贩毒是因为要养活家里人。检控方不想听这个。社会也不想听这个。政府体制更不想听这个。《以西结书》里有这样一段话，我不记得是哪里了，但是说的就是这个道理。原文好像是这样说的：‘如果你做的都是好事，只有一件是坏事，那么好事是不会被提及的。’”（坎伯兰联邦惩教所，马里兰州）“I was a good student. I did football, karate, basketball, all sorts of activities. I never skipped school. I first sold drugs when I was twelve or thirteen. It wasn’t a full time thing. Just whenever I needed money. My mom was raising four of us in a one-bedroom apartment, so we didn’t have money for clothes. I just needed enough to keep people from focusing on me. Just enough to keep moving. But as I got older, it cost more and more to stay up. Girls came into the picture. I wanted to impress them. I started dealing more and more, and all the other activities faded out of my life. I tried to study nursing after high school. I paid my tuition with drug money. But I lost focus after two years and fell back on drug dealing. I thought I could be double-minded. But it’s not possible. You can’t do good and bad at the same time. The bad always wins. There’s no such thing as Robin Hood. Nobody wants to hear that you’re dealing drugs to feed your family. Prosecutor doesn’t want to hear that. Society doesn’t want to hear that. The system doesn’t want to hear that. There’s a verse in the Book of Ezekiel, I forget which one, but it talks about this. It says something like: ‘If you do all good, and one bad, the good will not be mentioned.’”(Federal Correctional Institution: Cumberland, Maryland)Facebook: http://t.cn/RG9oVefTumblr: http://t.cn/RG9oVe9Twitter: http://t.cn/RG9oVeVInstagram: http://t.cn/RG9oVec
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DjjCN6mWb&u=005trlAajw1f1ad6460vnj31e00xcacm )

>  2016 年 2 月 8 日“我牵扯进了一点小事，还有二十天就出狱了。没有人知道我在这儿。我叫了人帮我更新我的 Facebook 页面了。我所有的朋友都以为我现在在夏威夷呢。”（大都会惩教中心，纽约）“I got caught up in a little something. I’ve got twenty days left. Nobody knows I’m here. I’ve got somebody updating my Facebook page for me. All my friends think I’m in Hawaii right now.”(Metropolitan Correctional Center, New York)Facebook: http://t.cn/RG96zfcTumblr: http://t.cn/RG96zfVTwitter: http://t.cn/RG96zftInstagram: http://t.cn/RG96zfI
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Djj6htJ48&u=005trlAajw1f1aaupvsudj31kw11xtc5 )

>  2016 年 2 月 8 日“我是一个人带着四个孩子，我的母亲也病着。我之前在哈林区的一家饭店工作，每周只赚 500 美元。然后这个哥伦比亚女子告诉我说她能帮助我。她说：‘我们需要像你这样的老实人。’我实在是太需要那笔钱了。他们给了我一个运输员的工作，让我开车把可卡因从曼哈顿运到马萨诸塞州。他们还额外给了我一些让我在饭店做交易。我只有过几个顾客。我做了两年，自己从来没有吸过毒。然后，在警方的一次卧底行动中，我中了这个让我开始贩毒的哥伦比亚女子的圈套。我知道我做错了，但是在此之前我从来没惹过事。我以为我坐牢的时间不会太久。警探们告诉我说：‘你就是头目。你做了这个，你做了那个。’律师则告知我要签下这些文件。我完全不懂应该做些什么。他们告诉我说，上了庭审我什么机会都不会有。他们和我说他们是在帮我。于是我被判了 25 年。”（大都会拘留中心，布鲁克林）“I was alone with four kids. My mother was sick. I was making $500 a week working at a restaurant in Harlem. This Colombian woman told me she could help. She said, ‘We need honest people like you.’ I really needed the money. They gave me a job as a transporter. I drove cocaine from Manhattan to Massachusetts. They gave me some extra to sell at the restaurant. I only had a few clients. I did it for two years. I never did any drugs myself. Then I was set up in a sting by the same woman who got me started. I knew I’d done wrong but I’d never been in trouble before. I thought I would do a little time in jail. The detectives told me: ‘You’re a leader. You’re this. You’re that.’ The lawyer told me to sign these papers. I didn’t understand what to do. They told me I didn’t have a chance at trial. They told me they were helping me. I was given 25 years.”(Metropolitan Detention Center, Brooklyn)Facebook: http://t.cn/RG9I1wfTumblr: http://t.cn/RG9I1wITwitter: http://t.cn/RG9I1wMInstagram: http://t.cn/RG9I1wx
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DjizJ0zgq&u=005trlAajw1f1a8jbb5hij31kw11xju9 )

>  2016 年 2 月 7 日“一开始我还以为是炸弹爆炸。整栋楼都被推动了，所以我撞到了墙上。没有人惊声尖叫，除了电话铃响之外只有沉默。也没有人作宣布或者什么的，所有人都开始朝出口走去。我记得楼梯是湿的，燃料全通过电梯井倾泻了下来，所以闻着就像一股非常强烈的清洁剂的味道。如今我做梦的时候依然能闻得到。楼梯间里每个人都很从容和安静。很多人都很胖，所以我们移动得很缓慢，间或又要腾出位置让消防员们跑过。直到我们到达底楼，人们才开始恐慌，因为碎玻璃到处都是，而地上都是尸体。那时我们才开始飞奔起来。警察其实还试图让我们停留在大堂内部，因为外面不断地有尸体在掉下来，但是我们还是推开他们挤了过去。我记得自己被所有人站在那儿朝天看的场景给震惊了。我根本不明白为什么会有人这么做。我走过了三十条街，叫车去了中城。我试着走进地铁站，看看列车运不运行，一位工作人员正坐在柜台里看着电视，她说：‘全都没了。’而那时我才终于开始感到害怕。在此之前，我是只顾着逃命。”（大都会惩教中心，纽约）“I thought it was a bomb at first. It pushed the building, so I was thrown against the wall. Nobody screamed. It was silent except for the sound of ringing phones. There was no announcement or anything, everyone just started walking toward the exits. I remember the stairs were wet. Fuel had poured down through the elevator shafts so it smelled like a really strong cleaning product. I still smell it when I’m dreaming. Everyone was calm and quiet in the stairwell. A lot of people were out of shape, so we were moving slowly. Occasionally we’d move out of the way to let a fireman run past. People didn’t begin to panic until we reached the ground floor because there was broken glass everywhere and bodies on the ground. That’s the first time we started running. The police actually tried to keep us inside the lobby because bodies were falling outside, but we pushed past them. I remember being shocked by all the people who were standing around, looking up. I couldn’t understand why a person would do that. I walked thirty blocks, then I caught a ride to midtown. I tried walking down into a subway station to see if the trains were running. An attendant was sitting in the booth, watching the television, and she said: ‘They’re gone.’ And that was when I finally felt fear. Until then, it had only been survival.”(Metropolitan Correctional Center, New York)Facebook: http://t.cn/RG9cG67Tumblr: http://t.cn/RG9cG6hTwitter: http://t.cn/RG9cG6zInstagram: http://t.cn/RG9cG6A
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Djia219tq&u=005trlAajw1f1a6hpl0mdj31kw11x76t )

-----------------------

>  2016 年 2 月 7 日(2/2) “我小时候试过走正途来赚钱。我试过铲雪。我试过送报。送报我坚持了好一会儿，但是有一天我在送报途中收钱的时候，一群比我大的孩子们抢劫了我。他们一共三个人，十六七岁的样子。我和他们打得很凶。我告诉他们说：‘这个钱是我辛苦赚来的。’但是他们还是把我压在了地上，拿走了我的钱。那是 27 美元，而我当时为此感到非常地无能为力。我记得自己知道有个人带着一把刀，所以就想：‘我要偷偷地拿到那把刀，然后一口气解决这件事。’我在一家游戏厅找到了那群男孩子。没有人被杀死，但是我弄伤了他们。捅伤他们之后我并没有觉得很自豪，但是我觉得他们活该，我觉得自己是无辜的。即使到了今日，我仍然无法同情他们。说来也奇怪，当别人委屈了我们时，我们想要他们接受最大程度的惩罚；但是当我们做错了事情的时候，我们想要的是别人最大程度的理解和原谅。”（大都会惩教中心，纽约）(2/2) “I tried to make some money the honest way as a kid. I tried shoveling snow. I tried a newspaper route. I stuck with it for awhile, but one day I was collecting money on my route and these older kids robbed me. There were three of them. They were 16 or 17. I fought hard. I told them: ‘I worked hard for this money.’ But they held me down and took it anyway. It was $27. And that made me feel so powerless. And I remembered that I knew someone with a knife. And I thought: ‘I’m going to steal that knife and deal with this firmly.’ I found those boys at an arcade. Nobody got killed. But I hurt them. I wouldn’t say that I felt proud after stabbing them, but I felt like they got what they deserved. I felt vindicated. Even today, I have trouble sympathizing with them. It’s funny how that works. When someone wrongs us, we want the maximum amount of punishment. But when we do wrong, we want the maximum amount of understanding and forgiveness.”(Metropolitan Correctional Center, New York)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGKKsaETumblr: http://t.cn/RGKKsaRTwitter: http://t.cn/RGKKsaDInstagram: http://t.cn/RGKKsa8
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DjbsHC4iQ&u=005trlAajw1f19d4sumbwj31kw11xjui )

>  2016 年 2 月 7 日(1/2) “我父亲死去的时候我才六岁。他是在一次钓鱼之旅中溺亡的。我母亲不得不在北费城独自抚养我们五个。我记得自己十二岁的时候去街角的集市，我母亲派我拿着一张纸条去请求店家让我们赊账买些食物。店主就让我等在一旁，因为店里有其他人在付钱，所以这个家伙就不断地跳过我。他是逼我要在所有人面前乞求他。他说着类似于：‘你妈妈还欠我钱呢。她从来都不付钱。’这样的话。我妈妈是我的女王，而他却在所有人的面前贬低她。那实在是太丢脸了。我很厌恶他可以这样把我踩在脚底，就好像他有水，而我很渴。于是我对他大叫了几句，然后气冲冲地走了。我不住地想：‘迟早有一天我会买下这家商店的。’但是之后我冷静了下来，意识到自己对着唯一一个能帮助我们的人发泄了一通。因此，我只有向街角那些贩毒的家伙们说我希望他们能让我赚点钱。他们认为我那个时候还太年轻，想保护我，所以就直接把钱给了我。”（大都会惩教中心，纽约）(1/2) “My father died when I was six. He drowned on a fishing trip. My mother had to raise five of us in North Philadelphia. I remember being twelve years old and going to a market on the corner. My mother had sent me with a note, asking for some credit so we could buy some food. The owner made me wait. There were other people in the store, and they were paying, so this guy is just skipping all over me. He’s making me beg in front of everyone. He’s saying things like: ‘Your mom still owes me. She never pays.’ My mom was my queen, and he’s running her down in front of all these people. It was degrading. I hated that he had that power over me. Like he had water, and I was thirsty. So I screamed at him and stormed out. I kept thinking: ‘One day I’m going to buy that store.’ But then I calmed down, and I realized that I just spazzed on the one guy who could help us. So I walked up to some of the dope boys on the corner, and asked them to let me earn. They thought I was too young at the time. They wanted to protect me. So they just gave me the money.”(Metropolitan Correctional Center, New York)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGKaOXjTumblr: http://t.cn/RGKaOXlTwitter: http://t.cn/RGKaOXTInstagram: http://t.cn/RGKaOXW
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Djb8bzRGi&u=005trlAajw1f19bo7uepcj31kw11xjuc )

>  2016 年 2 月 6 日“我当时在洪都拉斯的一个夜店上班，每晚赚 4 美元，而一个人告诉我说只要我到一艘船上工作，我就能在十二天里赚 6000 美元。那时候洪都拉斯没什么就职机会。我们也不像你们这边有政府福利。在没有任何其他赚钱的途径下，要说‘不’实在是太难了。所以我就同意了。他们把我放上了一艘小渔船，接着我们便把可卡因从哥伦比亚运送到了洪都拉斯。我的工作就是维护好容器并帮忙装载。我这辈子从来没有接触过毒品。在第四趟运送途中，我们在国际水域被美国海岸警卫队停了下来。我们有 986 公斤可卡因。这已经是十年前的事了。”（艾伦伍德联邦惩教所，宾夕法尼亚州）“I was working at a nightclub in Honduras, making $4 a night, and some guy tells me that I can make $6,000 in twelve days just by working on a boat. There weren’t any jobs in Honduras. We didn’t have government benefits like you have here. It’s really tough to say ‘no’ when there are no other options for money. So I agreed. They put me on a small fishing boat. We transported cocaine from Colombia to Honduras. My job was to maintain the vessel and help load the cargo. I’ve never done drugs in my life. On our fourth trip, we were stopped in international waters by the US coastguard. We had 986 kilograms of cocaine. That was ten years ago.”(Federal Correctional Complex: Allenwood, Pennsylvania)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGK7BxITumblr: http://t.cn/RGK7BxxTwitter: http://t.cn/RGK7BxSInstagram: http://t.cn/RGK7BxM
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Dj8qp5EAL&u=005trlAajw1f18zq3wanyj31kw11xjv4 )

>  2016 年 2 月 6 日(2/2) “有一天，我从我邻居家的信箱里偷走了她们的福利支票，而她在找支票的过程中找上了门。那时我已经二十多岁，而我的幻听也非常强烈了。它们尖叫着要我去做坏事。它们告诉我说要保护自己，说我正在危险之中。于是我上楼到了那个女人和她十岁的女儿一起住的公寓。不，我不能回想起这一切，不然我今晚会睡不着觉的。事情发生的时候我不停地在呕吐。我整整两周都没能睡觉。那个女人和她的女儿会不停地复活，我到哪儿都能看见她们。有一次我打开浴帘，而那个女人就站在那儿，我便尖叫了起来。警探们询问了我，但还是放我走了。他们没有怀疑我。之后我去了牙买加住了两年，也没有任何人来找过我。但是那些影像总是会出现在我的脑海里。我实在是再也承受不了了。于是我去了美国大使馆，告诉了他们说：‘我杀了人。’”（大都会拘留中心，布鲁克林）(2/2) “One day I stole my neighbor’s benefit check out of the mailbox, and she came looking for it. I was in my mid-twenties, and by that time the voices were very strong. They were screaming at me to do bad things. They were telling me to protect myself. That I was in danger. So I went downstairs to the woman’s apartment where she lived with her ten-year-old daughter. I can’t remember this or I won’t sleep tonight. I kept vomiting while it happened. I didn’t sleep for two weeks. The woman and her daughter kept coming back to life and I would see them everywhere. One time I opened the shower curtain and the woman was standing there and I screamed. The detectives questioned me but they let me go. They didn’t suspect me. I went to Jamaica and lived for two years and nobody looked for me. But the images were always in my head. I couldn’t take it anymore. I went to the American embassy, and I told them: ‘I’ve committed a murder.’”(Metropolitan Detention Center, Brooklyn)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGocjrUTumblr: http://t.cn/RGocjr4Twitter: http://t.cn/RGocjryInstagram: http://t.cn/RGocjrL
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Dj1QdBbF1&u=005trlAajw1f186now96kj31kw11yaci )

-----------------------

>  2016 年 2 月 6 日(1/2) “我的童年在很早的时候就结束了。一直到十一岁我都受着两个家庭成员的性虐待，每次我住在我祖母家的时候就会发生。我也不敢告诉我的母亲或父亲。西印第安文化是有些不同的，我们不会做过多的交流。人们会纳闷我为什么表现得不像一个孩子。他们总是会问我为什么不笑。我每时每刻都很恼怒。九年级的时候我由于打架而被停学，原因是有人在楼梯间里摸了我的胸。我的幻听是之后才开始的——在我父亲被谋杀之后的那个圣诞。如今我因为这个要打针，但是那个时候我并不知道那是幻听。我以前将它们称之为我的朋友。我以为是真的有人在和我说话。它们有着不同的人格。它们总是说一些不好的东西，比如：‘活下去是不值得的。’或者‘快动手杀了你自己吧。’”（大都会拘留中心，布鲁克林）(1/2) “My childhood ended early. I was sexually abused by two family members until the age of eleven. It happened every time I went to stay at my grandmother’s house. I didn’t feel like I could tell my mother or father. West Indian culture is a little different. We didn’t really talk like that. People wondered why I didn't act like a kid. They were always asking why I never smiled. I was angry all the time. I got suspended from school in 9th grade for fighting, because somebody touched my breast in the stairwell. The voices started later—the Christmas after my father was murdered. I take injections for them today. But back then I didn’t see them as voices. I used to call them my friends. I really thought people were talking to me. They had different personalities. They always said bad things, like: ‘It’s not worth being alive.’ Or ‘Go ahead and kill yourself.’”(Metropolitan Detention Center, Brooklyn)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGoGcvLTumblr: http://t.cn/RGoGcvqTwitter: http://t.cn/RGoGcvyInstagram: http://t.cn/RGoGcvU
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Dj1De8yzd&u=005trlAajw1f185q9kvn7j31kw11xmzr )

>  2016 年 2 月 5 日“他是个不同流俗的人。他总是告诉我说：‘我们必须在失败中找到成功的路。’在社会的眼中，我们已经失败了，每个牢里的人都是废物。我们可以对此感到愤怒，我们也可以继续努力成长。他总是纠正我的西班牙语，并会给我出些测验题。他曾经是个工程师，所以他也在教我三角学。他于我来说就是恩赐。他让我不再如此愤怒。他总是如此豁达和乐观。而我实在不明白他是如何保持这样乐观的态度的，因为我还有 40 个月就出狱了，他被判的是终身监禁。”（艾伦伍德联邦惩教所，宾夕法尼亚州）“He’s a beautiful person. He always tells me: ‘We’ve got to find a way to win by losing.’ In the eyes of society, we’ve lost already. Everyone in here is a loser. We can either be angry about it, or we can keep trying to grow. He’s always correcting my Spanish and giving me quizzes. He used to be an engineer, so he’s been tutoring me in trigonometry. He’s been a blessing to me. He’s helped me to not be so angry. He’s always so happy and optimistic. And I don’t know how he stays so positive. Because I’m getting out of here in 40 months. He’s doing life.”(Federal Correctional Complex: Allenwood, Pennsylvania)Facebook: http://t.cn/RGSmtwcTumblr: http://t.cn/RGSmtwVTwitter: http://t.cn/RGSmtw5Instagram: http://t.cn/RGSmtwt
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Dj0akvoHG&u=005trlAajw1f17z9c2kv9j31kw11xjuw )

>  2016 年 2 月 4 日“我妈妈是个单亲妈妈，养育了我们一共九个孩子。所有的孩子们都在田里干过活。我是从十二岁开始的。我们摘过黄瓜、苹果、玉米、草莓等等所有的作物。我们中没有一个人去学校读过书，也没人在意——如果你经常搬来搬去，政府的系统也找不到你。每当收成结束后，我们就会去另外的地方。我们总是签好一个合同。农民们会给我们安排住处并给我们一点钱，而我们则在他们的田里干活。但是每次我们干完活后，钱也不剩了。我十八岁时候的一天，一个朋友让我在我们的拖车里藏一些大麻。为此他给了我一点钱。我把钱给了我妈妈。事情就是这样开始的。” （黑泽尔顿联邦惩教所，西弗吉尼亚州）“My mom was a single mom and there were nine of us. All of the kids worked in the fields. I started when I was twelve. We picked cucumbers, apples, corn, strawberries, all of it. None of us went to school. Nobody cared-- if you move around a lot, the system loses track of you. Whenever the harvest was done, we’d go somewhere else. We always signed a contract. The farmers would give us a place to live and a little bit of money, and we worked in their fields. But there was never any money left when we finished. One day when I was eighteen, a friend of mine asked me to hide some marijuana in our trailer. He gave me a little money. I gave it to my mom. And that’s how it all began.” (Federal Correctional Complex: Hazelton, West Virginia)Tumblr: http://t.cn/RGS8bqMFacebook: http://t.cn/RGS8bqJ
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DiZGC7WQT&u=005trlAajw1f17x59za8lj31kw11xdio )

-----------------------

>  2016 年 2 月 4 日“这是我第五次坐牢了。我每次犯的罪都是源于我的毒瘾。最好的情况是我这次出狱之后会重新做人，成为那百分之一成功战胜了冰毒毒瘾的人。最坏的情况就是我还是现在这个老样子。实话说，如果我再复吸的话，我希望自己能就此一死了之，因为我不想再继续伤害别人了。我剥夺了我孩子们正常的生活。我十七岁的女儿正住在未成年妈妈之家。我二十一岁的儿子也在坐牢。我十八岁的女儿过得还不错，她一边在联邦快递工作，一边在读大学。她憎恨毒品，以为这世界很美好、外面没人会伤害她。她想要帮助我。她想让我出狱后陪她一起住，但我觉得这不是个好主意。”（黑泽尔顿联邦惩教所，西弗吉尼亚州）“This is my fifth time in prison. Every crime I’ve committed has come from my addiction. Best case scenario is I get out of here, rebuild my life, and join the one percent of people who have beaten a meth addiction. Worst case scenario is I become no more than what I am today. And honestly, if I mess up again, I hope it kills me. Because I don’t want to keep hurting people. I’ve cheated my kids out of normal lives. My seventeen-year-old daughter is in a home for teen moms. My twenty-one-year-old son is in jail. My eighteen-year-old daughter is doing OK. She’s got a job at FedEx and goes to college. She hates drugs and thinks the world is a good place and that nobody is out to hurt her. She wants to help me. She wants me to come live with her when I get out. I don’t think that’s a good idea.”(Federal Correctional Complex: Hazelton, West Virginia)http://t.cn/RGSjhNkhttp://t.cn/RGSjhNF
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DiZ5a9LE2&u=005trlAajw1f17uhabaakj31kw11x427 )

-----------------------

>  2016 年 2 月 4 日(2/2) “我其实越狱过一次。我当时因为持有海洛因而被逮捕，接着被带去了警察局。他们铐上了我的双手和双脚，再用墙上的卸扣把我锁住，然后把我一个人留在了审讯室，却留一下了一罐汽水。我把易拉罐撕烂，直到自己得到一条很窄的铝片，然后把它塞进了手铐的齿条，把锁反转，并打开了手铐。然后我拖着卸扣走了两英里到了一位朋友的家，借了一个发卡打开了我双手和双脚上的锁。我真的没想到警察会那么在意这件事——只不过是一包海洛因而已。我以为他们会在搜查完我妈的房子之后就放弃的，但是结果他们出动了警犬和直升机。新闻里面放的也全是我的照片。几个小时后他们就抓获了我。他们对此不是特别开心，因为要抓我可不是件简单的事。其实这事很愚蠢，我知道的。但是抓我真的不简单。” （艾伦伍德联邦惩教所，宾夕法尼亚州）(2/2) “I actually escaped once. I was picked up for possession of heroin and taken to the police station. They handcuffed my hands and feet, shackled me to the wall, and left me in the interrogation room with a can of soda. I ripped up the soda can until I had a thin strip of aluminum, and I wedged it into the teeth of the handcuffs so I could override the locking mechanism and pull them apart. Then I dragged the shackles for two miles to a friend’s house and borrowed a bobby pin to pick the locks on my hands and feet. I honestly didn’t think the police would care that much. It was just a bag of heroin. I thought they’d check my mom’s house and give up. Instead they sent out dogs and helicopters. My picture was all over the news. They caught me after a few hours. They weren’t very happy. It wasn’t an easy thing to do. Extremely stupid, I know. But not easy.” (Federal Correctional Complex: Allenwood, Pennsylvania)http://t.cn/RG62UeF
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DiqPADi5p&u=005trlAajw1f13n9omwjjj31kw11xdj6 )

-----------------------

>  2016 年 2 月 4 日(1/2) “我当时在宾夕法尼亚州立大学读景观设计，同时也一边在做毒品交易。二十岁的时候，我因持有四分之一磅迷幻蘑菇和一磅大麻而被捕。从那时起，我便默认自己的人生完蛋了。我没觉得自己能够从一项重罪指控中重新振作起来，所以我几乎把一切都放弃了。在等待判刑的那段时间里，我开始吸食可卡因和海洛因，我也从那时候起成了一个不折不扣的瘾君子。我因为各种不同的毒品指控已经先后坐了十五年牢。我最近一次被捕是因为生产芬太奴。这是种异常难制的毒品——它的药性比海洛因还要强，分子结构比冰毒还要复杂。在东海岸，我只知道一个人找到了生产芬太奴的方法。用来防止人们接触其原料的法律条文实在太多了。我没有资源也没有人脉，所以就自学了有机化学并找到了一个方法。当我最后被抓的时候，他们都只想知道我究竟是怎么做到的。这也就是我毒瘾的症结所在，我聪明到能解决各种阻力，所以从来都没有任何其他的东西能够阻挡我，除了我自己。”（艾伦伍德联邦惩教所，宾夕法尼亚州）(1/2) “I was studying landscape architecture at Penn State and dealing drugs on the side. At the age of twenty, I got arrested with a quarter pound of mushrooms and a pound of marijuana. I assumed my life was over at that point. I didn’t think I could bounce back from a felony charge so I pretty much gave up on everything. I started doing cocaine and heroin while I waited on my sentencing, and I’ve been an addict ever since. I’ve spent a total of fifteen years in prison for various drug charges. My last arrest was for producing Fentanyl. It’s extremely difficult to make—it’s stronger than heroin and a much more complicated molecule than meth. I only know of one other person on the east coast who figured out how to make it. There were so many laws in place to keep people from getting the materials. I had no resources and no connections but I studied organic chemistry and found a way. When I finally got caught, all they wanted to know was how I did it. That’s the problem with my addiction. I’m smart enough to get around anything. So there’s never been anything to stop me but myself.”(Federal Correctional Complex: Allenwood, Pennsylvania)http://t.cn/RGifOyo
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DijfuuTdS&u=005trlAajw1f12pskfu2uj31kw11x43i )

-----------------------

>  2016 年 2 月 3 日“我在外头有个女儿。我已经离开她 23 年了。这深深地伤害到了她。我姐姐告诉我说毕业典礼之后，当其他人都在和家人合影的时候，我女儿整个人崩溃并哭了起来。每次她来看我的时候都会和我说：如果她现在成家的话，我就看不到她的家庭了，这样她会很内疚。但是尽管有我这样的母亲，她还是非常成功的。她是个设计师，事业风生水起。我人在牢里做不了多少能支持她的事情，但是我尽力而为。我订阅了所有的时尚杂志：@Vogue服饰与美容、@嘉人美妆官方微博、@ELLE、@时尚芭莎。她太忙了，没时间全部都看一遍，所以我来帮她看，并试着去找一些能帮到她的内容。我会把任何能辅助她发布 Instagram 的内容给挑出来。她也会在那上面发布我的照片，但仅限于#怀旧星期四#。她并不以我为耻，她只是不想别人看见我这套土黄色的监狱服。她很讨厌这套监狱服。”（大都会拘留中心，布鲁克林）“I’ve got a daughter out there. I’ve been gone for 23 years now. It’s really hurt her. My sister told me that after graduation, when everyone else was taking photos with their family, my daughter just broke down and cried. When she visits, she tells me that she feels too guilty to start a family because I won’t be there to see it. But she’s been very successful despite me. She’s a stylist. She’s doing so well. I can’t do much in here to support her, but I try my best. I’ve ordered all the fashion magazines: Vogue, Marie Claire, Elle, Bazaar. She’s too busy to read them all, so I look through them and try to find something that might help her. I set aside anything that she might be able to use for an Instagram post. She posts pictures of me on there, but only on ‘Throwback Thursday.’ She’s not ashamed of me, but she just doesn’t want anyone to see this khaki uniform. She hates it.”(Metropolitan Detention Center, Brooklyn)http://t.cn/RGxVGd8
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Di4MVntjh&u=005trlAajw1f10xy11yt1j30u00jzjsk )

>  2016 年 2 月 1 日“我妻子在去年一月去世了。我们的婚姻长达 62 年。因为我最近正在阅读莎士比亚的十四行诗集，所以对于爱情自己也思考了很多，而你也正好在这个时候找到了我。爱情的定义难以捉摸，也正是因为如此，我们才永不停歇地歌颂着它。即使是莎士比亚自己也摸不透爱情，所有他的那些伟大的爱情故事，似乎都是关于外在的吸引。罗密欧与朱丽叶连他们自己是否喜欢同一本书或者同一部电影都不清楚，全凭外在的吸引。过了 62 年，我与妻子的爱情历久弥新。我妻子过去常说：‘我们亲密如一。’相信我，她不是那种说话会夸大其辞的人。现在她不在我身边了，我才意识到她是如此地正确。我们生活中大部分的事都紧密联系在一起。我们不仅在身体上两情相悦，在生活中亦有数不清的相同的癖好。每当我离开电影院却询问不了她的看法之时，我就会想念她，又或者当我在饭店吃饭的时候，却不能让她尝一尝我点的鸡肉的味道。而我最想念她是在深夜。过去的每个夜晚，我们都是在同一时间上床入睡的。”“My wife passed away last January. We’d been married for 62 years. You caught me at a time when I’ve been thinking a lot about love because I’m reading Shakespeare’s sonnets. The definition of love is elusive, which is why we write about it endlessly. Even Shakespeare couldn’t touch it. All the greatest love stories just seem to be about physical attraction. Romeo and Juliet didn’t know if they liked the same books or movies. It was just physical. After 62 years, it becomes something different entirely. My wife used to say: ‘We are one.’ And believe me, she was not the type of person to overstate something. Now that she’s gone, I realize how right she was. So much of our lives were linked. We were very physical and affectionate. But we also shared every ritual of our life. I miss her every time I leave a movie and can’t ask for her opinion. Or every time I go to a restaurant and can’t give her a taste of my chicken. I miss her most at night. We got in bed together at the same time every night.”http://t.cn/RbD9O09
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DhUvDmRrJ&u=005trlAajw1f0zma5d1jtj31kw11x7a2 )

>  2016 年 2 月 1 日“在我成长的过程中，我父母都在监狱里服刑。我自己 90% 的人生也是在监狱里度过的，大都是由于毒品。2014 年我出狱的时候，布朗克斯区有这样一位年迈的律师对我很感兴趣，他的名字叫 Ramon Jimenez。他可以说是一位社区活跃人士。我不知道他为什么如此关心我，他和我一起坐下并尝试给我的未来做了规划。当我又试图重回贩毒的老路的时候，Ramon 出门和我一起在街角站了整整三天。这是那位 72 岁的家伙的照片，不论我去哪里他都会盯着我、会对着所有走上前来和我说话的人大叫：‘我要打电话给警察了！’当时我气疯了，但是三天后我便放弃了。”“Both my parents were in prison while I was growing up. I’ve been in prison for 90% of my life, mainly for drugs. When I got out in 2014, there was this old lawyer in the Bronx who took an interest in me. His name was Ramon Jimenez. He’s kind of like a community activist. I don’t know why he cared so much, but he sat down with me and tried to map out my life. When I tried to start selling drugs again, Ramon came out and stood on the corner with me for three days straight. Here’s this 72 year old dude, shadowing me wherever I go, screaming at anyone who tried to walk up to me: 'I'm calling the cops!' I was so mad. But after three days I gave it up.”http://t.cn/RGI5a82第二张是来自 Ramon 的网站上的他的照片

>  2016 年 1 月 31 日“她是全家人的粘合剂。所有的事情都是由她来计划，而所有的事情都是为了要团结起我们家。我们刚刚和儿子吃完由她安排好的晚餐。放假的时候，她会组织各种各样的游戏和寻宝活动。她甚至会为每个人都买一套一模一样的睡衣来庆祝圣诞早晨。有一年我们的结婚纪念日，她把我们的客厅变成了一家叫‘爱之家’的法式餐厅，全都是因为当时我们八岁的女儿正在学校里学习法语。”“She’s the glue for the entire family. She plans everything, and everything centers around bringing us together. We’re just leaving a dinner with our son that she arranged. During the holidays, she organizes all sorts of games and scavenger hunts. She even buys everyone the same pair of pajamas for Christmas morning. On one of our anniversaries, she turned our living room into a French restaurant called ‘The House of Love.’ All because our eight-year-old daughter was studying French in school.”http://t.cn/RGVavgU

>  2016 年 1 月 30 日“我能持续节食两到三天，吃一点沙拉然后装出自己很享受的样子，但是过后我总会老毛病再犯。我刚刚离开 Checkers——有个人在街上递给了我一张优惠券，我没能禁得起诱惑，下一秒就已经在吃两个汉堡加薯条了。太失败了简直。不过只花了我 4 美元。明天晚餐我会吃沙拉的。”“I can diet for two or three days. I can eat a few salads and pretend like I enjoy them. But then I always have a massive relapse. I just left Checkers. Some guy handed me a coupon on the street and that was all it took. Next thing you know I’m eating two burgers and a fry. Total disaster. Only $4 though. I’ll have a salad for dinner tomorrow.”http://t.cn/RGcXx3i

>  2016 年 1 月 30 日“我好像永远都是小心翼翼的。全是压力啊。我每个月社保能领到 696 美元。如果我像我认识的一些人那样装成有躁郁症，那么我还能拿到更多，但是想要拿到身心障碍者福利的话，他们会逼着你吃药。我是不会为了多拿钱而像僵尸一样坐在那儿的。付完账单后，我就只剩下 30 美元了。我能用 59 美分一罐的金枪鱼罐头填饱自己的肚子。我去过一家那种食物银行，但是它们根本不值得去，我都不知道玻璃瓶装的牛奶竟然还没被淘汰。布朗克斯区的公交司机们人还不错，会让我免费搭乘，所以这挺好的，我还能四处走走。但是一旦出了任何事情，我便无法承担了。一位女士目前允许我以便宜的房租住在她那里，而她和她女儿一起住，所以我还是有住房的，但是因为有租金控制，所以我根本都不应该住在那边的。我每次回家都像是被四层劫难笼罩着。首先，我很惧怕自己的钥匙会打不开门。其次，我很惧怕信箱里会寄来一封信。然后，我也怕电梯不运行——但是这只是因为我懒到死。最后，当我终于到达家门口的时候，我害怕门下会有一封信。全是压力啊。我从来都没有安全感。每次有人敲门，我都觉得自己完了。”“It’s like I’m on eggshells all the time. Nothing but stress. I get $696 a month from social security. I could get more if I pretend to be bipolar like some people I know, but they make you take medicine to get your disability benefits. I'm not going to sit around like a zombie to get extra money. When I pay my bills, I have $30 left over. I can feed myself with 59-cent cans of tuna. I tried one of those food pantries but they aren’t even worth the time. I didn’t even know that pints of milk still existed. The bus drivers in the Bronx are cool so they let me ride for free. So that’s good. I can get around. But I can’t afford for anything to go wrong. Some lady is letting me stay in her place for cheap while she lives with her daughter, so I have a place to live. But it’s rent controlled so I’m not even supposed to be there. Every time I go home it’s like four layers of doom. First I’m terrified that my key won’t work. Then I’m terrified that there’s a letter in my mailbox. Then I’m afraid that the elevator won’t work—but that’s just cause I’m a lazy fuck. And then when I finally get to my apartment, I’m afraid there’s a letter under the door. Nothing but stress. I never feel safe. Every time there’s a knock on the door, I think it’s the end.”http://t.cn/RGcMlOT
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Dhx9sjfKy&u=005trlAagw1f0wtgewbxwj31kw11xwlr )

>  2016 年 1 月 26 日“我成长于一个蓝领家庭。我爸爸以前是一个印刷工——工会的一分子，所以他没有那个经济条件供我读大学和法学院。我不得不自己想办法。平日里我会给学生会的兄弟会成员们翻烤汉堡。暑假里我则靠在海军后备队度过而缴清了学费。我正在试着确保自己的孩子们不必再去经历这些事。我想要他们有能力去欧洲自由行，或者去中美洲做志愿者。那些有意义的活动。如果我儿子将来想要成为一个诗人或者一个印第安酋长，我也不会觉得有什么不好。我每周工作 60 到 70 小时，就是想确保他们能够做任何他们自己想做的事。为此我不得不错过很多东西，他的足球比赛我也只能听二手的消息。这也就是为什么周末的暴风雪如此之棒——孩子们不用上课、我也不用上班。我们没做什么事情，就是坐在一起、读读报纸、看看电视，就是有很多……说话的机会。”“I grew up in a blue collar family. My dad was a printer—a union guy. So he didn’t have the financial resources to pay for my college or law school. I had to make my own way. I flipped burgers during the week for frat guys at the Student Union. I covered my tuition by spending my summers in the Marine reserves. I’m trying to make sure my kids don’t have to do all that stuff. I want them to be able to backpack through Europe, or volunteer in Central America. Meaningful stuff. If my son wants to be a poet or an Indian chief, that’s fine with me. I work 60 or 70 hours a week to make sure they can do whatever they want. I miss a lot of stuff, though. I have to hear about the soccer games second hand. That’s why the snowstorm this weekend was so great. No school commitments. No work commitments. We didn't do much at all. Just sat around and read the newspaper or watched TV. There was just a lot of—talk.”http://t.cn/RGbTSoM

>  2016 年 1 月 26 日“我一边也在做职业摔角。它就是我周末的兴奋剂。我的摔角手名是‘人渣丹’。我没有特别魁梧，所以我是最阴险的摔角手之一。我的职责就是要让人们恨我。我会做各种不要脸的行为：抠眼珠、抓脸等等的。有一次我甚至把舔湿的手指伸进另一个家伙的耳朵里。我会冲进人群并撕烂人们带来的加油看板。我会告诉一个大学生说他娘本该用吞的。如果是在家庭之夜，我就会告诉一个小女孩说世上根本没有圣诞老人。总有人要做坏人的角色的，因为如果没有坏人也就不会有好人。没有‘人渣丹’就不会有 Chris Steeler。”“I do pro wrestling on the side. >  2016 年 1 月 23 日“我是在教会长大的。我七岁的时候接受了耶稣基督。在我十六岁参加一个宣教营的礼拜的时候，我决心贡献自己的一生来信奉主耶稣。我最大的成就是自己每一次地帮助年轻人们找到他们自己和耶稣基督的关系。而我最大的人生目标就是让每个人都知道主耶稣。我现在在纽约正尝试着播种教堂。这里和任何其他的宣教禾场都不同，这里的人们来自全世界各地，所以你传递出来的信息能够传播到世界的任何角落。我知道我所有的回答都特别有教会感，但是请随意分享，我不会去读评论的。”“I grew up in the church. >  2016 年 1 月 23 日“我想抚养出好人。我不想她们长大后成为为了成功而不择手段的人。所以我一有机会就会试着教导她们设身处地体谅别人。我总是叫我的大女儿描述她自己认为对方的感受如何。然后，我们还会试着想些让别人心情好起来的办法。我想让她们学会这点——诚然，能得到自己想要的东西的感觉很好，但是能帮助别人得到他们想要的东西的感觉同样很好。”“I want to raise good people. I don’t want them to grow into people who will do anything they can to get ahead. So every chance I get, I’m trying to teach them to put themselves in other peoples’ shoes. I always ask my oldest daughter to describe how she thinks another person feels. Then we try to imagine ways to make them feel better. I want them to learn that, yes, it feels good to get what you want. But it can feel just as good to help someone else get what they want.”

>  2016 年 1 月 22 日“在我的高中，第一个得到全新的乔丹球鞋的人就是皇帝，而负担不起人就会成为鲨鱼的诱饵。我和我妈妈没什么钱，所以我经常被欺负。有时情况特别糟糕的时候，我会惊恐发作。有一天，所有人都在历史课上对我特别地好，每个人都表现得像我的朋友一样，但是下课铃一响，他们就同一时间都开始朝着我扔肥皂。那段时间我住的是流浪者收容所，相比于学校我更喜欢呆在收容所。学校的每一件事情都是一场竞争，但是收容所的每个人都会互相帮助。人们会分享衣物、为别人做饭、照看彼此的孩子。我们都在人生的谷底，所以没有人觉得自己会比别人要优越。”“At my high school, the first kid to get a pair of new Jordan's was the king, and the kid who couldn’t afford them was bait for the sharks. My mom and I didn’t have much money so I got teased a lot. Sometimes it got so bad that I’d have panic attacks. One day all the kids were being especially nice to me in history class. Everyone was acting like my friend, but as soon as the bell rang, they all threw soap at me at the same time. I lived in a homeless shelter at the time. I liked being at the shelter much more than being at school. Everything at school was a competition. But everyone at the shelter helped each other out. People would share clothes, cook for each other, and babysit for each other. We were all at rock bottom, so nobody thought they were better than each other.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DgzBcgafV&u=005trlAagw1f0pijjf0mqj31kw11xn0h )

>  2016 年 1 月 21 日“我们最初是在一节武打课上遇见的，但是都没敢和对方说话。然而之后我们又碰巧一同拼车去了文艺复兴博览会。她是个牧羊女，而我则是威尔·斯卡列特——小约翰不在的时候罗宾汉的二把手。”“We first saw each other in a stage combat class, but were too afraid to speak to each other. But then we happened to ride in the same carpool to the Renaissance Fair. She was a shepherdess. I was Will Scarlett—who is Robin Hood’s number two, when Little John is not around.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DgrDRleHI&u=005trlAagw1f0ojewmnr7j311x1kwqan )

>  2016 年 1 月 21 日“我每天都在地铁上击大约三个小时的鼓。地下这儿简直就像是黑客帝国里的矩阵，满满的负能量，每个人都急急忙忙、紧张兮兮的，而且互相看都不看一眼。所以我在做的就是试着传播一些正能量，不让人们变成彻头彻尾的僵尸。昨天我在唱鲍勃·马利的歌的时候，一个男人大喊着说要我停止演奏。我想他是受到了我发出的光芒的影响。他离太阳太近了点。”“I play the drums on the subway for about three hours per day. It’s like the matrix down here. A lot of bad energy. Everyone is rushing and tense and people don’t like to look at each other. So I’m trying to spread some positivity and keep people out of the zombie zone. Yesterday I was singing some Bob Marley and a man screamed at me to stop playing. I think he was bothered by my light. He got too close to the sun.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Dgre7nzCT&u=005trlAagw1f0ohkqizt2j31kw11xn2x )

>  2016 年 1 月 20 日“我正在做卫生经济学方面的博士后学术研究。我的研究观察的是两个变量：开销和寿命。研究目标是判定如何才能最好地利用医疗补助款项来尽量延长受助者的寿命。学习医疗卫生非常重要，因为它是我们最宝贵的方针。周一是马丁·路德·金纪念日，而他曾说过‘在美国没有比我们医疗资源的分配更不公平的事了’。研究员们能根据离你家最近的地铁站判定你的预期寿命，不是因为基因、不是因为美国的粮食储备就要耗尽了，而是因为我们就是如此划分我们的资源的。而我认为这定义了我们整个社会的属性。”“I’m doing post doctorate research in health economics. My research looks at two variables: dollars spent and numbers of years lived. The goal is to determine how best to utilize Medicaid dollars to maximize the lifespan of recipients. It’s important to study healthcare because it’s the most precious resource we have. Monday was Martin Luther King Day, and he said that there was no greater injustice in America than our distribution of healthcare. Researchers can determine your life expectancy based on the closest subway stop to your house. That’s not due to genetics. That’s not because the breadbasket of America is running out. That’s because of how we choose to divide our resources. And I think it defines our character as a society.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DghhboANg&u=005trlAagw1f0n9kxrzgnj31kw11xaer )

>  2016 年 1 月 20 日“我只是在试图生存下去。我没有任何银行存款。不论是什么最低工资的活儿，能干的我都干，主要都是快餐业。在求职帮助项目里，他们告诉我们千万不要和面试官说：‘我需要一份工作。’取而代之，我们应该说：‘我喜欢做客服。’这句话对我倒是适用的。我做客服的时候感觉确实非常棒。它能帮助我不去纠结自己生活中其他的事情。”“I’m just trying to survive. I don’t have any money in the bank. I pick up whatever minimum wage jobs that I can, mainly fast food. At the job program, they tell us that we should never tell an interviewer: ‘I need a job.’ Instead we’re supposed to say: ‘I like customer service.’ That’s true for me though. I do feel good when I'm providing customer service. It helps me not worry about all the other stuff in my life.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DggnWCpte&u=005trlAagw1f0n5px78idj31kw11xaet )

>  2016 年 1 月 19 日“我正在试图找到一样能够激励自己每天早晨起床的事情。篮球能让我每天都到公园来努力练习，所以现在我只需要找到一样让自己对于其他一切事物都能努力的事情。我想把自己的成绩提高到 4.0。好吧，既然我已经在和你说话了，我想我的主要意志来源将会是我妈妈。她的梦想是拥有一幢我们每个人都能住不同楼层的房子。对于她这个想法我有所保留，但是我确实很想送给她一幢房子。”“I’m trying to find the thing that motivates me to get me out of bed every morning. Basketball makes me come to the park every day and work hard. Now I just need to find the thing that makes me work hard on everything else. I want to get my grades up to a 4.0. Now that I’m talking to you, I think my main motivation is going to be my mom. Her dream is to have a house where we all live on different floors. I'm not sure about that idea. But I do want to get her a house.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DgfNqxZ8d&u=005trlAagw1f0n33c0vhcj31kw11x0ye )

>  2016 年 1 月 18 日(2/2) “自从我丈夫进了神学院起，我便开始更多地研究基督教。我并没有觉得自己受到了基督教的冒犯。当你从字面解释退后一步再去看，你会意识到圣经旨在生存。看看所有那些疯狂的饮食限制。同性恋因为不能导致繁衍生息而被禁止。同样的原因，如果你在妻子月经期间和她发生性行为，你必须去庙里供奉一只仓鼠。书写圣经的人是在用彼时他们所了解的唯一的语言在说话——生存。当我退后了这一步，我看到了试图用符号和故事来理解生命源头的这样一本书。而那个源头被描述成了彻底的博爱。我觉得这真的很美。”(2/2) “I started studying Christianity more ever since my husband joined the seminary. I’m not offended by it. When you step back from the literal interpretation, you realize that so much of the Bible is aimed at survival. Look at all the crazy dietary restrictions. Homosexuality was forbidden because it didn’t lead to reproduction. For the same reason, if you had sex during your wife’s period, you had to sacrifice a hamster in the temple. The people who wrote the Bible were speaking with the only language that they knew at the time—survival. When I step back from that, I see a book that attempts to use symbols and stories to understand the source of life. And that source is depicted as completely loving. And I think that’s beautiful.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Dg6Wf3K14&u=005trlAagw1f0m008xsdjj31kw11xwhl )

-----------------------

>  2016 年 1 月 18 日(1/2) “我四岁的时候就觉得其他男孩子们很吸引我了，但是到了要青春期的时候，那种感觉简直就是牵引光束在把我拉向另一个人。我并不认识任何其他的同志，那个年代也没有互联网，所以对于我住的街坊、去的教堂、我的家人以及朋友们以外的事情，我一无所知。于是我以为自己是个变态。十三岁时我想过要自杀，我算好了要服的药片、准备好了一切。然而我在图书馆里找到了一本心理学教科书，书里说所有的青春期男孩们都会经历一个‘性探索’的阶段，所以我就想：‘这只是一个阶段。一个阶段我还是能应付得了的。’我以为只要自己邂逅了一位异性，所有的问题都会迎刃而解。当然，这根本就是个天大的谎言，但是至少它让我平安度过了自己十几岁的时光。而当我意识到这根本不是一个阶段的时候，我早已发展出了好多其他的自我认同。我已经变得很擅长游泳、跑步和拉大提琴。我的成绩也很好。我甚至还抽大麻。所以在我终于接受自己是同性恋的时候，我树立自我认同所基于的，已经是远远不止于自己的性取向了。”(1/2) “I felt attracted to other boys when I was four years old, but by the time I hit puberty, it felt like a tractor beam was pulling me toward another person. I didn’t know any other gay people. There was no Internet back then. I had no information about life beyond my neighborhood, church, family, and friends. So I thought I was sick. I considered suicide when I was thirteen. I had the pills measured out and everything. But I picked up a psychology textbook from the library, and it said that all teenage boys go through a phase of sexual exploration. So I thought: ‘It’s just a phase. I can handle a phase.’ I thought as soon as I had a heterosexual encounter, it would all go away. It was a lie, of course. But it got me through my teenage years. And by the time I realized it wasn’t a phase, I’d developed so many other parts of my identity. I’d become good at swimming, running, and playing the cello. I was making good grades. I was even smoking pot. So by the time I finally accepted being gay, my identity was based upon a lot more than my sexuality.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=Dg6oqu4n6&u=005trlAagw1f0lxlgi08nj31kw11xq84 )

>  2016 年 1 月 17 日“我们开始时只是约炮，但是之后却真的谈起了恋爱，而那真的太怪了，所以我们就停止交往了一段时间。之后我们又意识到其实这也没什么，所以我们又开始重新交往，直到现在都挺不错的。我希望这听起来没有很糟糕。听起来好像挺糟糕的。我的意思是，我说的都是实话，只是我表述的方式错了。这实在是太怪了，我看起来像个烂人。啊，你有问题还是问他吧。”“We started out just hooking up but then it got serious and that was weird so we stopped dating for awhile, but then we realized it’s OK so we started dating again and now it’s great. I hope that doesn’t sound bad. That sounded bad. I mean, it was the correct information but I presented it in the wrong way. This is weird. I look like a dick. Ask him a question now.”
![]( https://weibo.cn/mblog/oripic?id=DfZ9j8ECH&u=005trlAagw1f0l1mkgcdsj311x1kw45b )

>  2016 年 1 月 16 日“我还只是个初级实习医生，所以只动最简单的手术，但是有一次我给一个男人移除胆囊只留下了很小的一个疤痕，以至于他送给我了一盒巧克力。”“I’m still a junior resident so I only do basic surgeries. But once I left such a small scar after removing a man’s gallbladder that he sent me a box of chocolates.”
